1-6B-1: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Deposits And Disbursements; Records And Accounts: The city treasurer
shall receive all monies of the city paid to the treasurer in accordance with
law or ordinance, and shall deposit such monies in depositories designated by
the city council. Such monies shall be disbursed only in accordance with law.
The treasurer shall keep proper books of account and other financial records,
properly recording all financial transactions.
   B.   Other Powers And Duties: The city treasurer shall have such other
powers and duties as may be prescribed by law or ordinance. (1986 Code § 1-8)
1-6B-2: BOND REQUIRED 1 :
The city treasurer, before entering upon the duties of the office, shall
execute and file with the city clerk a good and sufficient bond in the sum of
fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00), executed by some reliable fidelity and
surety company lawfully transacting business in the state of Oklahoma, said
bond and surety to be approved by the city council, and the bond being
conditioned for the faithful performance of duties of the city treasurer as
provided by ordinances of the city, and enjoined by law; provided, that the
city shall pay out of its general revenue the premium for such bond. (1986 Code
§ 1-9)
 
Notes
1 2. See also subsection
  1-6-4A of this title.
1-6B-3: FINANCE OFFICER:
   A.   Appointment: A finance officer shall be appointed by the mayor subject
to confirmation by the city council.
   B.   Duties: The finance officer shall invest the funds of the city, assist
the mayor and city administrator with the preparation of the city's annual
budget, monitor budget revenues and expenses, and, when required, advise the
city council on other financial activities.
   C.   Salary: The finance officer shall be paid a salary as determined by
ordinance by the city council. The finance officer shall be paid biweekly in
the same manner as all other city employees and shall be subject to salary
increases and decreases received by all other city employees. If the city
treasurer of the city of Vinita is appointed to perform the additional
administrative duties of the finance officer, the salary for performing said
additional duties shall not be subject to constitutional restrictions. (Ord.
3358, 5-15-2007)
ARTICLE C. CITY ATTORNEY
SECTION:
1-6C-1: Appointment; Term; Qualifications
1-6C-2: Powers And Duties
1-6C-3: Salary
1-6C-1: APPOINTMENT; TERM; QUALIFICATIONS:
The city attorney shall be appointed by the mayor and the appointment confirmed
by the city council, and shall hold office at the pleasure of the mayor and
council. He shall have such qualifications, powers, and duties as are
prescribed by law for city attorneys in cities of the first class. (1986 Code §
1-38)
1-6C-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the city attorney to advise the mayor and city council
and each member thereof, and all city officials, upon all law questions, and he
shall give opinions in writing when requested, and shall represent the city as
counsel in all litigation, in all courts, for or against the city, and shall
perform such other legal service in behalf of the city, its officers or
employees, as may be required. (1986 Code § 1-38)
1-6C-3: SALARY:
Salary of the city attorney shall be established by the mayor and city council,
and the salary shall compensate for all routine duties performed for the city;
provided, that whenever the mayor and council deem it necessary, they may
employ the city attorney, or any other attorney or law firm, for any particular
matter, at a fee to be agreed upon between them. (1986 Code § 1-39)
ARTICLE D. STREET COMMISSIONER
SECTION:
1-6D-1: Appointment
1-6D-2: Powers And Duties
1-6D-1: APPOINTMENT:
There shall be a street commissioner. The mayor, with approval of the city
council, may appoint a street superintendent and such other street employees as
they deem necessary. (1986 Code § 1-40)
1-6D-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
The street commissioner, street superintendent and other employees appointed as
provided in section
1-6D-1 of this article shall maintain and improve the streets and alleys of the
city; and shall place, maintain, and remove street signs and traffic signs and
devices as directed. The street commissioner shall have such powers, duties,
and functions as may be prescribed by law or by ordinance. (1986 Code § 1-41)
ARTICLE E. CODES ENFORCEMENT OFFICER
SECTION:
1-6E-1: Position Created; Appointment
1-6E-2: Powers, Duties And Responsibilities
1-6E-3: Enforcement Actions; Appeals
1-6E-1: POSITION CREATED; APPOINTMENT:
There is hereby created the position of the codes enforcement officer who shall
have such duties, powers and responsibilities as may be herein set forth or
hereinafter prescribed. The codes enforcement officer shall be appointed by the
mayor, with the advice and consent of the city council (1986 Code § 1-91; amd.
2005 Code)
1-6E-2: POWERS, DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   Building And Zoning Regulations: The codes enforcement officer shall
have all the powers, duties and responsibilities of the plumbing inspector,
mechanical inspector, electrical inspector and the zoning enforcement officer,
including the authority to issue citations for the violation of the building,
plumbing, mechanical, electrical or zoning codes or ordinances.
   B.   Other Duties: The codes enforcement officer shall have such other
duties, responsibilities and powers, including the enforcement of other
ordinances of the city as the city council may from time to time provide by
ordinance or resolution. (1986 Code § 1-92)
1-6E-3: ENFORCEMENT ACTIONS; APPEALS:
The codes enforcement officer shall take such action as may be reasonable to
enforcement of title 4, chapter 3 of this code relating to nuisances,
including, but not limited to, the enforcement of title 4, chapter 4 of this
code relating to the abatement of weeds and trash and dilapidated buildings.
(1986 Code § 1-93)
ARTICLE F. LOCAL ENERGY OFFICER; COMMITTEE
SECTION:
1-6F-1: Officer Designated; Appointment
1-6F-2: Committee Created; Membership
1-6F-3: Terms And Vacancies
1-6F-4: Meetings
1-6F-5: Compensation
1-6F-6: Officers
1-6F-7: Duties And Powers
1-6F-1: OFFICER DESIGNATED; APPOINTMENT:
   A.   Designation: There is hereby designated an employee within the existing
city staff, which shall be known as the local energy officer (LEO). This person
shall be the city engineer, building official, or someone with similar
technical training. (Ord. 2837, 11-4-1991; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Appointment: The local energy officer shall be appointed by the mayor
upon approval by a majority vote of the city council. (Ord. 2837, 11-4-1991)
1-6F-2: COMMITTEE CREATED; MEMBERSHIP:
   A.   Creation: There is hereby created a committee which shall be known as
the energy management committee.
   B.   Membership; Appointment: The energy management committee shall consist
of five (5) members to be appointed by a majority vote of the city council.
(Ord. 2837, 11-4-1991)
1-6F-3: TERMS AND VACANCIES:
   A.   Committee; Terms: The term of office of a member of the energy
management committee shall be two (2) years and shall end on the first Monday
of November. Of the original appointive members, one shall serve for one year,
two (2) shall serve for three (3) years, and two (2) shall serve for two (2)
years. The individual term of office of an original appointive member shall be
determined by the mayor in such manner as he shall select.
   B.   Filling Vacancies On Committee:
      1.   Any vacancy which occurs shall be filled for the unexpired term in
the same manner as the original appointment.
      2.   A member who shall miss three (3) consecutive regularly scheduled
meetings of the committee shall cease to be a member. The vacancy created shall
be filled by an appointment of a new member to serve the remainder of the
unexpired term by the mayor upon approval by a majority vote of the city
council.
   C.   Term Of LEO: The term of office for the LEO shall be established by the
mayor and approved by the majority vote of the city council. (Ord. 2837, 11-4-
1991)
1-6F-4: MEETINGS:
   A.   Time And Place: The energy management committee and LEO shall hold
regular monthly meetings. The members of the committee shall determine the time
and place of such meetings.
   B.   Special Meetings: The local energy officer, the mayor or any three (3)
members of the energy management committee may call a special meeting.
   C.   Open Meetings: Except for instances wherein executive sessions are
authorized by state law, all meetings shall be open to the public with proper
notice given as required by the Oklahoma open meeting act 1 . (Ord. 2837, 11-4-
1991)
 
Notes
1 1. 25 OS § 301 et seq.
1-6F-5: COMPENSATION:
   A.   Committee Members: The members of the energy management committee shall
serve without compensation but shall be reimbursed for such reasonable expense
incurred in the performance of their duties as allowed by the city council.
   B.   LEO: The LEO shall be compensated through his/her salary. (Ord. 2837,
11-4-1991)
1-6F-6: OFFICERS:
   A.   Officers; Term: The energy management committee shall elect from its
membership a vice chairman and a secretary to serve for terms of one year.
   B.   Chairman: The LEO shall serve as the chairman of the committee.
   C.   Secretary: The secretary shall keep minutes of all meetings of the
board and certify to the chairman that proper notice has been given to the city
clerk and the public of all meetings. (Ord. 2837, 11-4-1991)
1-6F-7: DUTIES AND POWERS:
   A.   Advisory Committee: The energy management committee shall act as an
advisory committee to the city council and mayor.
   B.   Copies Of Bills, Contracts: Copies of city utility bills, contracts,
franchise agreements, and records pertaining to expenditures shall be made
available to the committee upon request.
   C.   Develop Energy Management Program: The committee shall develop an
ongoing energy management program (EMP) to be implemented citywide as a method
of:
      1.   Reducing energy costs by identifying energy management opportunities
for which effective solutions are commercially available.
      2.   Developing and maintaining a regularly scheduled maintenance program
of all facilities.
      3.   Identifying and implementing "low cost/no cost measures" for proper
energy management.
      4.   Developing strategies for future energy management measures.
      5.   Conducting technology seminars with manufacturers to keep abreast of
current technology and future trends.
   D.   Monitoring Program: The committee shall monitor the EMP on an ongoing
basis to ensure the program is obtaining the desired objectives, forecast
savings, and policies of the program's current direction.
   E.   Quarterly Reports:
      1.   The committee shall prepare quarterly reports involving the status,
current objectives, goals, and accomplishments of the energy management
program.
      2.   The committee chairman shall present the quarterly reports to the
city council with recommendations for consideration of implementation.
   F.   Public Meetings: The committee shall hold two (2) public meetings
annually to obtain citizen input, and to inform the citizens of the current
status, objectives, goals, and accomplishments of the EMP.
   G.   Copies Of Minutes To Clerk: The committee secretary shall provide
copies of the minutes to the office of the city clerk within ten (10) days from
the date of their approval. (Ord. 2837, 11-4-1991)
ARTICLE G. CITY ADMINISTRATOR
SECTION:
1-6G-1: Position Created
1-6G-2: Powers, Duties And Responsibilities
1-6G-1: POSITION CREATED:
There is hereby created the position and office of city administrator who shall
be a nonelected officer of the city of Vinita and who shall have such duties,
powers and responsibilities as may be herein set forth or hereinafter
prescribed. (Ord. 3275, 6-7-2005)
1-6G-2: POWERS, DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   Attend staff meetings with all department heads to inform them of such
needed information as to coordination of projects being conducted or planned in
other departments within the city.
   B.   Gather information to make monthly reports to be given to the mayor and
council members on a monthly basis.
   C.   Gather information and related facts so the mayor and council members
can make evaluations of departments to establish needs and priorities that will
be placed in a format with other compiled data so that if outside funding, such
as state or federal monies are available, they may be applied for in the proper
manner.
   D.   Compile information so the mayor and council members can create and
maintain an affirmative action program for the city of Vinita.
   E.   Work with any group of citizens or committees designated by the mayor
and council members to keep both parties informed and to compile such
information as both would desire.
   F.   Assist the mayor, council members, city clerk and city attorney in
filing applications for federal or state assistance; after funding is
successful, work with those agencies and contractors until project is completed
and finalized.
   G.   Attend negotiations on behalf of the city administration with unions of
city employees.
   H.   Work with city department heads, city clerk, mayor and council members
in formulating, preparing and finalizing a budget for the city.
   I.   Coordinate with each department head in the screening of employees to
be hired and coordinate with the city attorney to make certain that federal
regulations dealing with hiring practices are complied with.
   J.   Work with departments of other governmental agencies and coordinate
with the city clerk, city attorney and city department heads to keep them
informed of new regulations, such as wage and hour laws and safety laws that
must be adhered to by cities.
   K.   Cooperate with outside engineering firms so that needed data may be
compiled on any project being conducted for the city. (Ord. 3275, 6-7-2005)
   L.   Approve necessary expenditures of the city for amounts up to five
thousand dollars ($5,000.00) per purchase. (Ord. 3396, 6-3-2008)
   M.   Exercise such duties as the mayor of the city of Vinita shall
specifically instruct and request.
   N.   Suspend for cause any nonunion employees of the city of Vinita.
   O.   Any such other duties, responsibilities and powers, including
enforcement of other ordinances of the city of Vinita, as the Vinita city
council may from time to time provide by ordinance or resolution. (Ord. 3275,
6-7-2005)
CHAPTER 7
CITY DEPARTMENTS
SECTION:
1-7-1: Water And Sewer Department
1-7-2: City-County Cooperative Health Department
1-7-3: Library Department
1-7-4: Park And Cemetery Department
1-7-5: City Hall Building And Maintenance Department
1-7-1: WATER AND SEWER DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Superintendent; Employees: The water and sewer department of the city
shall consist of a superintendent of the water and sewer department who shall
be the business agent of the city in charge of such department. In addition to
the superintendent, there may be employed clerical help and such other
employees as may be authorized by the mayor and city council from time to time.
   B.   Duties: The water and sewer department, its officers, agents and
employees shall have supervision of the water utility of the city and of the
sewage disposal system of the city and shall be charged with the maintenance
and operation thereof, and shall perform such other duties as are now or may
hereafter be prescribed by the mayor and city council. (1986 Code § 1-42)
1-7-2: CITY-COUNTY COOPERATIVE HEALTH DEPARTMENT:
   A.   General Enforcement By State: Under the laws of the state of Oklahoma,
the Oklahoma state department of health has agreed to enforce ordinances of
cities and towns relating to the public health, welfare and safety.
   B.   County Enforcement For City: The Craig County health department
operating under the Oklahoma state health department has agreed to enforce the
ordinances of the city of Vinita, Oklahoma, relating to the public health,
welfare and safety.
   C.   City Delegation Of Authority To County:
      1.   It has been determined that for the best interest of the citizens of
the city of Vinita, Oklahoma, that the city of Vinita authorize and delegate
the Craig County health department to assist and enforce the ordinances of the
said city relating to the public health, welfare and safety.
      2.   The Craig County health department is hereby authorized and
delegated the authority to enforce all the ordinances of the city of Vinita,
Oklahoma, relating to the public health, welfare and safety. (1986 Code § 1-43)
1-7-3: LIBRARY DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Librarian; Employees: The city library department shall consist of the
city librarian and such additional employees as may be employed from time to
time when authorized by resolution or motion of the mayor and city council.
   B.   Duties: The library department, its officers and employees, shall
perform such duties as are now prescribed by state law, and in addition
thereto, such duties as may now or hereafter be imposed by the mayor and city
council. (1986 Code § 1-44)
1-7-4: PARK AND CEMETERY DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Departments Combined; Duties: The park and cemetery departments shall
have the same superintendent who shall work under the direction of the mayor
and city council and perform such duties as are now or may be hereafter
prescribed by ordinance.
   B.   Employees: The mayor and council may employ as many employees as they
deem appropriate to perform the maintenance and upkeep of the city parks and
cemetery.
   C.   Playground Supervisors: Playground supervisors may be temporarily
employed during the summer months, at the discretion of and upon motion by the
city council. (1986 Code §§ 1-45, 1-46; amd. 2005 Code)
1-7-5: CITY HALL BUILDING AND MAINTENANCE DEPARTMENT:
The city hall building and maintenance department shall consist of a custodian
whose duties shall be to see to the maintenance and cleanliness of the city
hall building, and such other duties as may be directed from time to time by
the mayor and city council. Additional employees may be hired from time to time
as provided by resolution of the council. (1986 Code § 1-47)
ARTICLE A. POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
1-7A-1: Appointment; Terms Of Office; General Duties
1-7A-2: Review By Police Personnel Board; Probation
1-7A-3: Qualifications Of Candidates
1-7A-4: Reserve Police Officers
1-7A-5: Tenure Of Office
1-7A-6: Suspension Or Removal For Cause; Appeal
1-7A-7: Political Campaigns, Activities Restricted
1-7A-8: Unclaimed Property
1-7A-1: APPOINTMENT; TERMS OF OFFICE; GENERAL DUTIES:
   A.   Appointment: There shall be a chief of police 1 . The mayor, with
approval of the city council, shall appoint an assistant chief of police and
such other police officers as the mayor and council deem necessary, as provided
by 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 9-105. (1986 Code § 1-11)
   B.   Term Of Office: The assistant chief of police and police officers shall
hold their offices until their respective successors have been appointed and
qualify, but may be removed at any time as provided by 11 Oklahoma Statutes
section 9-118. (1986 Code § 1-11; amd. 2005 Code)
   C.   Powers And Duties: The chief of police, assistant chief of police, and
other police officers shall constitute the police department and shall have the
powers and duties prescribed by 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 34-101, and other
provisions of law or by ordinance. (1986 Code § 1-12)
   D.   Police Officers Defined: Police officers are those persons in the
employment of the city who have been commissioned as police officers and who
are directly engaged in the enforcement of the ordinances of the city. (1986
Code § 1-13)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsections
  1-4-1A2 of this title for election, and 1-6-3A and B for compensation.
1-7A-2: REVIEW BY POLICE PERSONNEL BOARD; PROBATION:
   A.   Board Recommendation: Names of potential appointees of the police
department of the city shall, upon recommendations of the chief of police, be
submitted to the police personnel board for approval and recommendation and
then be appointed by the mayor and confirmed by the city council by a majority
vote thereof, including the vote of the mayor. (1986 Code § 1-14; amd. 2005
Code)
   B.   Probationary Period: Members so appointed shall serve on probation for
a period of one year from the time of such appointment, during which time the
chief of police, upon the confirmation of the police personnel board, may
terminate the appointment of such probationary member if, upon observation,
investigation or consideration of performance of duty, he shall be deemed
unsatisfactory. (1986 Code § 1-14)
1-7A-3: QUALIFICATIONS OF CANDIDATES:
Candidates for appointment to the position of police officer for the city shall
be qualified as follows:
   A.   Criminal Background: Such candidate shall not have been guilty of any
felony or crime involving moral turpitude (unless granted a full pardon).
   B.   Evaluation And Certification: No person shall receive a permanent
appointment as a police officer in the city unless:
      1.   He has undergone evaluation similar to the Minnesota multiphasic
personality inventory or its equivalent (as determined by the council on law
enforcement education and training [CLEET]); and
      2.   He has been awarded a certificate, attesting to his satisfactory
completion of a basic police course of not less than three hundred (300) hours
of accredited instruction from said council (CLEET) or curriculum or course of
study approved by said council (CLEET). The "council (CLEET)" shall be defined
as the council on law enforcement, education and training. A reserve officer
shall have not less than one hundred twenty (120) hours of instruction.
   C.   Time Limit For Certification: Every person who is not a holder of such
certificate and is duly appointed as a member of the police force shall hold
such position on a temporary basis only, and shall, within one year from the
date of appointment, qualify as required by this section or forfeit such
position. In computing the one year, all service shall be cumulative from date
of first appointment as a police officer of the City. The City Council may
extend the time requirement for good cause. (1986 Code § 1-15; amd. 2005 Code)
1-7A-4: RESERVE POLICE OFFICERS:
   A.   Appointment: In addition to regular full time police officers, reserve
police officers may also be appointed by the Chief of Police.
   B.   Powers And Duties: Reserve officers shall have the powers, duties and
functions as set forth in law or ordinance for regular full time police
officers.
   C.   Part Time Basis: A reserve officer shall serve on a part time basis and
shall perform his duties only while on authorized duty and for not more than
twenty five (25) hours per calendar week.
   D.   Requirements: Such reserve officer must meet the minimum requirements
of section
1-7A-3 of this article and 70 Oklahoma Statutes section 3311. (1986 Code § 1-
16)
1-7A-5: TENURE OF OFFICE:
The police officers of the City shall hold their respective offices and
positions regardless of change of City officials or City administration unless
removed or discharged for cause. No police officer employed by the City shall
be demoted except for cause.
   A.   Notice Of Cause; Hearing; Determination: All members of the Police
Department who are suspended or removed from office may request to be notified
of the specific cause therefor in writing within three (3) days after such
suspension or removal from office. Within ten (10) days from such suspension or
removal, the person affected may make a written request to the City Clerk for a
hearing before the Mayor and City Council, and the Mayor and City Council shall
hold a public hearing within ten (10) days of the filing of the request
therefor. If after hearing, the City Council shall find that cause has not been
shown for the suspension, removal from office or discharge, it shall order the
person restored to his former position without loss of pay.
   B.   Action To Suspend Or Remove:
      1.   If the City Council by a majority vote shall find that cause has
been shown, it may order the removal, suspension or discharge of such persons,
or may, in their discretion, discipline such persons by a suspension of a
period of not more than ninety (90) days and a fine of an amount not to exceed
five hundred dollars ($500.00), or both. The accused may represent himself or
appear by counsel. (1986 Code § 1-17; amd. 2005 Code)
      2.   The Chief of Police may, for misconduct, suspend any member of the
Police Department without pay for a period not to exceed ten (10) days for one
offense, and not to exceed twenty (20) days in any one calendar year, and shall
notify the City Council in writing of his action. (1986 Code § 1-17)
   C.   Nondiscrimination: No police officer shall be suspended or removed from
office because of his race, creed or color, gender, age, religious or political
beliefs, except when such persons advocate or belong to any organization which
advocates the overthrow of the government by force or violence. (1986 Code § 1-
17; amd. 2005 Code)
   D.   Right To Hearing Before Court: No action of the City Council shall be
construed to deny any police officer of his right to file a proper case for
hearing before any court of general jurisdiction. (1986 Code § 1-17)
1-7A-6: SUSPENSION OR REMOVAL FOR CAUSE; APPEAL:
Any member of the police force who is removed, suspended or separated from the
police force for cause as provided herein shall have the right of appeal to the
District Court of Craig County, Oklahoma, or as otherwise provided by law or
contract. (1986 Code § 1-18)
1-7A-7: POLITICAL CAMPAIGNS, ACTIVITIES RESTRICTED:
   A.   Participation In Campaign: No police officer of the City shall take
part in any political campaign, except to vote, while on duty or in uniform and
no police officer shall use his official position to further the interest of
any political candidate, faction, or party. (Ord. 3696, 2-5-2019)
1-7A-8: UNCLAIMED PROPERTY:
   A.   Complete Record Required: All personal property which comes into the
possession of any police officer, which has been found or stolen or taken off
the person or out of the possession of any prisoner or person suspected of, or
charged with, being a criminal, and which is not known to belong to some person
laying claim thereto, shall be, by the officer securing possession thereof,
delivered into the charge of the Chief of Police. The Chief shall, in a
permanent record book kept for that purpose, make a record sufficient to
identify the property, with the date and circumstances of the receipt thereof,
the name of the person from whom it was taken and the place where it was found;
and the record shall also disclose the subsequent disposal thereof, giving the
date of sale, name and address of the purchaser, and the amount for which it
was sold. (1986 Code § 17-1)
   B.   Disposition Of Property:
      1.   The Chief of Police is authorized to sell personal property other
than money or legal tender of the United States, which comes into his
possession if:
         a.   The owner of the personal property is unknown or has not claimed
the property; and
         b.   The property has been in the custody of the Chief of Police for
at least six (6) months; and
         c.   The property or any part thereof is no longer needed to be held
as evidence or for any other purpose in connection with any litigation.
      2.   The Chief of Police shall file an application in the District Court
of Craig County requesting the authority of such court to conduct a sale of
such personal property. The Chief of Police shall attach to its application a
list describing the property including any identifying numbers and marks, the
dates that property came into his possession, and the name of the owner and his
address, if known. The court shall set said application for hearing not less
than ten (10) days nor more than twenty (20) days after the filing of said
application.
      3.   At least ten (10) days prior to the date of hearing, notice of said
hearing shall be sent by certified mail to each owner at his address as listed
in said application. Said notice shall contain a brief description of the
property of said owner and the place and date of the hearing. Said notice shall
be posted at the assigned place for posting of Municipal notices and at two (2)
other public places in the City.
      4.   If no owner appears and establishes ownership of said property at
the hearing, the court shall enter an order authorizing the Chief of Police to
sell said personal property for cash to the highest bidder, after at least five
(5) days' notice of such sale has been published. The Chief of Police shall
make a record of said sale and the order of the court confirming said sale
shall vest title to said property in the purchaser. After payment of court
costs and other expenses, the remainder of money received from the sale of said
property shall be deposited in the City General Fund.
      5.   All monies or legal tender of the United States which has come into
the possession of the Chief of Police pursuant to the circumstances provided
for in subsection B1 of this section shall be transferred by the Chief of
Police to the City Clerk for deposit in the City General Fund. Prior to any
such transfer, the Chief of Police shall file an application in the District
Court requesting the court to enter an order authorizing him to transfer said
property for deposit in the City General Fund. The application shall describe
the money or legal tender, any serial numbers, the date the same came into his
possession, and the name of the owner and his address, if known. Upon filing
the application which may be joined with an application as described in
subsection B2 of this section, a hearing shall be set not less than ten (10)
days nor more than twenty (20) days from the date of filing of such
application. Notice of said hearing shall be given as provided for in
subsection B3 of this section. The notice shall state that upon failure of
anyone to appear to prove ownership to said money or legal tender, the court
shall order the same to be deposited in the City General Fund. The notice may
be combined with a notice to sell personal property as provided for in
subsection B2 of this section. If no one appears to claim and prove ownership
to said money or legal tender at the hearing, the court shall order the same to
be transferred to the City General Fund as provided in this subsection.
      6.   The provisions of this section shall not apply to any dangerous or
deadly weapons, narcotic or poisonous drugs, explosives, or any property of any
kind or character, which the possession of is prohibited by law. By order of
the court, any such property filed as an exhibit or held by the City shall be
destroyed or sold or disposed of, pursuant to the conditions prescribed in such
order. (1986 Code § 17-2)
   C.   Property Found By Private Person: Any personal property found by a
person other than a public official or employee, which is delivered to any
police officer for identification, if not claimed or identified within thirty
(30) days, shall, within ten (10) additional days thereafter, if requested by
the finder, be returned to him, and a record of such disposal made thereof. If
the finder does not request return of the property to him within such
additional ten (10) days, then the Chief of Police shall sell the property as
if it had been found by a public official or employee, or, on instruction by
the Mayor, deliver it to some department or office of the City government for
its use. The finder of a thing is entitled to compensation for all expenses
necessarily incurred by him for its preservation, and for any other service
necessarily performed by him about it, and to a reasonable reward for keeping
it. If the finder knows or suspects who the owner is, he must, with reasonable
diligence, give notice to him of the finding; and if he fails to do so, he is
liable in damages to the owner, and has no claim to any reward offered by him
for the recovery of the thing, or to any compensation for his trouble or
expenses. (1986 Code § 17-3)
ARTICLE B. FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
1-7B-1: Department Created
1-7B-2: Appointment And Removal
1-7B-3: Fire Chief And Assistant Fire Chief
1-7B-4: Compensation
1-7B-5: Company Officers
1-7B-6: New Members; Probation
1-7B-7: Rules And Regulations; Members
1-7B-8: Suspension Of Firefighters
1-7B-9: Inspection And Prevention Of Fires
1-7B-10: Fire Protection Outside City
1-7B-11: Protection And Repair Of Apparatus
1-7B-12: Refusing To Obey Orders At Fires
1-7B-13: Right Of Way On Streets
1-7B-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There shall be a fire department which shall consist of a chief, an assistant
chief, and such other personnel as the city council may authorize. (1986 Code §
1-20)
1-7B-2: APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL:
   A.   Appointment: The members of the fire department shall, on approval of
the chief of the fire department, be appointed in the manner provided by law
for the appointment of municipal employees.
   B.   Terms; Removal; Hearing: The chief, assistant chief, and firefighters
shall serve for indefinite terms, subject to removal for good and sufficient
cause by the mayor and city council, after a hearing held after ten (10) days'
notice. (1986 Code § 1-21)
1-7B-3: FIRE CHIEF AND ASSISTANT FIRE CHIEF:
   A.   Administration; Supervision:
      1.   The city shall have a full time fire chief whose primary duties
shall be the administration of the fire department in accordance with the
policies and procedures prescribed by the city council and mayor.
      2.   The fire department shall be under the direction and control of the
fire chief who shall not serve as fire chief and police chief.
   B.   Qualifications: The fire chief shall have had at least three (3) years'
actual experience as a paid firefighter.
   C.   Duties Of Chief: The fire chief:
      1.   Shall be at the head of the department, subject to the laws of the
state of Oklahoma, ordinances of the city, and the rules and regulations herein
adopted.
      2.   Shall be held responsible for the general condition and efficient
operation of the department, the training of members, and the performance of
all other duties imposed upon him.
      3.   May inspect or cause to be inspected by members of the department,
the fire hydrants, cisterns and other sources of water supply at least twice
each year.
      4.   Shall maintain a library or file of publications on fire prevention
and fire protection and shall make use of it to the best advantage of all
members.
      5.   Shall make every effort to attend all fires and direct the officers
and members in the performance of their duties.
      6.   Shall see that the citizens are kept informed on fire hazards in the
community and on the activities of the department.
      7.   Shall see that each fire is carefully investigated to determine its
cause, and, in the case of suspicion of incendiarism, shall notify proper
authorities and secure and preserve all possible evidence for future use in the
case. (1986 Code § 1-22)
      8.   Shall file the appropriate activity report forms with the office of
the state fire marshal in Oklahoma City on an annual basis. The report forms
designed by the state fire marshal shall include, but not be limited to, the
amount of property and vehicle fire loss, types of fires, inspections and
investigations. The report shall include notification of all fire related
civilian deaths and injuries in the respective jurisdiction, and of firefighter
deaths in the line of duty and of firefighter injuries in the line of duty
requiring the services of a hospital or physician or both. (1986 Code § 1-22;
amd. 2005 Code)
      9.   Shall keep a record of all fires occurring within the city in a
suitable book, to be provided for that purpose, showing the estimated value of
the loss or damage to property, the amount of insurance, the cause and origin
of fire, and the names of the firefighters attending, and the expenses incurred
to the department thereby. (1986 Code § 1-35)
      10.   Shall prepare and keep a complete inventory of all property
belonging to the fire department, and shall, at the expiration of his term,
turn over such inventory and all such property to his successor, together with
all books, records, reports, and data of such department. (1986 Code § 1-36)
   D.   Duties Of Assistant Chief: In the absence of the chief, the assistant
chief on duty shall command the department and shall have the full powers and
responsibilities of the chief. (1986 Code § 1-23)
1-7B-4: COMPENSATION:
The chief, assistant chief and each firefighter shall receive such compensation
as may be determined by the city council. (1986 Code § 1-37)
1-7B-5: COMPANY OFFICERS:
   A.   Basis For Selection: The company officers shall be selected upon their
ability to meet the following requirements:
      1.   Their knowledge of firefighting.
      2.   Their ability to lead firefighters.
      3.   Their knowledge of firefighting equipment. (1986 Code § 1-24)
   B.   Secretary-Treasurer: One member elected by the fire department shall be
secretary-treasurer. His duties shall consist of the following:
      1.   Calling the roll at the opening of each meeting.
      2.   Keeping the minutes of each meeting.
      3.   Collecting the monies due the department by the members. (1986 Code
§ 1-25)
1-7B-6: NEW MEMBERS; PROBATION:
   A.   Term Of Probation: All new members shall be on probation for one year
after their appointment.
   B.   Department Approval: New volunteer members, upon completion of their
probation period, must be approved by the majority of the fire department.
(1986 Code § 1-26)
1-7B-7: RULES AND REGULATIONS; MEMBERS:
The volunteer fire department shall be subject to the following rules and
regulations which shall be incorporated in the bylaws of the department:
   A.   All volunteer firefighters are required, when notified, to respond to
alarms of fire and other emergencies.
   B.   Firefighters are required to be present at all regular meetings, called
meetings and schools presented for the benefit of the firefighters.
   C.   There shall be at least one regular business meeting each month.
   D.   Any volunteer firefighter having two (2) unexcused absences in
succession or three (3) unexcused absences in a period of three (3) months will
be dropped from the fire department rolls.
   E.   Volunteer firefighters leaving the city for an extended period of time
will be required to notify the chief.
   F.   Any volunteer firefighter refusing to attend training classes provided
for him will be dropped.
   G.   Any volunteer member of the fire department shall be dropped from the
rolls for the following offenses:
      1.   Conduct unbecoming a firefighter.
      2.   Any act of insubordination.
      3.   Neglect of duty.
      4.   Any violation of rules and regulations governing the fire
department.
      5.   Conviction of a felony. (1986 Code § 1-27)
1-7B-8: SUSPENSION OF FIREFIGHTERS:
The chief shall have the power and authority to suspend any firefighter of the
department for drunkenness, neglect of duty, disobedience of orders, or for
other good cause, and he shall, immediately after such suspension, report the
same to the mayor in writing, stating the reasons for such suspension for the
action by the mayor and city council. (1986 Code § 1-28)
1-7B-9: INSPECTION AND PREVENTION OF FIRES:
   A.   Right Of Entry For Inspection: The chief shall adopt all prudent
measures for the prevention of fires, and whenever he has reasons to believe
that the safety of property demands it, he and his authorized representatives
shall have reasonable access in the daytime to any house, building or premises
in the city to examine fireplaces, flues or other property or apparatus likely
to cause fire; also places where ashes, gunpowder, straw, paper, shavings, hay,
or other combustible or inflammable materials may be deposited, and shall give
directions for the alteration or removal of the same, as he shall deem proper;
and such directions shall be obeyed and complied with by the person so directed
immediately at their expense. (1986 Code § 1-33)
   B.   Inspection Of Public Places: The chief shall have full power and
authority, and he is hereby enjoined, to enter all theaters, shows, show houses
or tents, and public halls and buildings in the city where scenery, drop
curtains, and stage fittings are used during any performance therein and to
require every possible precaution to be taken to prevent fire, and to guard the
public from panic therein. (1986 Code § 1-34)
1-7B-10: FIRE PROTECTION OUTSIDE CITY:
   A.   Right To Enter Into Contracts: The city is hereby authorized and
empowered to enter into contracts or agreements with individuals, firms,
private corporations or associations, or political subdivisions of the state of
Oklahoma for fire protection outside the corporate limits of the city, and to
contract to provide fire protection jointly with other organizations and
municipal subdivisions of the state. (1986 Code § 8-21)
   B.   Contract Rate; Monies To General Fund Budget:
      1.   Any contract entered into by the city with an individual owner,
firm, private corporation, or association, for outside aid, or mutual aid for
fire protection, shall provide for the payment by said owner, firm, private
corporation, or association, or political subdivision to the city for such fire
apparatus and personnel at a rate not less than four hundred fifty dollars
($450.00) per occurrence or run of the fire department. (Ord. 3459, 2-16-2010)
      2.   All monies received from said calls shall go into the general fund
to be used in the general fund budget in the general operation of the city.
(1986 Code § 8-22; amd. 2005 Code)
   C.   Authority To Answer Calls: The fire department of the city is hereby
authorized to answer outside fire calls from the owner of the property unless,
in the opinion of the fire chief, it is inexpedient to do so on account of
another fire in the city, broken apparatus, impassable or dangerous highways,
or other physical conditions. (1986 Code § 8-23)
   D.   Firefighters' Benefits: All firefighters of the fire department of the
city attending and serving at fires or doing fire prevention work outside the
corporate limits of the city, as herein provided, shall be considered as
serving in their regular line of duty as fully as if they were serving within
the corporate limits of the city, and said firefighters shall be entitled to
all the benefits of any firefighters' pension and relief fund in the same
manner as if the firefighting or fire prevention work was being done within the
corporate limits of the city. (1986 Code § 8-24)
   E.   Department Considered Agent Of State: The fire department of the city
answering any fire alarm, or call, or performing any fire prevention services
outside the corporate limits of the city shall be considered as an agent of the
state of Oklahoma, and acting solely and alone in a governmental capacity, and
the city shall not be liable in damages for any act of commission, omission, or
negligence while answering or returning from any fire, or reported fire, or
doing any fire prevention work under and by virtue of this section. (1986 Code
§ 8-25)
   F.   Right Of Way Of Equipment: All motorized equipment of the fire
department of the city shall have the right of way over all other commercial
and pleasure vehicles. (1986 Code § 8-26)
1-7B-11: PROTECTION AND REPAIR OF APPARATUS:
   A.   Protection: It shall be unlawful for any person, without authority, to
take, remove, or to in any manner disturb, molest, or interfere with any
hydrants, hose, ladder or any apparatus or tools to be used in connection with
the fire department. (1986 Code § 1-31; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Repair: The chief shall report to the city council any necessary
repairs, alterations or improvements needed by the fire department, with an
estimate of their probable cost and shall superintend the making of such
repairs, alterations and improvements, and, in case any apparatus shall become
disabled for immediate use, he shall repair the same and report his action to
the city council. (1986 Code § 1-32)
1-7B-12: REFUSING TO OBEY ORDERS AT FIRES:
It shall be the duty of every person at a fire to observe and obey the lawful
orders of any public officer or firefighter of the city, and to offer no
resistance to, or in anywise interfere with said officer and firefighter, or
any company of firefighters, in the performance of their duties at any fire
within the limits of the city. (1986 Code § 1-29)
1-7B-13: RIGHT OF WAY ON STREETS:
At every fire alarm, it shall be the duty of all persons driving, or in charge
of, any animal, wagon, carriage, automobile or other vehicle in any street,
alley or other way in the city upon which the fire apparatus belonging to the
fire department may go, to yield immediately the right of way so as not to
obstruct or delay the fire department, or any person in attendance at any fire.
The gong or siren attached to the fire apparatus shall be sounded and emergency
lights shall be turned on and operating from the time of leaving the fire
station until the arrival at the fire. (1986 Code § 1-30; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 8
CITY FINANCES
SECTION:
1-8-1: Deposit Of City Funds
1-8-2: Purchasing
1-8-3: Claims Against City
1-8-4: Penalty
1-8-1: DEPOSIT OF CITY FUNDS:
   A.   Deposit By Treasurer; Designation Of City Depositories: The city
treasurer shall deposit daily all the funds and monies of whatever kind that
shall come into his possession by virtue of his office as such city treasurer,
in his name as city treasurer, in one or more responsible banks located in the
city and designated by the city council as such depositories. Provided, that
there shall not be deposited in any one bank at any one time a greater amount
of such funds than the capital stock of such bank. Such bank or banks shall
receive all monies, drafts or checks, at par, and pay interest on the average
daily balance at such rate as may be agreed upon between such banks and the
city council and shall credit the same monthly to the account of the city
treasurer. (1986 Code § 7-22)
   B.   Deposit Records: The city treasurer shall, when making up his deposit
for the banks, make duplicate tickets for such deposit and file the same with
the city clerk, and it shall be the duty of the city clerk to charge the bank
designated as the depository of public monies with all monies deposited by the
city treasurer, and credit the city treasurer with such amount deposited. (1986
Code § 7-23)
   C.   Monthly Bank Statements: Such bank or banks shall, at the end of each
month, transmit to the city clerk a statement of the amounts received from the
city treasurer and the amounts paid out by it or them and for what purpose.
(1986 Code § 7-24)
   D.   Bonds Of Depositories: The city depository or depositories shall secure
the city for all deposits by giving a good and sufficient bond with some surety
company or companies to be approved by the city council. Said bond shall be for
double the sum of the probable maximum deposits of the city at any one time
with said depository or depositories and a new bond may be exacted by the city
council at any time when the existing bond shall be deemed insufficient, but
until such bond or bonds are given, the city treasurer shall be liable on his
bond for the loss of any money so deposited. (1986 Code § 7-25)
1-8-2: PURCHASING:
No purchase or contract shall be made unless in compliance with 62 Oklahoma
Statutes section 310.1 et seq. (1986 Code § 7-26)
1-8-3: CLAIMS AGAINST CITY:
No payroll or other claim shall be made unless in compliance with 62 Oklahoma
Statutes section 304.1 et seq., or the governmental tort claims, or such other
statute or provisions allowing a claim against the city. (1986 Code § 7-27)
1-8-4: PENALTY:
Any officer, agent or employee who wilfully and knowingly violates the
provisions of this chapter or of any code adopted herein, or any legal order or
regulation made pursuant thereto, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this title. Each day upon which a violation shall continue shall be
deemed a separate offense. (1986 Code § 7-28; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 9
MUNICIPAL COURT
SECTION:
1-9-1: Court Created
1-9-2: Definitions
1-9-3: Jurisdiction Of Court
1-9-4: Judge Of Municipal Court
1-9-5: Change Of Venue; Disqualifications
1-9-6: Chief Of Police
1-9-7: Clerk Of The Court
1-9-8: Prosecuting Officer, City Attorney
1-9-9: Contempt Of Court
1-9-10: Complaints
1-9-11: Traffic Violations; Procedure
1-9-12: Fines For Traffic Violations And Nontraffic Offenses
1-9-13: Maximum Fine And Imprisonment
1-9-14: Costs To Defendant
1-9-15: Jury Trials
1-9-16: Summons
1-9-17: Warrant Of Arrest
1-9-18: Bail
1-9-19: Arraignment
1-9-20: Court Procedure
1-9-21: Imprisonment
1-9-22: Witnesses
1-9-23: Acquittal
1-9-24: Suspended Sentence
1-9-25: Work Performed By Prisoners
1-9-26: Community Service
1-9-1: COURT CREATED:
This chapter shall govern the organization and operation of the municipal court
of the city, as put into operation by resolution duly passed on January 21,
1969, and filed in accordance with law, as authorized by 11 Oklahoma Statutes
sections 27-101 and 27-102. To the extent of conflict between any provisions of
this chapter and the provisions of any other ordinance of the city, the
provisions of this chapter shall control. Said court shall be operative on and
after February 1, 1969. (1986 Code § 12-1)
1-9-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless the context requires a different meaning, the
following words shall mean:
CHIEF OF POLICE: The peace officer in charge of the police force of the city.
CLERK: The clerk of the city, including any deputy or member of the office
staff of the city clerk while performing duties of the clerk's office.
COURT: The municipal court of the city.
GOVERNING BODY: The city council of the city, including the mayor under those
circumstances where he is entitled to vote under the laws of the state of
Oklahoma, and ordinances of the city.
JUDGE: The judge of the municipal court, aforesaid, including any acting judge
or alternate judge thereof as provided for by the statutes of the state, and
this chapter.
THIS JUDICIAL DISTRICT: The district court judicial district of the state of
Oklahoma, wherein the government of the city is situated. (1986 Code § 12-2;
amd. 2005 Code)
1-9-3: JURISDICTION OF COURT:
The court shall exercise original jurisdiction to hear and determine all
prosecutions wherein a violation of any ordinance of the city is charged,
including any such prosecutions transferred to the court in accordance with
applicable law. (1986 Code § 12-3)
1-9-4: JUDGE OF MUNICIPAL COURT:
   A.   Appointment; Qualifications:
      1.   There shall be one judge of the court. A judge must be duly licensed
to practice law in the state of Oklahoma, except as provided herein. He may
engage in the practice of law in other courts, but he shall refrain from
accepting employment inconsistent with his duties as judge, or arising out of
facts which give rise to or are connected with cases within the jurisdiction of
the court pending therein, or which might become the subject of proceedings
therein. He must be a resident of the county in which the city is located or in
an adjacent county, or maintain a permanent office therein. Further, any
suitable person residing in the city or within twenty (20) miles of the
boundaries of the city who is not a licensed attorney may be appointed to serve
as judge as provided by law, but any trial shall be to the court, and the court
may not impose a fine of more than fifty dollars ($50.00) and may not order the
defendant imprisoned except for the nonpayment of fines or costs, or both.
(1986 Code § 12-4)
      2.   Judges and alternate judges shall be appointed by the mayor with the
consent of the governing body. (1986 Code § 12-8)
   B.   Term Of Office: The official term of the judge shall be two (2) years,
expiring on February 1 in each odd numbered year. Each judge, unless sooner
removed for proper cause, shall serve until his successor is appointed and
qualified. (1986 Code § 12-5)
   C.   Alternate Judge: There shall be appointed, for each judge of the court,
an alternate judge, possessed of the same qualifications as a municipal judge.
His appointment shall be for the same term and made in the same manner as the
judge. He shall sit as acting judge of the court in any case if the judge is
absent from the court, unable to act as judge or disqualified from acting as
judge in the case. (1986 Code § 12-6)
   D.   Acting Judge: If, at any time, there is no judge or alternate judge
duly appointed and qualified, available to sit as judge, the mayor shall
appoint some person, possessing the qualifications required by this chapter for
the judge, who shall preside as acting judge over the court in the disposition
of pending matters until such time as a judge or alternate judge shall be
available. (1986 Code § 12-7)
   E.   Salaries:
      1.   A judge, other than an alternate judge or an acting judge shall
receive a monthly salary in such amount as the governing body shall determine,
to be paid in the same manner as the salaries of other officials of the city.
      2.   An acting judge shall be paid the sum of ten dollars ($10.00) for
each day devoted to the performance of this duty or such other amount as the
governing body shall determine, except that, for any month, the total payments
so calculated shall not exceed the salary of the judge in whose stead he sits.
An acting judge who sits for an entire month shall receive the amount specified
as the salary of the judge in whose stead he sits. (1986 Code § 12-9; amd. 2005
Code)
   F.   Removal:
      1.   Judges shall be subject to removal from office, by the governing
body, for the causes prescribed by the constitution and laws of the state for
the removal of public officers. Proceedings for removal shall be instituted by
the filing of a verified written petition, setting forth facts sufficient to
constitute one or more legal grounds for removal. Petitions may be signed and
filed by: a) the mayor; or b) twenty five (25) or more qualified electors of
the city; in the latter event, verification may be executed by one or more of
the petitioners. The governing body shall set a date for hearing the matter,
and shall cause notice thereof, together with a copy of the petition, to be
served personally upon the judge at least ten (10) days before the hearing. At
the hearing, the judge shall be entitled:
         a.   To representation by counsel;
         b.   To present testimony and to cross examine the witnesses against
him; and
         c.   To have all evidence against him presented in open hearing.
      2.   So far as they can be made applicable, the provisions of the
Oklahoma administrative procedure act governing individual proceedings (75
Oklahoma Statutes sections 309 through 317 and any amendments or additions
thereto in effect at the time of the hearing) shall govern removal proceedings
hereunder. Judgment of removal shall be entered only upon individual votes by a
majority of all members of the governing body in favor of such removal. (1986
Code § 12-10)
   G.   Vacancies:
      1.   A vacancy in the office of judge shall occur if the incumbent:
         a.   Dies; or
         b.   Resigns; or
         c.   Ceases to possess the qualifications for office; or
         d.   Is removed, and the removal procedure has been affirmed finally
in judicial proceedings or is no longer subject to judicial review.
      2.   Upon the occurrence of a vacancy in the office of judge, the mayor
shall appoint a successor to complete the unexpired term, upon the same
procedure as an original appointment is made. (1986 Code § 12-11)
   H.   Prescribe Rules: The judge may prescribe rules, consistent with the
laws of the state and with the ordinances of the city, for the proper conduct
of the business of the court. (1986 Code § 12-17)
1-9-5: CHANGE OF VENUE; DISQUALIFICATIONS:
In prosecutions before the court, no change of venue shall be allowed; but the
judge before whom the case is pending may be disqualified from sitting under
the terms, conditions and procedure provided by law for courts of record. If a
judge is disqualified, the matter shall be heard by an acting judge. (1986 Code
§ 12-12)
1-9-6: CHIEF OF POLICE:
All writs or processes of the court shall be directed, in his official title,
to the chief of police of the city, who shall be the principal officer of the
court. The chief of police shall execute any writs or other processes directed
to him, except as herein otherwise provided, and such duty may be performed by
any members of the police force of the city. The chief of police shall be ex
officio marshal of the court. (1986 Code § 12-13)
1-9-7: CLERK OF THE COURT:
   A.   Functions: The municipal clerk, or a deputy designated by him, shall be
the clerk of the court.
      1.   He shall assist the judge in recording the proceedings of the court
and in preparing writs, processes and other papers.
      2.   He shall administer oaths required in proceedings before the court.
      3.   He shall enter all pleadings, processes, and proceedings in the
dockets of the court.
      4.   He shall perform such other clerical duties relating to the
proceedings of the court as the judge shall direct.
      5.   He shall receive and receipt for fines, forfeitures, fees, deposits
and sums of money payable to the court.
      6.   The court clerk shall make duplicate receipts for the fees, fines,
and forfeitures collected by him, one copy of which shall be retained by the
city treasurer together with a detailed statement of all costs, the style of
the case in which they were paid, and the name of the party paying the same.
      7.   He shall pay to the city treasurer, on the first and the fifteenth
days of each month, all monies so received by him, except such special deposits
or fees as shall be received to be disbursed by him for special purposes.
   B.   Disposition Of Funds: All monies received by the city treasurer shall
be placed in the general fund of the city, or in such other fund as the
governing body may direct, and it shall be used in the operation of the
municipal government in accordance with budgetary arrangements governing the
fund in which it is placed. (1986 Code § 12-14)
   C.   Bond: The clerk of the court shall give bond in the form provided by 11
Oklahoma Statutes section 27-111, in the sum of one thousand dollars
($1,000.00). When executed, said bond shall be submitted to the governing body
for approval. When approved, it shall be filed with the clerk of the city and
retained in the municipal archives. (1986 Code § 12-16)
1-9-8: PROSECUTING OFFICER, CITY ATTORNEY:
The attorney for the city, or his duly designated assistant, shall be the
prosecuting officer of the court. The prosecutor shall have full power to
prosecute all alleged violations of the ordinances of the city and shall be
authorized, in his discretion, to prosecute and resist appeals, proceedings in
error and review from this court to any other courts of the state, and to
represent the City in all proceedings arising out of matters in this court.
(1986 Code § 12-15)
1-9-9: CONTEMPT OF COURT:
Obedience to the orders, rules and judgments made by the Judge or by the court
may be enforced by the Judge, who may fine or imprison for contempt committed
as to him while holding court, or committed against processes issued by him, in
the same manner and to the same extent as the district courts of this State.
(1986 Code § 12-18)
1-9-10: COMPLAINTS:
All prosecutions commenced in the Municipal Court shall be by complaint which
shall be subscribed by the person making the complaint and shall be verified
before a Judge, the Court Clerk, a Deputy Court Clerk, or a Police Officer. No
warrant for arrest shall be issued until the complaint has been approved by the
Judge of the Municipal Court. All prosecutions for the violation of Municipal
ordinances shall be styled, "The City of Vinita, Oklahoma, vs. (naming person
or persons charged)". (1986 Code § 12-19)
1-9-11: TRAFFIC VIOLATIONS; PROCEDURE:
   A.   City Resident: If a resident of the City is arrested for the violation
of any ordinance, traffic or nontraffic, by a law enforcement officer, the
officer shall immediately release said person if the person acknowledges
receipt of a citation by signing it, unless it reasonably appears to the
officer that the person may cause injury to himself or others or damage to
property if released, that the person will not appear in response to the
citation, or the person is arrested for an offense against a person or
property. If said person fails to appear in response to the citation, a warrant
shall be issued for his arrest and his appearance shall be compelled.
   B.   Conditions For Release: Any person arrested by a law enforcement
officer for violation of a Municipal traffic ordinance or regulation may be
released after:
      1.   Posting cash bail; or
      2.   Depositing with the arresting office a guaranteed arrest bond
certificate. (1986 Code § 12-20; amd. 2005 Code)
   C.   Parking Violation; Citation Attached To Vehicle: If the alleged offense
be a violation of an ordinance restricting or regulating the parking of
vehicles, including any regulations issued under such an ordinance, and the
operator be not present, the police officer shall place on the vehicle, at a
place reasonably likely to come to the notice of the operator, a citation with
such variation as the circumstances require. The operator of the vehicle shall
be under the same obligation to respond to the citation as if it had been
issued to him personally. (1986 Code § 12-20)
1-9-12: FINES FOR TRAFFIC VIOLATIONS AND NONTRAFFIC OFFENSES:
   A.   Fines Established: A person cited for traffic or nontraffic violations
may elect to pay a fine in the Municipal Court according to the following
schedule; provided however, said schedule may be amended by ordinance or
resolution from time to time:
Violation Code Section Amount Of Fine
