(Ord. 3664, 7-18-2017; amd. Ord. 3708, 8-6-2019)
All other offenses may be bonded by a fine in the amount of one hundred dollars
($100.00), plus court costs then in force and effect.
In addition to a fine, each case is to have collected court costs and penalty
assessments in the maximum amount then permitted by 11 Oklahoma Statutes
section 27-126, as amended, or otherwise imposed by State law.
   B.   Rules; Payment Of Fine: The court may adopt rules to carry into effect
this section. Payment of a fine under this section shall constitute a final
determination of the cause against the defendant. If a defendant who has
elected to pay a fine under this section fails to do so, prosecution shall
proceed under the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 3664, 7-18-2017)
1-9-13: MAXIMUM FINE AND IMPRISONMENT:
The maximum fine for each violation shall be seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00), not including costs, or imprisonment not exceeding sixty (60) days,
or both such fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 3664, 7-18-2017)
1-9-14: COSTS TO DEFENDANT:
   A.   If judgment of conviction is entered, the Clerk of the Court shall tax
the costs and penalty assessments to the defendant in the maximum amount then
permitted by 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 27-126, as amended, or otherwise
imposed by State law, plus the fees and mileage of jurors and witnesses, all of
which the defendant shall pay, in addition to a fine that may be imposed.
   B.   In addition to the costs imposed by subsection A of this section, the
following fees may be assessed to the defendant:
 
Administrative fee             $500.00
Compact letter fee             20.00
Deferral fee                   150.00
Warrant fee, failure to appear 150.00
Warrant fee, failure to pay    10.00
 
   (Ord. 3664, 7-18-2017)
1-9-15: JURY TRIALS:
   A.   Conditions For Trial; Waiver: In all prosecutions for violations of
ordinances punishable by fine of more than two hundred dollars ($200.00), or by
imprisonment, or by both fine and imprisonment, trial shall be by jury unless
waived by the defendant and City. In prosecution for all other offenses, or in
cases wherein a jury trial is waived, trial shall be to the court. (Ord. 3132,
7-18-2000; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Request For Jurors: Whenever a calendar has been made up for the trial
of cases by jury, the Judge shall request, in writing, the Presiding Judge of
the District Court for this judicial district to cause the names of a stated
number of jurors, deemed sufficient to dispose of the cases on the calendar, to
be drawn from the jury wheel in accordance with the governing Statutes of the
State, and to be certified by the Clerk of the District Court to the Judge of
the Municipal Court. The request shall be made in time for the list to be
certified and the jurors to be summoned legally before the trial of the
calendar begins. If it is anticipated that the completion of the calendar will
require more than two (2) weeks, the request for jurors shall specify the
number required for each two (2) week period, as provided by law for the
drawing of jurors for the District Court. Additional drawing of other names
also may be requested by the Judge, when necessary, in accordance with the law
for such additional drawings in the District Court. If, in the future,
provisions of the law respecting the drawing of jury lists for the District
Court are changed, the Judge shall take such steps, in requesting jury lists
for the court, as are necessary to comply with the State law. (1986 Code § 12-
33)
   C.   Jury Summons:
      1.   Upon receipt of the jury list, the Clerk of the Court shall cause a
summons substantially in the following form to be issued and served upon each
person on the list:
   STATE OF OKLAHOMA, COUNTY OF CRAIG, SS:
To (Name of juror) GREETING: You are hereby summoned to appear in the municipal
court for the City of Vinita, Oklahoma, to be held at (specify the address,
room number, etc.) on the      day of               , 20     , at the hour of
(specify hour) to serve as a juror in said court, and to continue in such
service until discharged by the court.
Hereof fail not, under penalty of law.
Issued under the authority of said court, this      day of             ,
20     .
                                                    
         Clerk of the Municipal Court
         of Vinita, Oklahoma
      (Seal of Court)
(1986 Code § 12-34; amd. 2005 Code)
      2.   Service shall be made, as the Judge may prescribe by rule or direct
by order, either in person upon the juror by the Chief of Police or by any
member of the police force of the City, or by the Clerk of the Court, through
certified mail, directed to the juror at his address as given in the jury list,
with request for a personally signed receipt. In any proceeding wherein service
of summons by mail is an issue, evidence of the due mailing of the summons by
the Clerk or a member of his staff and the presentation of an official postal
return receipt purportedly signed by the addressee shall be prima facie
evidence that the summons was duly received by the addressee and, therefore,
that he was properly served therewith. (1986 Code § 12-34)
   D.   Composition Of Jury: A jury in the court shall consist of six (6)
jurors, good and lawful men or women, citizens of Craig County, possessing the
qualifications of jurors in district court. (1986 Code § 12-35)
   E.   Vote Of Jury: A verdict of the jury may be rendered by the vote of five
(5) jurors, except as otherwise provided by law. (1986 Code § 12-36)
   F.   Judicial Notice Of Statutes, Ordinances: The court shall take judicial
notice of state statutes and the ordinances of the city. (1986 Code § 12-37)
   G.   Compensation Of Jurors: Jurors shall receive for their services the sum
of twenty dollars ($20.00) per day, plus mileage at the rate of thirty six
cents ($0.36) per mile for each mile necessarily traveled by the most direct
route in going to and from the court from their respective places of residence.
The claims for such compensation shall show the location of the juror's
residence and the route and miles traveled, and must be verified as other
claims against the city are verified. Jurors shall be paid out of the general
funds of the city. (1986 Code § 12-38; amd. 2005 Code)
1-9-16: SUMMONS:
   A.   Issuance Of Summons: Upon the filing of a complaint charging violation
of this code, or an ordinance, the judge, unless he determines to issue a
warrant of arrest, or unless the defendant previously has been issued a
citation or has been arrested and has given bond for appearance, shall issue a
summons, naming the person charged, specifying his address or place of
residence, if known, stating the offense with which he is charged and giving
him notice to answer the charge in the court on a day certain, containing a
provision for the official return of the summons, and including such other
pertinent information as may be necessary.
   B.   Serving Of Summons: The summons shall be served by delivering a copy to
the defendant personally. If he fails to appear and to answer the summons
within the prescribed period, a warrant shall be issued for his arrest, as
provided by this chapter. (1986 Code § 12-22)
1-9-17: WARRANT OF ARREST:
   A.   Form Of Warrant: Except as otherwise provided in the ordinances of the
city, upon the filing of a complaint approved by endorsement by the judge,
there shall be issued a warrant of arrest, in substantially the following form:
The City of Vinita to the chief of police of Vinita, Oklahoma. Complaint upon
oath having this day been made by (naming complainant) that the offense of
(naming the offense in particular by general terms) has been committed and
accusing (name of defendant) thereof, you are commanded therefore forthwith to
arrest the above named (name of defendant) and bring (insert him, her, or them,
as appropriate) to (naming the place).
WITNESS my hand this        day of              , 20     .
                                                 
         Judge of the Municipal Court
         of Vinita, Oklahoma
(1986 Code § 12-23; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Execution Of Warrant: It shall be the duty of the aforesaid chief of
police, personally, or through a duly constituted member of the police force of
the city, or through any other persons lawfully authorized so to act, to
execute said warrant as promptly as possible.
   C.   Serving Within Craig County: An arrest warrant issued by the court can
be served any place in Craig County. (1986 Code § 12-23)
1-9-18: BAIL:
Upon arrest, or upon appearance without arrest in response to citation or
summons, or at any other time before trial, before or after arraignment, the
defendant shall be eligible to be released upon giving bail for his appearance
in an amount and upon conditions fixed by the judge, who shall prescribe
appropriate rules of court for the receipt of bail and for the release on one's
own recognizance. In case of arrests made at night or under other conditions of
emergency or when the judge is not available, the rules can authorize the chief
of police, or his designated representative, to accept a temporary cash bond,
not more than the maximum monetary penalty provided by ordinance for such
offense charged. The chief of police or his designated representative is
authorized, subject to such conditions as shall be prescribed by the judge, to
release a resident of Vinita on his own recognizance. (1986 Code § 12-24)
1-9-19: ARRAIGNMENT:
Upon making his appearance before the court, the defendant shall be arraigned.
The judge, or the prosecuting attorney, shall read the complaint to the
defendant, inform him of his legal rights, including the right of trial by
jury, if available, and of the consequences of conviction, and ask him whether
he pleads guilty or not guilty. (1986 Code § 12-25)
1-9-20: COURT PROCEDURE:
Except as otherwise provided for by law, the code of procedure in the municipal
court shall be the same as is provided for by law for the trial of
misdemeanors, including rules duly promulgated by the supreme court of Oklahoma
and the court of criminal appeals of Oklahoma. (1986 Code § 12-26)
1-9-21: IMPRISONMENT:
   A.   Refusal To Pay Fine; Work On Public Ways: If a defendant who is
financially able refuses or neglects to pay a fine or costs, or both, payment
may be enforced by imprisonment until the same shall be satisfied at the rate
of five dollars ($5.00) per day. The defendant may be compelled to satisfy the
amount owed by working on the streets, alleys, avenues, areas, and public
grounds of the city at a rate of ten dollars ($10.00) per day for useful labor,
or such amount set by the city from time to time by ordinance, until the fine
or costs are satisfied, if he is able but unwilling to pay such fine.
   B.   Inability To Pay Fine: If the defendant is without means to pay the
fine or costs, the municipal judge may direct the total amount due to be
entered upon the court minutes and to be certified to the district court in
Craig County, where it shall be entered upon the judgment docket and have the
full force and effect of a district court judgment. Thereupon the same remedies
shall be available for the enforcement of the judgment as are available to any
other judgment creditor. (1986 Code § 12-27)
1-9-22: WITNESSES:
   A.   Payment Allowed: Witnesses in any proceeding in the court, other than
police officers or peace officers, shall be entitled to ten dollars ($10.00)
per each day of attendance, plus thirty six cents ($0.36) for each mile
actually and necessarily traveled in going to and returning from the place of
attendance if their residence is outside the limits of the city. However, no
witness shall receive fees or mileage in more than one case for the same period
of time or the same travel. (1986 Code § 12-28; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Deposit From Defendant; Indigents Excepted:
      1.   A defendant seeking to subpoena witnesses must deposit with the
clerk a sum sufficient to cover fees and mileage for one day of attendance for
each witness to be summoned.
      2.   Such deposit shall not be required from an indigent defendant who
files an affidavit setting out:
         a.   The names of no more than three (3) witnesses;
         b.   That the defendant, by reason of his poverty, is unable to
provide the fees and mileage allowed by law;
         c.   That the testimony of said witnesses is material; and
         d.   That their attendance at the trial is necessary for his proper
defense.
The fees of such witnesses shall be paid by the city. (1986 Code § 12-28)
1-9-23: ACQUITTAL:
If judgment is of acquittal, and the defendant is not being detained for any
other legal cause, he must be discharged at once. (1986 Code § 12-29; amd. 2005
Code)
1-9-24: SUSPENDED SENTENCE:
After conviction and sentence, the judge trying the cause may suspend judgment,
costs, or both, in accordance with the provisions of and subject to the
conditions and procedures imposed by, 11 Oklahoma Statutes sections 27-123 and
27-124. (1986 Code § 12-30)
1-9-25: WORK PERFORMED BY PRISONERS:
   A.   Credit Allowed: All prisoners confined to jail on conviction or on plea
of guilty will be credited for serving two (2) days of imprisonment under his
sentence for each day of work on the public streets, avenues, alleys, parks,
buildings, or other public premises or property.
   B.   Direction And Supervision Of Work: The chief of police, subject to the
direction of the mayor, shall direct where the work shall be performed. The
head of the department in charge of the place where the work is to be
performed, himself or by some person designated by him, shall oversee the work.
If a guard is necessary, the chief of police shall make provision therefor.
(1986 Code § 12-39)
1-9-26: COMMUNITY SERVICE:
Any person pleading guilty, pleading no contest, being found guilty, or
agreeing to be assessed an administrative fee for violation of a municipal
ordinance or state statute, may be ordered at the discretion of the court to
perform community service. Community service may be in addition to, or in place
of, incarceration, fines, costs, administrative fees imposed by the court.
Community service shall be performed in the service of departments of the city
of Vinita or any public works controlled by the city of Vinita. (Ord. 3240, 7-
6-2004)
CHAPTER 10
COMPREHENSIVE DEVELOPMENT PLAN
SECTION:
1-10-1: Comprehensive Plan Required
1-10-2: Comprehensive Plan Prepared
1-10-3: Public Hearing; Plan Adopted
1-10-1: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN REQUIRED:
The city council is required to prepare and adopt a comprehensive plan to guide
the physical development of the Vinita urban area. (1986 Code § 16-8)
1-10-2: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN PREPARED:
The planning commission has caused to be prepared a proposed plan titled "A
Comprehensive Development Plan - Vinita, Oklahoma", adoption of which the city
council deems to be in the public interest and in keeping with the purposes set
forth in 11 Oklahoma Statutes sections 43-103. (1986 Code § 16-9; amd. 2005
Code)
1-10-3: PUBLIC HEARING; PLAN ADOPTED:
   A.   Hearing: The planning commission did hold a public hearing on August
29, 1967, for the purpose of considering the adoption of the comprehensive
plan, in whole or in part. Public notice of such meeting was duly given as
required by law. (1986 Code § 16-10)
   B.   Plan Considered: The city council attended said public hearing and have
given consideration to the public hearing and the contents of "A Comprehensive
Plan - Vinita Oklahoma". (1986 Code § 16-11)
   C.   Plan Adopted: The city council determined that the comprehensive
development plan as prepared by the planning commission and presented at said
public hearing (a true and correct copy of which is attached to resolution
dated August 25, 1967, as exhibit A) is hereby adopted as a part of the
official comprehensive plan of the city as prescribed by 11 Oklahoma Statutes
section 43-103. Said comprehensive plan consists of the following parts: (1986
Code § 16-12; amd. 2005 Code)
Goals and policies for the use of private property:
Residential development goals
   Commercial development goals
Industrial development goals
Goals and policies for the development of public property and facilities:
Education facilities
Parks, recreation, and open space
Public parking
Trafficways plan
Public utilities
Civic center plan
(1986 Code § 16-12)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 0
BOARDS; GENERALLY
SECTION:
2-0-1: Membership
2-0-1: MEMBERSHIP:
Membership on the library board or the board of directors of the Eastern Trail
Museum or the board of directors of Vinita senior citizens or the Vinita
chamber of commerce shall not serve to disqualify an otherwise qualified
individual from simultaneously serving upon one or all of such boards while
also serving on the Vinita city council. (Ord. 3599, 5-19-2015)
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Created; Terms; Compensation
2-1-2: Chairman And Secretary
2-1-3: Rules And Regulations; Meetings
2-1-4: Duties And Powers
2-1-5: Actions Of Commission And Council
2-1-6: Plats And Subdivisions
2-1-7: Expenditures
2-1-8: Regional Planning Commission
2-1-1: COMMISSION CREATED; TERMS; COMPENSATION:
   A.   Membership; Terms: There is hereby created in the city a planning
commission to be composed of five (5) members. The members shall be nominated
by the mayor and confirmed by the city council. Each member shall serve for a
period of three (3) years.
   B.   Appointment; Qualifications: The members of said commission shall be
appointed from residents of the city, and effort is to be made to secure the
services of persons best qualified to plan for the future growth, development
and improvement of the city, and in the orderly development of city planning
for the city as a whole.
   C.   Compensation: The members of the city planning commission shall serve
without salary.
   D.   Vacancy: In the event of a vacancy on said commission for any reason, a
successor shall be appointed as herein provided for the unexpired term only of
such vacancy. (1986 Code § 16-1)
2-1-2: CHAIRMAN AND SECRETARY:
The commission shall meet and elect one of their number as chairman and one of
their number as secretary. Such officers when so elected shall serve in their
respective capacity for a term of one year, or until their successors are
elected and qualified. (1986 Code § 16-2)
2-1-3: RULES AND REGULATIONS; MEETINGS:
The city planning commission shall prescribe rules and regulations governing
and controlling the transaction of business before it, and shall determine a
date each quarter for regular meetings. Special meetings may be called at any
time by the chairman of the commission or by any three (3) members. (Ord. 3586,
10-21-2014, eff. 1-1-2015)
2-1-4: DUTIES AND POWERS:
The duties and powers of the planning commission shall be as follows:
   A.   The planning commission shall investigate and recommend to the mayor
and city council suitable zoning ordinances for the city.
   B.   The planning commission shall prepare from time to time plans for the
betterment of the municipality as a place of residence or for business. It may
consider and investigate any subject matter tending to the development and
betterment of the municipality, and make recommendations as it may deem
advisable concerning the adoption thereof, to any department of the municipal
government, and for any purpose make or cause to be made surveys, maps or
plans.
   C.   The planning commission shall have the power and authority to employ
engineers, attorneys, clerks and a secretary, or any other help deemed
necessary, subject to the approval of the city council.
   D.   Before final action may be taken by any municipality or department
thereof on the location, construction, or design of any public building,
statue, memorial, park, parkway, boulevard, street, alley, playground, public
ground, or bridge, or the change in the location or grade of any street or
alley, the question shall be submitted to the planning commission for
investigation and report.
   E.   The planning commission may exercise jurisdiction over subdivision of
land and adopt regulations governing the subdivision of land within its
jurisdiction. Any such regulations, before they become effective, shall be
approved by the city council and shall be published as provided by law for the
publication of ordinances.
   F.   All findings and recommendations of the city planning commission
affecting private property shall be submitted in writing to the city council
for its examination, approval or rejection.
   G.   Any suit to challenge any action, decision, ruling or order of the
planning commission shall be filed with the district court within thirty (30)
business days from the action, decision, ruling or order.
(1986 Code § 16-4; amd. Ord. 3842, 6- 18-2024)
2-1-5: ACTIONS OF COMMISSION AND COUNCIL:
All projects or matters that fail within the purview of the duties of the city
planning commission, as herein specified, that may come before the city council
shall be referred to the city planning commission for investigation and report
before any final action shall be taken thereon; provided however, that if the
city planning commission shall fail to make an investigation and report on any
matter or subject referred to it for a period of sixty (60) days, such failure
shall be considered a refusal to approve the proposed plan or project and the
city council may thereupon act to approve the proposed plan or project and the
city council may thereupon act upon such proposal, plan or project as though
such matter had not been referred to the said planning commission. (1986 Code §
16-5)
2-1-6: PLATS AND SUBDIVISIONS:
   A.   Hearing: No platting of unplatted property in the city, no replatting
of any existing subdivision in the city and no platting or subdivisions of
property adjoining the city shall be permitted until such plat or resubdivision
shall be presented to the city planning commission and a hearing had thereon.
   B.   Publishing And Posting Notice: Upon such matter being presented to the
city planning commission, it shall cause a notice to be published at least once
in a newspaper published in the city not less than fifteen (15) days prior to
the hearing, which notice shall briefly set out the proposed replatting or
subdivision, and the time and place of hearing upon such proposal. In addition,
there shall be posted for not less than fifteen (15) days on the property
involved, a sign of type and size approved by the city planning commission
stating briefly the proposed platting, replatting or subdivision, and the time
and place of hearing on such proposal.
   C.   Recommendations To Council: After a hearing conducted in the manner
above set forth, the city planning commission shall make its findings and
recommendations to the city council concerning the adoption, modification or
rejection of said platting, replatting or subdivision.
   D.   Costs Borne By Applicant: All costs of publication and other expenses
necessarily incurred in connection with such hearings shall be at the expense
of the person or parties applying for such approval. (1986 Code § 16-6)
2-1-7: EXPENDITURES:
The city planning commission shall make application to the city council for the
funds which are necessary for such planning commission to expend in order to
carry out its duties as herein specified. At the beginning of each fiscal year,
the planning commission shall make application to the city council for an
appropriation to be set up for its use in carrying out its duties, and the city
shall include such appropriation in its estimate to be approved by the excise
board of Craig County. (1986 Code § 16-7)
2-1-8: REGIONAL PLANNING COMMISSION:
   A.   Composition And Compensation: There is hereby appointed a regional
planning commission, which members shall consist of the members of the city
planning commission, the mayor, city engineer, chairman of the board of county
commissioners, and the county engineer. Said members shall serve without pay.
(1986 Code § 16-21)
   B.   Jurisdiction: The regional planning commission shall have jurisdiction
over a regional district which shall include any land outside the incorporated
limits of the city whose any one boundary, at any point, shall be within a
distance of three (3) miles from the incorporated limits of the city. (1986
Code § 16-22)
   C.   Duties And Responsibilities: The regional planning commission shall
have such duties, powers, rights and responsibilities as set out at 11 Oklahoma
Statutes section 46-101 et seq., as may be amended from time to time. (1986
Code § 16-23)
CHAPTER 2
AIRPORT COMMISSION
(Rep. by Ord. 3535, 9-4-2012)
CHAPTER 3
EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT ORGANIZATION
SECTION:
2-3-1: Purpose
2-3-2: Department Established; Composition
2-3-3: Director Of Emergency Management
2-3-4: Plans; Information; Records
2-3-5: Emergencies
2-3-6: Law Enforcement; Arrests
2-3-7: Compensation
2-3-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to create an emergency management organization
for the city to be prepared for, and to function in the event of, emergencies
endangering the lives and property of the people of the city. The duty of the
emergency management organization shall be the protection of the lives and
health of the citizens of the city and of property and property rights, both
private and public, and to perform all functions necessary and incident
thereto. (1986 Code § 1-60; amd. 2005 Code)
2-3-2: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED; COMPOSITION:
There is hereby established under the executive branch of the government of the
city a department of emergency management, which shall consist of: (1986 Code §
1-61; amd. 2005 Code)
   A.   Director, Deputy Director: A director of emergency management who shall
be appointed by the mayor, with the advice and consent of the city council, and
serve at his pleasure. A deputy director of emergency management who shall be
appointed by the mayor, with the advice and consent of the city council, and
serve at his pleasure. (Ord. 3434, 6-2-2009)
   B.   Committee: An emergency management advisory committee.
      1.   This committee shall consist of the mayor as chairman and five (5)
members appointed by the mayor and serving at his pleasure.
      2.   The committee shall select from its members a vice chairman and
secretary.
      3.   It shall hold such meetings as are directed by the mayor, and its
function shall be to act in an advisory capacity as needed or requested by the
mayor or the director of emergency management. (1986 Code § 1-61; amd. 2005
Code)
2-3-3: DIRECTOR OF EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT:
   A.   Powers And Duties:
      1.   The director of emergency management shall be the executive head of
the department of emergency management and shall be responsible for carrying
out the emergency management program of the city.
      2.   It is the duty of the director of emergency management, as soon as
practicable after his appointment, to perfect an organization to carry out the
purposes set forth in this chapter, and he shall have all necessary power and
authority to form committees or other bodies and to appoint and designate the
chairman or chief officer of such bodies as may be necessary to perfect such an
organization.
      3.   He shall have such further duty and responsibility to cooperate with
all emergency management agencies of other governmental units including the
state of Oklahoma and the federal government.
      4.   The deputy director shall assist the director in carrying out the
emergency management program of the city and shall have such powers and duties
as specified by the director. In the absence of the director, the deputy
director shall have the full powers and duties of the director.
   B.   Compensation; Expenses: The director and deputy director shall serve
without compensation but may be reimbursed for expenses incurred in the
performance of their duties. (Ord. 3434, 6-2-2009)
2-3-4: PLANS; INFORMATION; RECORDS:
The director of emergency management is further authorized to formulate written
plans and gather information and keep written records thereof to govern the
functions of the emergency management organization. (1986 Code § 1-63; amd.
2005 Code)
2-3-5: EMERGENCIES:
   A.   Authority Of Director: In the event of an enemy caused emergency or
emergency resulting from natural causes, the director of emergency management,
after due authorization from the mayor, shall have the power and authority to
enforce all rules and regulations relating to and, if necessary, take control
of transportation, communications, stocks of fuel, food, clothing, medicine and
public utilities for the purpose of protecting the civilian population.
   B.   Cooperate With Other Governmental Agencies: He shall cooperate in every
way with the activities of other governmental agencies or organizations; and,
if required by the mayor, shall have control over any and all funds allocated
from any source for the purpose of alleviating distress conditions in the city.
(1986 Code § 1-64; amd. 2005 Code)
2-3-6: LAW ENFORCEMENT; ARRESTS:
The director of emergency management and other members of the emergency
management organization shall have the power and authority to enforce the laws
of the state of Oklahoma and ordinances of the city during the period of
emergency and shall at such time have the further power to make arrests for
violations of such laws or ordinances. (1986 Code § 1-65; amd. 2005 Code)
2-3-7: COMPENSATION:
All members of the emergency management organization created hereunder shall
serve without compensation. (Ord. 3434, 6-2-2009)
CHAPTER 4
FIREFIGHTERS PENSION AND RETIREMENT BOARD
SECTION:
2-4-1: Board Created
2-4-2: Operation Of Fund
2-4-3: Deductions From Compensation
2-4-1: BOARD CREATED:
There is hereby created the local firefighters pension and retirement board of
the firefighters pension and retirement system of the city, with membership,
organization, powers, duties and functions as prescribed by 11 Oklahoma
Statutes section 49-103 et seq., and as may be provided by any later laws
relating to said board. (1986 Code § 1-73)
2-4-2: OPERATION OF FUND:
The firefighters pension and retirement system shall be operated in accordance
with state law relating to the fund, and pensions and other benefits shall be
paid as provided by state law. (1986 Code § 1-74)
2-4-3: DEDUCTIONS FROM COMPENSATION:
   A.   Monthly Deductions From Compensation:
      1.   It shall be the duty of the city treasurer to deduct monthly from
the salary or wages of each member of the fire department of the city an amount
equal to eight percent (8%), which deduction shall be considered the minimum
deduction. The members of a fire department, by a majority vote of its paid
members, may vote to increase the amount of the deduction.
      2.   The treasurer shall deposit monthly in the Oklahoma firefighters
pension and retirement system the amounts deducted from the salary or wages of
each member of the fire department.
      3.   All such deductions so made shall be set forth on each payroll in a
legible manner so that each member of the fire department contributing to the
fund may be able to ascertain the exact amount which he is contributing.
   B.   Monthly Deposit With State: It shall be the duty of the city treasurer
to deposit monthly with the Oklahoma firefighters pension and retirement board
an amount equal to ten percent (10%) of the total actual pay based salaries of
the members of the fire department. (1986 Code § 1-75)
CHAPTER 5
POLICE PENSION AND RETIREMENT BOARD
SECTION:
2-5-1: Board Created
2-5-2: Operation Of Fund
2-5-1: BOARD CREATED:
There is hereby created the local pension and retirement board of the Oklahoma
police pension and retirement system of the city, with membership,
organization, powers, duties, and functions as prescribed by 11 Oklahoma
Statutes section 50-101 et seq. (1986 Code § 1-89)
2-5-2: OPERATION OF FUND:
The Oklahoma police pension and retirement system shall be operated in
accordance with the state law relating to the fund, and pensions and other
benefits shall be paid as provided by state law. (1986 Code § 1-90)
CHAPTER 6
TREE BOARD
SECTION:
2-6-1: Definitions
2-6-2: Board Created; Membership
2-6-3: Terms Of Office; Vacancies
2-6-4: Compensation
2-6-5: Duties And Responsibilities
2-6-6: Board Operation
2-6-7: Review By Council
2-6-8: Public Tree Care
2-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms, as used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
PARK TREES: Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation in public
parks having individual names, and all areas owned by the city, or to which the
public has free access as a park.
STREET TREES: Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation on land
lying between property lines on either side of all streets, avenues, or ways
within the city. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-2: BOARD CREATED; MEMBERSHIP:
There is hereby created and established a city tree board for the city which
shall consist of five (5) members, citizens and residents of this area, who
shall be appointed by the mayor with the approval of the city council. (Ord.
2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-3: TERMS OF OFFICE; VACANCIES:
   A.   Terms: The terms of the five (5) persons to be appointed by the mayor
shall be three (3) years, except that the term of two (2) of the members
appointed to the first board shall be for only one year and the term of two (2)
members of the first board shall be for two (2) years.
   B.   Vacancies: In the event that a vacancy shall occur during the term of
any member, his successor shall be appointed for the unexpired portion of the
term. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-4: COMPENSATION:
Members of the board shall serve without compensation. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-5: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   Tree Plan Preparation:
      1.   It shall be the responsibility of the board to study, investigate,
counsel and develop and/or update annually a written plan for the care,
preservation, trimming, planting, replanting, removal or disposition of trees
and shrubs in public ways, streets and alleys.
      2.   Such plan will be presented annually to the city and upon their
acceptance and approval shall constitute the official council comprehensive
city tree plan for the city of Vinita, Oklahoma.
   B.   Planting, Pruning, Removal; Permit:
      1.   The city tree board, or its agent, shall be responsible for the
planting, pruning, and removal of all trees located within the street rights of
way, easements, alleys and parks of the city.
      2.   The owner of land abutting on any street may, when acting within the
provisions of this chapter, prune, spray, plant or remove trees in that part of
the street abutting his land not used for public travel.
      3.   A street tree permit shall be required only when the owner of
property intends to deviate from the rules and regulations contained in this
chapter.
   C.   Investigations; Recommendations To Council: The board, when requested
by the city council, shall consider, investigate, make findings, report and
recommend upon any special matter or question coming within the scope of its
work. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-6: BOARD OPERATION:
   A.   Officers; Rules: The board shall choose its own officers, make its own
rules and regulations and keep a journal of its proceedings.
   B.   Quorum: A majority of the members shall be a quorum for the transaction
of business. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-7: REVIEW BY COUNCIL:
   A.   Review: The city council shall have the right to review the conduct,
acts and decisions of the city tree board.
   B.   Appeal Board Ruling To Council: Any person may appeal from any ruling
or order of the city tree board to the city council who may hear the matter and
make the final decision. (Ord. 2831, 7-2-1991)
2-6-8: PUBLIC TREE CARE:
   A.   Planting Of Trees: The city shall have the right to plant, trim, spray,
preserve, and remove trees, plants, and shrubs within the lines of all streets,
alleys, avenues, lanes, squares, and public grounds, as may be necessary to
ensure safety when servicing city utilities or to preserve the symmetry and
beauty of such public grounds.
   B.   Removal Of Trees: The city tree board may remove or cause or order to
be removed, any tree or part thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which
by reason of its nature is injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas
lines, water lines or other public improvements, or other pest. (Ord. 2831, 7-
2-1991)
TITLE 3
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUSINESS LICENSE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
3-1-1: License Required; Tax; Term
3-1-2: Separate Licenses Required
3-1-3: Display Of License
3-1-4: Transfer Of License
3-1-5: Duplicate License; Fee
3-1-6: License Tax Levied On Certain Occupations
3-1-7: Itinerant Occupations
3-1-8: Revocation Of License
3-1-9: Penalty
3-1-1: LICENSE REQUIRED; TAX; TERM:
   A.   Payment Of Tax; Securing Of License: It is unlawful for any person,
firm, association or corporation to engage in, exercise or pursue any business,
profession, trade, occupation or privilege for which a license tax is levied by
this title or by any other ordinance or ordinance provision without paying the
license tax, and securing and possessing a valid license therefor.
   B.   Issuance Of License: Upon making proper application to the city clerk,
the payment of the license tax and fulfillment of any other condition which may
be prescribed by law and/or ordinance, the city clerk shall issue a license
therefor. (1986 Code § 5-1)
   C.   License Expiration; Proration Of Tax: Annual licenses shall expire on
June 30 of the year for which they are issued. When an annual license is issued
after July 1 for the remainder of the year to a person, firm, association or
corporation just beginning to engage in, exercise or pursue a business,
profession, trade, occupation or privilege, the tax collected shall be a
fractional part of the annual tax equal to the fraction of the year remaining;
provided, that the minimum tax for a part of a year shall be one-twelfth (1/12)
of the required annual tax. (1986 Code § 5-1; amd. 2005 Code)
3-1-2: SEPARATE LICENSES REQUIRED:
Every person, firm, association or corporation who engages in, exercises, or
pursues a business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege for which a
license is required, at or from more than one place in the city, or who engages
in, exercises or pursues more than one such business, profession, trade,
occupation or privilege, shall pay the fee, and secure a separate license, for
each such place and/or for each such business, profession, trade, occupation or
privilege. (1986 Code § 5-2)
3-1-3: DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
   A.   Display: Every holder of a license to engage in, exercise or pursue a
business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege shall conspicuously
display the license at all times in some part of his place of business or
activity where a person who has entered the place may readily see it; or, if he
has no particular place of business or activity, shall carry the license and
display it to any person who requests to see it.
   B.   Coin Operated Devices: Provided that, in lieu of the above manner of
displaying such licenses, when licenses are required for coin operated music or
amusement devices, vending machines, and similar devices and equipment, the
license may be placed on or attached to such device or equipment in such
position and manner that it will be clearly visible; and shall be so placed or
attached if the license so states on its face.
   C.   Refusal To Display: It is unlawful to fail or refuse to display the
license as required in this section. (1986 Code § 5-3)
3-1-4: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
Unless otherwise provided, it shall be unlawful to assign or transfer any
licenses issued by the city. (1986 Code § 5-5)
3-1-5: DUPLICATE LICENSE; FEE:
   A.   Issuance: Whenever any license to engage in, exercise or pursue a
business, profession, trade, occupation or privilege has been lost or destroyed
without any wrongful act or connivance by the holder, the city clerk, on
application, shall issue a duplicate license for the unexpired time.
   B.   Affidavit: Before the duplicate is issued, the holder shall make and
file with the city clerk an affidavit that the license has not been
transferred, that it has been lost or destroyed without any wrongful act or
connivance by the holder; and that, if believed lost, he has made diligent
search for it and has not been able to find it. (1986 Code § 5-6)
   C.   Fee: The fee for every duplicate license issued, payable to the city
clerk, shall be ten dollars ($10.00). (1986 Code § 5-6; amd. 2005 Code)
3-1-6: LICENSE TAX LEVIED ON CERTAIN OCCUPATIONS:
There is hereby levied an occupation tax in the amount per annum or per day, at
the option of the taxpayer, against persons, firms, associations and
corporations engaged in itinerant occupations, trades or business within the
city, in the amount hereinafter specified:
          Tax
Business  Per Annum Per Day
