   C.   One License: Only one license fee shall be required for such place of
business. (1986 Code § 5-9)
3-4-3: MORAL CHARACTER OF OPERATOR:
The operation of a pool, billiard or domino hall by a person not of good moral
character is considered and declared to be a public nuisance. (1986 Code § 5-
13)
3-4-4: TIME OF OPERATION:
No such hall shall be operated between twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and
seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. on any day nor on Sunday, with the exception that
recreation centers containing pool or billiard tables but not containing domino
tables or similar tables may be opened and operated under the provisions of
this chapter between the hours of one o'clock (1:00) P.M. and five thirty
o'clock (5:30) P.M. on Sundays. (1986 Code § 5-12)
3-4-5: AGE LIMIT:
No person under the age of sixteen (16) years shall be permitted to play pool,
dominoes, billiards or checkers in said pool, domino or billiard hall, unless
accompanied by parent or guardian, nor shall they be allowed to work in said
pool, billiard or domino hall. (1986 Code § 5-12)
3-4-6: VIEW INSIDE PREMISES:
   A.   Window Requirement: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to operate or conduct a public pool hall or public billiard hall or
place of business where beer is sold for consumption on the premises in the
city, except in a building with large front glass windows, or with a large
glass front, and which faces on the public street.
   B.   Curtains Or Blinds Prohibited: It shall further be unlawful for any
such person, firm or corporation, and the employees thereof, to place and
maintain blinds, curtains or any other thing upon or over such windows or glass
front which in anywise obstructs the view of the interior of such room from the
outside front of such building while such place is open for business. (1986
Code § 5-14)
3-4-7: SPECIFIC VIOLATIONS:
The following acts are hereby prohibited:
   A.   Violation of any of the provisions of this chapter.
   B.   Drunkenness of the person holding such license, including any agent,
servant or employee taking any active part in the management, conducting or
carrying on of such business, or permitting any intoxicated person to loiter in
such business.
   C.   Permitting persons prohibited by ordinances of the city by reason of
age to resort to such place of business unless accompanied by parent or
guardian. (1986 Code § 5-11)
   D.   Violation of any of the laws of the state of Oklahoma pertaining to
intoxicating liquor or low point beer, or violation of any of the laws of the
state of Oklahoma in or about such place of business by the owner or lessee
thereof or any person engaged in management, operating, conducting or carrying
on of such business, or permitting anyone to violate such laws in said place of
business. (1986 Code § 5-11; amd. 2005 Code)
   E.   The employment of any person to participate in the management,
operating, conducting or carrying on of such business that is not of good moral
character.
   F.   Any conduct on the part of the owner, lessee or agent, servant or
employee engaged in the management, conducting, operating or carrying on of
said business which evidences bad moral character. (1986 Code § 5-11)
3-4-8: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The mayor and city council may revoke the license of any person, firm,
corporation or association to operate a pool, billiard or domino hall, and such
revocation shall operate to close any pool, billiard or domino hall under said
license upon the grounds set out in section
3-4-7 of this chapter. (1986 Code § 5-10)
3-4-9: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 5
AUCTIONS; SOLICITATIONS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Auction Sales
3-5-2: Solicitation Of Orders
3-5-3: Penalty
3-5-1: AUCTION SALES:
   A.   License Fee: Before any person, firm or corporation shall sell or
expose for sale, at public or private auction in the city, any bankrupt or
other stock of goods, wares or merchandise, or shall sell or offer for sale any
merchandise of any character whatsoever in the city, at public or private
auction, the owner thereof shall first pay to the city a license fee or tax of
one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each day such goods, wares or merchandise is
to be sold or offered for sale in the city. (1986 Code § 5-15; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Application For License: Any person, firm or corporation desiring to
sell or to offer for sale any of the goods, wares or merchandise at auction in
the city under the provisions of subsection A of this section shall make
application to the city clerk in writing, specifying the name of the owner of
the goods, wares or merchandise to be sold or exposed for sale, the character
of the same, and the name of the person proposing to carry on said business,
and the place where said business is to be carried on, and the length of time
such auction business is to be conducted. (1986 Code § 5-16)
3-5-2: SOLICITATION OF ORDERS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to solicit orders for, solicit the purchase
of, or otherwise attempt to sell any goods or services or to solicit
appointments for such purposes either in person, by telephone or otherwise at
any place of residence within the city after seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. of any
day, unless the person soliciting such orders, purchases or appointments has
previously obtained an appointment with the occupants of such place of
residence and their consent to solicit such purchases or orders at the
approximate time involved. (1986 Code § 5-17)
3-5-3: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 6
JUNKYARDS
SECTION:
3-6-1: Definitions
3-6-2: Application For License; Fee
3-6-3: Junkyards Prohibited; Exception
3-6-4: Yard Wall
3-6-5: Register Of Property
3-6-6: Inspection Of Register And Merchandise
3-6-7: Junk Motor Vehicles
3-6-8: Penalty
3-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
JUNK: All kinds of previously used or secondhand rags, sacks, bottles, cans,
paper, metal and used or damaged automobiles, or other vehicles or machinery
not in running condition or not suitable economically to be repaired or
restored to their original use, or used or damaged automobiles, vehicles or
other machinery purchased, acquired or used for salvage purposes for the
benefit of the metal, material or parts therein contained in whole or in part,
and all other articles of whatsoever nature or kind, commonly purchased after
primary use and kept or sold for subsequent use, consumption or traffic, and
otherwise commonly known as "junk".
JUNK DEALER: Any person, firm or corporation, or agent, employee or servant
thereof engaged in the business of buying, selling or offering for sale or
trade, or otherwise dealing in junk, including the storing or the displaying of
junk or the dismantling, stripping or removal of parts from used automobiles or
other vehicles or machinery in whole or in part for the benefit of the metal,
materials or parts therein contained or stripped. Automobile and tire dealers
who receive or accept used automobiles or tires as down payment or part payment
upon commodities handled by them shall not be included within the terms of this
chapter; provided however, in the case of automobile dealers, that such used
automobiles are not dismantled or stripped in whole or in part by such
automobile dealer for the purpose of obtaining the metal, material, salvage or
parts therefrom.
JUNK MOTOR VEHICLE: Means and includes all automobiles, trucks or other motor
vehicles in such used or damaged condition as not to be economically suitable
to be repaired and restored to their original intended use; all automobiles,
trucks or other motor vehicles from which the metals, materials or parts have
been or are being removed for other use; and all automobiles, trucks or other
motor vehicles which are not in operating condition, unless such latter
automobiles, trucks or other motor vehicles are actually being repaired by or
on behalf of the owner thereof within the time reasonably required for the
repair of the same after they have ceased to operate. Any automobile, truck or
other motor vehicle which is required by law to bear and display a license tag
and which is not in safe operating condition and does not bear and display a
current license tag as required by law shall be presumed to be a "junk motor
vehicle".
JUNKYARD: Includes any place where "junk", as defined herein, is dismantled or
stripped in whole or in part, bought, sold, stored, displayed or otherwise
dealt with by a junk dealer. (1986 Code § 5-25)
3-6-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; FEE:
   A.   Application: Application for a license to operate a junkyard shall be
made to the city clerk on forms provided by him. The application shall contain
the name of the junk dealer, the location of the junkyard or business, and such
other information as the mayor and city council may from time to time require.
(1986 Code § 5-27)
   B.   Fee: For the operation of a business of dealing in junk, the license
fee for each shop or yard shall be fifty dollars ($50.00) per year. (Ord. 3310,
4-18-2006)
3-6-3: JUNKYARDS PROHIBITED; EXCEPTION:
   A.   Prohibition; New Junkyards: No new junkyard shall be established within
the corporate limits of the city.
   B.   Exception; Existing Junkyards: This prohibition shall not apply to
junkyards existing in areas which may subsequently be annexed within the
municipal boundaries. Such preexisting junkyards in annexed areas shall, upon
annexation, secure the license for operation, and shall comply with the other
provisions of this chapter within the time limits from the date of such
annexation as are granted to junkyards existing within the city upon the
initial effective date hereof. (1986 Code § 5-28)
3-6-4: YARD WALL:
   A.   Fence Required; Height: In any case where a junkyard is operated in a
yard or open space outside of any building, it shall be the duty of the
operator or proprietor to erect and maintain a solid fence, not less than seven
feet (7') high, entirely around the premises where junk is stored, displayed or
visible.
   B.   Construction Materials; Maintenance: The fence shall be made of new,
noncombustible materials, sightly in appearance, and it shall be kept in good
repair at all times.
   C.   Visibility Of Junk: Junk shall be piled in such manner within the
junkyard as not to be visible from the street or alley upon which such yard
abuts, nor from the ground floor of residential or business property which may
be adjacent thereto.
   D.   Time Limit For Compliance: Any junkyard which exists on the effective
date of this chapter is given a period of thirty (30) days within which to
comply with the yard wall requirements herein set forth. (1986 Code § 5-29)
3-6-5: REGISTER OF PROPERTY:
   A.   Register; Information Required: Each junkyard operator shall maintain a
register in which he shall enter the item or items which he acquired in the
course of trading, for sale or trade, showing its true character, sufficient
for purposes of identification, the person from whom acquired, and the date on
which acquired.
   B.   Making Entries:
      1.   He shall make such entry within two (2) hours of receiving or
purchasing the property.
      2.   Every entry shall be made in ink and shall not in any manner be
obliterated or erased. (1986 Code § 5-30)
3-6-6: INSPECTION OF REGISTER AND MERCHANDISE:
The register herein required and any goods, wares and merchandise which such
junk dealer may acquire in the course of his business and offers for sale or
trade shall be subject to the inspection of the chief of police, the city
attorney, and anyone authorized in writing by the chief of police, which
authorization shall be exhibited to the junkyard dealer before inspection is
made. (1986 Code § 5-31; amd. 2005 Code)
3-6-7: JUNK MOTOR VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation, or agent, employee or
servant thereof, to park and leave standing upon any public property within the
view of the public or persons living nearby, or to permit to be parked and left
standing upon any private property under his possession or control within view
of the public or persons living nearby any "junk motor vehicle", as defined in
section
3-6-1 of this chapter, except for such time as may be reasonably required to
cause the same to be removed; provided, however, that the provisions of this
section shall not apply to junk motor vehicles parked and left standing at any
place of business authorized by law to deal with, store or repair such motor
vehicles and which is operating in compliance with the zoning ordinances and
other ordinances of the city. (Ord. 3380, 11-20-2007)
3-6-8: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 7
STREET SALES
SECTION:
3-7-1: Street Sale Regulations
3-7-2: Penalty
3-7-1: STREET SALE REGULATIONS:
   A.   Sales Prohibited: No person, firm or corporation shall engage in any
selling of goods, wares, automobiles and merchandise upon the streets and
alleys of the city. (1986 Code § 5-32)
   B.   Exception: Prohibition of street sales shall not apply to any such
sales of goods, wares, and merchandise on the streets and alleys of the city
when said streets and alleys have been barricaded by the police department of
the city. (1986 Code § 5-33)
3-7-2: PENALTY:
Any persons violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code; amd. Ord. 3282, 8-2-2005)
CHAPTER 8
PAWNBROKERS
SECTION:
3-8-1: Definition
3-8-2: License Required; Fee
3-8-3: Records And Reports
3-8-4: Sale Of Property Or Pledge
3-8-5: Minors And Intoxicated Persons
3-8-6: Penalty
3-8-1: DEFINITION:
Any person who lends money upon deposit, or pledge of personal property or
valuable thing, or any person who lends money upon chattel property for
security, and requires possession of property so mortgaged, on condition of
returning the same upon payment of a stipulated amount of money, hereby is
declared to be a "pawnbroker". (1986 Code § 5-18)
3-8-2: LICENSE REQUIRED; FEE:
   A.   License Required: No person, corporation, partnership or association of
any kind shall carry on the business of a pawnbroker without first having
obtained a license to do so.
   B.   Fee: The license fee shall be fifty dollars ($50.00) per year. (1986
Code § 5-19)
3-8-3: RECORDS AND REPORTS:
   A.   Record Kept; Contents; Inspection: All persons who shall be engaged in
the business of pawnbrokers shall keep a book in which shall be legibly written
in ink, or typewritten, at the time of any loan or purchase, an accurate
account or description, in the English language, of the goods, articles, or
things pawned, pledged, or purchased, the amount of money lent or paid
therefor, the time the same was received, and the name, residence and
description of the person pawning, pledging or selling the same, which book as
well as the articles pawned or purchased, at all times, shall be open to the
inspection of the chief of police. (1986 Code § 5-20)
   B.   Daily Report, Contents: Every pawnbroker in the city shall make out and
deliver to the chief of police every day a legible and correct copy from the
book required in subsection A of this section of all personal property or other
valuable things received, deposited or purchased during the preceding day,
together with the time when received or purchased and a description of the
person by whom left in pledge. (1986 Code § 5-21)
3-8-4: SALE OF PROPERTY OR PLEDGE:
   A.   Holding Personal Property: No personal property received on pledge by
any pawnbroker shall be sold or permitted to be redeemed from the place of
business of such pawnbroker for the space of twenty four (24) hours after the
copy and statement required to be delivered to the chief of police shall have
been delivered as required by subsection
3-8-3B of this chapter. (1986 Code § 5-22)
   B.   Selling Pledge Before Default: No pawnbroker shall sell any article
received by him in pledge before the time to redeem has expired. (1986 Code §
5-23)
3-8-5: MINORS AND INTOXICATED PERSONS:
No pawnbroker shall take or receive upon deposit, pawn or pledge any personal
property of any kind from a minor; and no pawnbroker knowingly shall receive on
pawn or deposit any personal property of any kind from any person not being the
owner thereof or from any intoxicated person. (1986 Code § 5-24)
3-8-6: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 9
ICE CREAM SALES FROM VEHICLES
SECTION:
3-9-1: License Required; Insurance
3-9-2: License Fees
3-9-3: Transfer Of License
3-9-4: Public Address System Restricted
3-9-5: Penalty
3-9-1: LICENSE REQUIRED; INSURANCE:
   A.   License Required: No person should operate within the city limits any
motor vehicle used for the commercial purpose of selling ice cream, ice cream
products, or frozen novelties to the public intended for individual use and
immediate consumption without prior obtaining of a license from the city clerk
for such sales.
   B.   Proof Of Insurance: The city is authorized to approve for licensing any
vendor who pays the subsequently stated fee and provides the city clerk proof
of commercial liability insurance coverage in and on said vehicle sufficient to
meet state compulsory insurance requirements. (Ord. 3018, 6-20-1995)
3-9-2: LICENSE FEES:
The city is authorized to charge a fee for said license of five hundred dollars
($500.00) which shall be charged fully as initial application requirement
regardless of the percentage of licensing year which remains at the time of
application and one hundred dollars ($100.00) per year for each subsequent
year's renewal of said licenses thereafter which shall be due July 1 as in
accordance with subsection
3-1-1C of this title. (Ord. 3018, 6-20-1995)
3-9-3: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
Any person who has paid the initial fee of five hundred dollars ($500.00) may
sell his business, including the transfer of said license, and the continuity
of his license shall continue to the new owner and any subsequent owners;
therefore, relieving them from the duty of paying the initial application fee.
(Ord. 3018, 6-20-1995)
3-9-4: PUBLIC ADDRESS SYSTEM RESTRICTED:
   A.   Time For Operating System: Any person operating for commercial purposes
a vehicle used for the sale of ice cream, ice cream products, or frozen
novelties intended for individual use and immediate consumption may not utilize
or operate any public address system to facilitate the sale of their products
in city limits after sunset except during local league sponsored sporting
events at which such broadcasting may continue until the official end of such
sporting contest.
   B.   Noise Level: Any such public address system used must be in working
order and may not be played in city limits at an audible level above ninety
five (95) decibels.
   C.   Playing Music: In addition, no such public address system may play any
music or song repetitively in the same five hundred (500) square foot area for
more than one hour without changing said music or song so as not to constitute
a nuisance. (Ord. 3018, 6-20-1995)
3-9-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 10
TAXICABS
SECTION:
3-10-1: Definitions
3-10-2: Licenses Required
3-10-3: Fees
3-10-4: Insurance
3-10-5: Drivers; Requirements And Restrictions
3-10-6: Vehicles
3-10-7: Passengers
3-10-8: Revocation Or Suspension Of Driver's License
3-10-9: Penalty
3-10-1: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
DRIVER'S LICENSE: A license that the driver shall be required to obtain before
operating any vehicle for the transportation of passengers for hire.
MOTOR BUS: Shall mean and include any vehicle used to carry passengers for hire
but operating on a fixed route.
OPERATOR'S LICENSE: A license that the owner of the vehicle shall be required
to obtain before utilizing any vehicle for the transportation of passengers for
hire, provided, if the operator (owner) and driver is one and the same person,
only the operator's license shall be required, provided no other person is
permitted to drive the same vehicle at any time.
TAXICAB: All motor vehicles operated for the transportation of passengers for
hire but not operating on a fixed route. (1986 Code § 21-7)
3-10-2: LICENSES REQUIRED:
   A.   Operators:
      1.   Requirement: It shall be unlawful to engage in the business of
operating or driving a taxicab or motor bus within the city without first
having secured an operator's or driver's license. Applications for such
licenses shall be made to the city clerk by any applicant requesting same.
(1986 Code § 21-6)
      2.   Character Of Applicant: No such license shall be issued to or held
by any driver or owner who is not a person of good character, nor shall such
license be issued to or held by any corporation if any officer thereof would be
ineligible for a license under this chapter. (1986 Code § 21-8)
   B.   Individual Driver's License From City:
      1.   Requirement: No person shall drive a taxicab or motor bus unless and
until he has secured a driver's license therefor from the city clerk. Any owner
or operator of a taxicab or motor bus who permits or allows an unlicensed
driver to drive his taxicabs or motor buses shall, after notice and hearing,
have his license to operate revoked by the city council. (1986 Code § 21-16)
      2.   Qualifications Of Drivers: No such driver's license shall be issued
to any person who is not competent to operate a motor vehicle or who is not
familiar with traffic laws and ordinances of the city. Nor shall such driver's
license be issued to any person who does not have a valid license for the state
of Oklahoma. (1986 Code § 21-18)
3-10-3: FEES:
   A.   Operators:
      1.   The annual fee, payable in advance, for an operator's license shall
be fifty dollars ($50.00) per taxicab and one hundred dollars ($100.00) per
motor bus.
      2.   Every license shall expire on April 30 following the effective date
from which same is issued. No rebates or refunds shall be made.
      3.   Any license fee shall be in addition to any fee required by the
state of Oklahoma.
      4.   Whenever the number of cabs so operated shall be increased during
the license year, the licensee shall notify the city clerk of such change and
shall pay the additional fee.
      5.   The city clerk shall issue a receipt for said fee and assign to said
operator a number or numbers for each taxicab or motor bus to be covered by
said license. Said number may a transferred to any other vehicle put into
operation to replace one that has been withdrawn from service. (1986 Code § 21-
9)
   B.   Vehicles: The annual fee for a taxicab or motor bus driver's license
shall be twenty five dollars ($25.00). (1986 Code § 21-17; amd. 2005 Code)
3-10-4: INSURANCE:
   A.   Insurance Amounts: No taxicab or motor bus shall be operated unless the
taxicab/motor bus is covered by a bond or a public liability insurance policy
of at least fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) for injury or death of any one
person and one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for any number of persons
in any one accident, and with a coverage of at least twenty thousand dollars
($20,000.00) for property damage in any one accident. (1986 Code § 21-12; amd.
2005 Code)
   B.   Certificate Of Insurance: Prior to the issuance of any license for the
operation of any such vehicle, the owner thereof shall furnish to the city
clerk a certificate of insurance reflecting the coverage herein required.
   C.   Insurance Carrier Notify City Of Cancellation: Prior to the issuance of
a permit to operate any taxicab or motor bus, the insurance carrier shall be
required to agree that it will notify the city clerk within thirty (30) days of
the cancellation of such insurance for any reason, and it shall be the
responsibility of the owner to secure such agreement. (1986 Code § 21-12)
3-10-5: DRIVERS; REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS 1 :
   A.   State License Required: No person shall drive a taxicab or motor bus or
be hired or permitted to do so, unless he is duly licensed by the state as a
chauffeur. (1986 Code § 21-11)
   B.   Prohibited Acts: It shall be unlawful for any driver of a taxicab while
on duty to drink any intoxicating liquor or low point beer, or to use any
profane or obscene language, to shout or call to prospective passengers, or to
disturb the peace in any way, or to solicit employment by repeatedly or
persistently driving his vehicle to and fro in a short space or by otherwise
interfering with the proper and orderly access to or egress from any theater,
hall, hotel, public resort, bus station, department store, or other public
gathering, or in any other manner to obstruct or impede traffic, either by such
driving or parking. (1986 Code § 21-11; amd. 2005 Code)
   C.   Traffic Rules: It shall be the duty of every driver of a taxicab or
motor bus to obey all traffic rules and ordinances of the city and of the state
of Oklahoma. (1986 Code § 21-13)
   D.   Unlawful Use Of Vehicle: It shall be unlawful to knowingly permit any
taxicab or motor bus to be used in the perpetration of a crime or misdemeanor,
or for any immoral purpose. (1986 Code § 21-14)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsections
  6-4-11E and F of this code for use of bus and taxicab stands.
3-10-6: VEHICLES:
   A.   License And Equipment Required; Inspection:
      1.   No taxicab or motor bus shall be operated unless it bears a state
license duly issued; and no such vehicle shall be operated unless it is
equipped with proper brakes, lights, tires, horn, muffler, rear vision mirror
and windshield wiper in good condition.
      2.   It shall be the duty of the police department to furnish an annual
inspection to ascertain and determine that every taxicab or motor bus meets the
requirements of this subsection and to certify the same.
   B.   Serial Number Issued By City: Each taxicab or motor bus, while
operated, shall contain a serial body number assigned to each taxicab or motor
bus by the city clerk, which serial number shall be painted on each side and on
the rear exterior of the vehicle. No other number shall be painted on such
vehicle; provided however, the telephone number of the company or owner may be
painted thereon. (1986 Code § 21-10)
3-10-7: PASSENGERS:
   A.   Acceptance Of Passengers: It shall be the duty of the driver of any
taxicab or motor bus to accept as a passenger any person who seeks to so use
such vehicle, provided such person is not intoxicated and conducts himself in
an orderly manner. No person shall be admitted to a taxicab occupied by a
passenger without the consent of the passenger.
   B.   Taking Most Direct Route: The driver of any such taxicab shall take his
passenger to his destination by the most direct route available from the place
where the passenger enters the cab.
   C.   Payment Of Fare: It shall be unlawful for a passenger to fail or refuse
to pay the lawful fare at the termination of a trip. (1986 Code § 21-15)
3-10-8: REVOCATION OR SUSPENSION OF DRIVER'S LICENSE:
   A.   Council Authority: The city council may revoke or suspend any taxicab
or motor bus driver's license for repeated violations of traffic laws or
ordinances, or of any ordinance provision regulating the conduct of such
driver, or for any violation of any provision of this chapter upon ten (10)
days' notice of the proposed action to be taken at a city council meeting;
provided, that the licensee or its representative may appear at such city
council meeting, with or without legal counsel, to object to such license
revocation. (1986 Code § 21-19; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Reasons For Revocation Or Suspension:
      1.   A driver's license shall be revoked by the city council for any of
the following reasons:
         a.   Upon conviction for violation of any federal or state law, except
major traffic violations. (1986 Code § 21-20)
         b.   For operating a taxicab or motor bus while drunk or under the
influence of intoxicating liquor or low point beer. (1986 Code § 21-20; amd.
2005 Code)
         c.   For leaving the scene of an accident.
         d.   For failure to make full report of an accident to the police
department.
         e.   For permitting any other person to use his license or
certificate.
         f.   For erasing or obliterating any official entry on his license or
identification certificate.
         g.   Upon conviction of a third major traffic violation during any one
license year. A "major traffic violation" is hereby defined to be:
            (1)   Speeding.
            (2)   Reckless driving.
            (3)   Nonobservance of lights or signs.
            (4)   Improper brakes.
            (5)   Making a left or U-turn where not permitted.
            (6)   Driving on wrong side of the street.
      2.   A driver's license may be suspended by the city council for a period
of not to exceed ninety (90) days for any of the following reasons:
         a.   First and second offenses of a major traffic violation.
         b.   Repeated infractions of minor traffic rules.
      3.   The provisions of this section are supplementary and in addition to
other penalties and fines provided by other sections of this chapter. (1986
Code § 21-20)
3-10-9: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating or aiding, abetting or assisting in
the violation of any provision of this chapter is guilty of a separate offense
for each provision violated, and upon conviction, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-9-13 of this code for each offense. Wherever any violation is capable of
being continuing in nature, each day's continuation thereof shall constitute a
separate offense. (1986 Code § 21-21; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 11
AMBULANCE SERVICES
SECTION:
3-11-1: Definitions
3-11-2: License Review Board
3-11-3: License Required; Application
3-11-4: License Issuance; Fee
3-11-5: License Nontransferable
3-11-6: Inspection Of Ambulances, Equipment
3-11-7: Revocation Of License
3-11-8: Penalty
3-11-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
respectively ascribed to them in this section:
AMBULANCE: Any vehicle operated for hire, the purpose of which is to transport
individuals to or from hospitals or medical facilities, or between hospitals or
medical facilities for the purpose of receiving medical care, or from any
hospital or medical facility after receiving medical care.
AMBULANCE SERVICE: Any individual, association, firm or corporation operating
an ambulance or ambulances as defined herein within the city. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-
1995)
3-11-2: LICENSE REVIEW BOARD:
   A.   Authority: The ambulance committee is hereby authorized to function as
a license review board to review and pass upon the qualification of any
applicant for a license to operate an ambulance service.
   B.   Duties: The license review board shall issue licenses to applicants
qualified under this chapter, hear complaints and determine revocations of
licenses in proper cases.
   C.   Application Waiting Time; Waiver:
      1.   No license shall be issued by the board until the application shall
have been on file with the city clerk at least ten (10) days.
      2.   Any ambulance service already operating and located within the city
limits shall be exempt from the ten (10) day waiting period for license
issuance, and may continue to operate until said license is issued or
application is denied. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995)
3-11-3: LICENSE REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
   A.   Requirement: No association, person, firm or corporation shall maintain
or operate an ambulance service business or operate an ambulance within the
city without having first made application for a license to the city clerk, and
without having received a license from the city after approval thereof by the
license review board. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Qualifications Of Applicant: No association, firm or corporation shall
receive a license for the operation of an ambulance service business or an
ambulance within the city without possessing, at the time application is made
for the license, paramedic life support licensure status through the state of
Oklahoma and without meeting, at the time application is made for the license,
the following additional minimum qualifications: (Ord. 3360, 5-31-2007)
      1.   Ambulance Requirements: An applicant for a license shall own or be
in full possession under a lease purchase arrangement of a minimum of two (2)
ambulances available for service within the city. All ambulances and related
equipment contained therein shall be in proper and satisfactory operating
condition suitable for emergency use, and all ambulances shall meet all federal
and state standards as to space requirements, accessories, equipment and
supplies required to be contained within the ambulances.
      2.   Place Of Business: An applicant shall have secured and have
available a place of business where the ambulances may be kept and maintained,
the location to be within the city limits and in conformity with the zoning
ordinances of the city for the establishment and operation of an ambulance
business. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
      3.   Qualified Employees: An applicant shall have employed at the time
application is made or submit evidence of being able to employ prior to the
time the license is granted a sufficient number of trained personnel to handle
sick or injured persons in a proper and reasonable manner when rendering
services to the person. Pursuant to Oklahoma administrative code section 310:
641-3-15, each ground ambulance service shall have on staff an adequate number
of emergency medical personnel and a sufficient number of ambulances available
in order to be en route to ninety percent (90%) of all emergency calls within
five (5) minutes of the time the call is received in dispatch at the highest
level of care for which the service is licensed. The request for emergency
medical services shall be considered "received in dispatch" as soon as
sufficient information has been received to allow appropriate response, i.e.,
location of the emergency and nature of the call. Under no circumstance during
the transport of an ambulance patient shall the attendant be less than a
licensed paramedic; in addition to the requirement of licensed paramedics, each
ground ambulance service shall have drivers who, at a minimum, are certified as
a first responder, subject to any exceptions provided by Oklahoma
administrative code section 310:641-3-15. All drivers of a ground ambulance
service shall successfully complete an emergency vehicle operator course
approved by the state department of health within one hundred twenty (120) days
of employment. Emergency vehicle operators shall successfully complete a
refresher course approved by the state department of health every two (2)
years. (Ord. 3360, 5-31-2007)
      4.   Full Time Service: An applicant shall submit evidence that in
connection with the number of personnel employed or subject to employment by
the applicant, the applicant has sufficient number of personnel to maintain the
ambulance service business twenty four (24) hours per day, seven (7) days a
week.
      5.   Response To Emergency Calls: The applicant shall agree that in
consideration of a license being issued by the city, the applicant shall make a
response to each and every call received in all emergency cases, except when
all available ambulances and equipment are in previous use, in which case the
applicant would immediately advise the police department of the city. (Ord.
3020, 6-30-1995)
      6.   Insurance: The applicant shall furnish satisfactory evidence at the
time application is made that the applicant has in force or prior to the
issuance of the license, can obtain liability insurance covering all vehicles
and the operation of the ambulance business in an amount not less than twenty
five thousand dollars ($25,000.00) for property damage; one hundred twenty five
thousand dollars ($125,000.00) per individual liability for personal damage or
death, and one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for any number of claims arising
out of a single occurrence or accident. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
      7.   Schedule Of Rates Provided To City: The applicant shall furnish with
the application a printed rate schedule of all rates and charges which shall be
imposed by the applicant upon all individuals using the ambulance service and,
if a license is issued and any subsequent change is made in the charges, to
immediately notify and furnish to the city clerk a revised schedule of the
existing rates and charges to be imposed upon anyone using the ambulance
service.
   C.   Felony Conviction: No license shall be issued to any applicant who has
been convicted of a felony or any crime involving moral turpitude.
   D.   Names Of Owners: If the applicant for a license is an association, firm
or corporation or any other entity composed of more than one person other than
the applicant, the applicant shall furnish the name, address and occupation of
each and every person owning any interest in the association, firm or
corporation.
   E.   Compliance With State Standards: Any requirement which is subsequently
found to be less than a state minimum standard is void to the extent that it is
below the state's requirements.
   F.   Licensing Exceptions: No such license shall be required for any person
operating an ambulance or other vehicle who:
      1.   Renders assistance during any catastrophe or major emergency when
the ambulances authorized to operate in the city by certificate are
insufficient by number or for any other reason inadequate; or
      2.   Operates from a location outside the city and transports any patient
from a point of origin outside the city to a destination inside the city; or
      3.   Operates from a location outside the city and transports any patient
from a point of origin within the city to a destination outside the city; or
      4.   Municipal service agencies including police and fire rescue units;
or
      5.   Private companies operating an ambulance solely for the
transportation of their employees for illness or injury sustained while
performing their work. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995)
3-11-4: LICENSE ISSUANCE; FEE:
   A.   Issuance; Fee: Upon complying with all the requirements set forth in
this chapter, the license review board shall authorize the city clerk to issue
a license to the applicant to operate an ambulance service business within the
city upon payment of the prescribed license fee of one hundred dollars
($100.00) per ambulance per year. (Ord. 3360, 5-31-2007)
   B.   License Term; Conditions: All licenses issued pursuant to this chapter
shall expire on June 30 of each year. License fees shall be prorated on a
monthly basis based upon the date of the issuance of the license. No license
fee shall be returned or transferred from person to person, and all licenses
issued shall bear the signature of the city clerk with the proper corporate
seal of the city affixed thereto. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995)
3-11-5: LICENSE NONTRANSFERABLE:
No license issued to any applicant pursuant to the terms of this chapter shall
be transferred to any other person, firm, association or corporation. Any
attempted assignment of the license shall be void as to the city. (Ord. 3020,
6-30-1995)
3-11-6: INSPECTION OF AMBULANCES, EQUIPMENT:
The license review board shall have the right at any time to direct the
inspection of all ambulances and related equipment by any designated
responsible individual which are owned or operated by the holder of a license
under the terms of this chapter. These inspections shall be made at reasonable
times and are to be for the purpose of determining that the ambulance equipment
being operated by the licensee complies with the requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995)
3-11-7: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
In addition to any other penalty provided herein, any violation of the terms of
this chapter or failure to maintain the minimum requirements set forth in this
chapter for the operation of an ambulance services business or ambulances,
shall, under the terms of this chapter, be immediate grounds for revocation by
the license review board of any license issued hereunder after due notice to
the licensee affected and a public hearing by the license review board. (Ord.
3020, 6-30-1995)
3-11-8: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any provisions of this
chapter by doing any act prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or
declared to be an offense or misdemeanor thereby, or who shall fail to do any
act required by any such provision, or shall fail to do any act when such
provision declares such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or
misdemeanor, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor; and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which any such violation continues shall
constitute a separate misdemeanor. (Ord. 3020, 6-30-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 12
GAMBLING DEVICES
SECTION:
3-12-1: Operation Of Gambling Devices
3-12-2: Definition
3-12-3: Annual Fee
3-12-4: Decals
3-12-1: OPERATION OF GAMBLING DEVICES:
Every person or entity who owns and has available to any of the public for
operation, or who permits to be operated in or on his place of business,
gambling devices shall pay for such privilege an annual fee. A fee shall be
required for each device. (Ord. 3218, 8-5-2003)
3-12-2: DEFINITION:
A "gambling device" is a contrivance designed primarily for gambling purposes
which for a consideration affords the player an opportunity to obtain something
of value, the award of which is determined by chance, or any token, chip,
paper, receipt or other document which evidences, purports to evidence or is
designed to evidence participation in a lottery or the making of a bet. The
fact that the prize is not automatically paid by the device does not affect its
character as a gambling device. (Ord. 3218, 8-5-2003)
3-12-3: ANNUAL FEE:
There is hereby imposed an annual fee of two hundred dollars ($200.00) on each
gambling device located in the city. (Ord. 3281, 8-2-2005)
3-12-4: DECALS:
Each gambling device shall be required to have affixed and displayed a decal
provided by the city evidencing payment of the fee. Decals shall not be
transferred from one gambling device to another. (Ord. 3218, 8-5-2003)
CHAPTER 13
MEDICAL MARIJUANA
SECTION:
3-13-1: Definitions
3-13-2: General Requirements
3-13-3: Medical Marijuana Dispensary
3-13-4: Commercial Medical Marijuana Growing And/Or Processing Facilities
3-13-5: Medical Marijuana Wholesale And/Or Storage Facilities
3-13-6: Medical Marijuana Growing For Personal Use
3-13-7: Penalty
3-13-1: DEFINITIONS:
COMMERCIAL MEDICAL MARIJUANA GROWING AND/OR PROCESSING FACILITIES: Any medical
marijuana growing or processing facility licensed by the State of Oklahoma to
grow or process medical marijuana in excess of twelve (12) plants. Growing
includes the cultivation, manufacturing, processing, packaging, and
distribution of marijuana and marijuana products. Processing includes but is
not limited to: drying, cleaning, curing, packaging, and extraction of active
ingredients to create medical marijuana, medical marijuana products or
concentrates.
MEDICAL MARIJUANA DISPENSARY: Any retail medical marijuana establishment
licensed by the State of Oklahoma and the City of Vinita to sell or dispense
medical marijuana or medical marijuana products.
MEDICAL MARIJUANA GROWING FOR PERSONAL USE: Any individual licensed by the
State of Oklahoma and the City of Vinita to grow up to twelve (12) plants
within a single residence for personal medical use.
MEDICAL MARIJUANA WHOLESALE AND/OR STORAGE FACILITY: Any wholesale or storage
establishment licensed by the State of Oklahoma and the City of Vinita that
acquires, possesses, stores, delivers, transfers, transports, supplies, sells
or dispenses marijuana or related supplies and educational materials to the
holder of a valid medical marijuana dispensary license.
The City hereby adopts all other terms and definitions as established by State
law or Department of Health regulations. In the event of a conflict between any
definitions contained herein, the definition promulgated by the State or the
Department of Health shall prevail. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-2: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   State Issued Medical Marijuana License Required: Applicants for any
license contained herein shall be required to possess a valid State of Oklahoma
issued medical marijuana license prior to making application for the City
license.
   B.   Property Inspection Prior To Issuance: The license outlined in this
chapter will be subject to property inspection by an authorized City inspector
prior to issuance to insure compliance with all codes of the City.
   C.   Scheduled Property Inspection: The property inspection will occur at a
time scheduled and approved by both the applicant and the City inspector.
   D.   Applicant Presence Required: The applicant will be required to be
present during the inspection.
   E.   Code Compliance: All structures, equipment and apparatuses shall comply
with all Building and Fire Codes adopted by the State of Oklahoma and the City
of Vinita.
   F.   Application Due Before Inspection: A Medical Marijuana Business License
Application shall be filled out and signed by the property and business owner
and submitted to the City Clerk prior to scheduling an inspection.
   G.   License Fee: A nonrefundable license fee, as established in this
chapter, shall be paid at the time the application is submitted.
   H.   License Fee Amount: The license fee shall be set according to and used
to offset Municipal expenses covering costs related to licensing, inspection,
administration and enforcement of this chapter.
   I.   Distance Requirements: For the distance requirements outlined in this
chapter, the distances described shall be computed by direct measurement in a
straight line from the nearest property line of the parcel of land on which the
use described in herein is located to the nearest property line of the building
or unit in which the proposed retail marijuana establishment would be located.
   J.   Enclosed And Secure Structures: All medical marijuana dispensary,
commercial medical marijuana growing and/or processing facilities, and medical
marijuana wholesale and/or storage facility establishments shall be located
within an entirely enclosed and secure structure, as required by the rules and
regulations of the Department of Health, as may be amended from time to time.
   K.   Remitting Sales Taxes: License holder shall remit all required State
and City Sales Taxes.
   L.   Intent: It is the intent of the City of Vinita that nothing in this
chapter be construed to:
      1.   Allow persons to engage in conduct that endangers the health,
safety, or welfare of the citizens of the City of Vinita, or causes a public
nuisance;
      2.   Allow the use of marijuana for non-medical purposes; or
      3.   Allow any activity that is otherwise illegal and not permitted by
State law.
   M.   Additional Regulations:
      1.   The smell of noxious odor emitted from smoking or consumption of
medical marijuana by a person possessing a valid State issued medical marijuana
license shall constitute a public nuisance.
      2.   Smoking and vaping marijuana shall be prohibited on all City
property including vehicles, buildings, parks or other facilities.
      3.   Revocation or suspension of Municipal issued marijuana license;
hearing.
         a.   The Mayor or designee shall revoke or suspend a license issued
under this section on any of the following grounds:
            (1)   The license was procured by fraudulent conduct or false
statement of a material fact or a fact concerning the applicant was not
disclosed at the time of his application, and such fact would have constituted
just cause for refusal to issue the license;
            (2)   Violation of City ordinance, State law, or Department of
Health regulations governing medical marijuana.
         b.   Prior to suspension or revocation the permittee shall be given
notice of the proposed action to be taken and shall have an opportunity to be
heard before the Mayor, or his designee. If an employee has been designated by
the Mayor, or his designee, such employee shall make a report to the Mayor, or
his designee, together with a recommendation as to whether the license should
be suspended or revoked.
      4.   Any person or entity applying for or issued a license by the City of
Vinita shall comply with all State law and Department of Health rules and
regulations, as may be amended from time to time.
      5.   Revocation of the State issued license shall result in immediate
revocation of the City issued license. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-3: MEDICAL MARIJUANA DISPENSARY:
Medical marijuana dispensaries are hereby allowed within the Municipal
boundaries of Vinita, Oklahoma upon compliance with section
3-13-2 of this chapter, issuance of a retail medical marijuana dispensary
business license and the following additional provisions.
   A.   Districts Allowed: A medical marijuana dispensary shall only be located
within one of the following zoning districts.
      1.   C-1 Convenience Commercial District, upon approval of the Board of
Adjustments;
      2.   C-2 Highway Commercial and Commercial Recreation District; or
      3.   C-3 General Commercial District.
   B.   Location Restriction: Medical marijuana dispensary business license
shall not be granted to any applicant where the proposed location would be
located within one thousand feet (1,000') of any public or private school.
   C.   Conditions Of Operation:
      1.   Buildings where medical marijuana is stored or dispensed must be
equipped with ventilation/air filtration systems so that no odors are
detectable off premises.
      2.   The retail establishment must maintain a valid Sales Tax permit
issued by the State of Oklahoma.
      3.   No on premises use of marijuana or its derivatives shall be allowed.
      4.   Any violations of this section will result in the revocation of the
retail medical marijuana business license.
   D.   License Fees: There shall be a business license fee in the amount of
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) and an annual renewal fee in the amount
of seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). The annual business license will
expire on June 30th and shall be renewed prior to July 1st each year. Failure
to renew will result in a penalty fee of fifty percent (50%) of the annual fee
and shall require re-inspection as required by subsection
3-13-2B of this chapter. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-4: COMMERCIAL MEDICAL MARIJUANA GROWING AND/OR PROCESSING FACILITIES:
Commercial medical marijuana growing and/or processing facilities are hereby
allowed within the Municipal boundaries of Vinita, Oklahoma upon compliance
with section
3-13-2 of this chapter, issuance of a commercial medical marijuana growing and/
or facility license and the following additional provisions.
   A.   Districts Allowed: Commercial medical marijuana growing and/or
processing facility shall only be located within one of the following zoning
districts.
      1.   A-1 Agricultural District;
      2.   I-1 Light Industrial District; or
      3.   I-2 Heavy Industrial District.
   B.   Conditions Of Operation:
      1.   The facility shall be secure with limited access. The secure area
must be locked at all times. A key or access code shall be provided to all
emergency services (fire, police and EMS). Changing the code or key shall not
be allowed without proper notification to all emergency services.
      2.   The establishment must maintain a valid Sales Tax permit issued by
the State of Oklahoma.
      3.   The facility must be constructed in such a manner that the growing
of medical marijuana plants cannot be seen by the public from the public right-
of-way.
      4.   The growing area including any lighting, plumbing or electrical
components used shall comply with all Building and Fire Codes adopted by the
State of Oklahoma and the City of Vinita.
      5.   The growing area must be properly ventilated so as not to create
humidity, mold or other related problems.
      6.   Growing medical marijuana shall not be conducted in a manner that
constitutes a public nuisance. A public nuisance may be deemed to exist if
growing marijuana produces light, glare, heat, noise, odor or vibration that is
detrimental to public health, safety or welfare or interferes with the
reasonable enjoyment of life and property.
   C.   License Fees: There shall be a business license fee in the amount of
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) and an annual renewal fee in the amount
of seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). The annual business license will
expire on June 30th and shall be renewed prior to July 1st of each year.
Failure to renew will result in a penalty of fifty percent (50%) of the annual
fee and shall require re-inspection as required by subsection
3-13-2B of this chapter. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-5: MEDICAL MARIJUANA WHOLESALE AND/OR STORAGE FACILITIES:
Medical marijuana wholesale and/or storage facilities are hereby allowed within
the Municipal boundaries of Vinita, Oklahoma upon compliance with section
3-13-2 of this chapter, issuance of a medical marijuana wholesale and/or
storage facility license and the following additional requirements.
   A.   Districts Allowed: Medical marijuana wholesale or storage facility
shall only be located within one of the following zoning districts.
      1.   A-1 Agricultural District;
      2.   I-1 Light Industrial District; or
      3.   I-2 Heavy Industrial District.
   B.   Conditions Of Operation:
      1.   The facility shall be secure with limited access. The secure area
must be locked at all times. A key or access code shall be provided to all
emergency services (fire, police and EMS). Changing the code or key shall not
be allowed without proper notification to all emergency services.
      2.   Buildings where medical marijuana is stored or dispensed must be
equipped with ventilation/air filtration systems so that no odors are
detectable off premises.
      3.   The retail establishment must maintain a valid Sales Tax permit
issued by the State of Oklahoma.
   C.   License Fees: There shall be a business license fee in the amount of
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) and an annual renewal fee in the amount
of seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). The annual business license will
expire on June 30th and shall be renewed prior to July 1st of each year.
Failure to renew will result in a penalty of fifty percent (50%) of the annual
fee and shall require re-inspection as required by subsection
3-13-2B of this chapter. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-6: MEDICAL MARIJUANA GROWING FOR PERSONAL USE:
Medical marijuana growing for personal use is hereby allowed within the
Municipal boundaries of Vinita, Oklahoma upon compliance with section
3-13-2 of this chapter, issuance of a medical marijuana growing for personal
medical use license and the following additional provisions.
   A.   Any license issued to an individual for the growing of medical
marijuana for personal use will be for the growing of medical marijuana at the
individual's primary residence. The City Clerk shall be notified immediately
upon any change of address of the licensee.
   B.   Any access or entry point to residential facilities used for medical
marijuana cultivation for personal medical use must be secured by lock and key
or equivalent, at all times except when the residential facility is actively
being supervised in person by the permit holder.
   C.   Growing medical marijuana shall not be visible from the public right-
of-way.
   D.   The growing area including any lighting, plumbing or electrical
components used shall comply with Municipal Building and Fire Codes. The
growing area must be properly ventilated so as not to create humidity, mold or
other related problems. Lighting shall not exceed one thousand watts (1,000 W)
per light. The use of gas products (CO2, butane, etc.) or CO2 and ozone
generators in the growing area is prohibited.
   E.   Growing medical marijuana shall not be conducted in a manner that
constitutes a public nuisance. A public nuisance may be deemed to exist if
growing marijuana produces light, glare, heat, noise, odor or vibration that is
detrimental to public health, safety or welfare or interferes with the
reasonable enjoyment of life and property.
   F.   The primary use of the residential property in which medical marijuana
is grown shall remain at all times a residence, with legal and functioning
cooking, eating, sleeping and sanitation/bathing facilities with proper ingress
and egress. No room shall be used for growing marijuana where such cultivation
will impair or prevent the primary uses of cooking, eating, sleeping or
sanitation/bathing.
   G.   If the residence is rented, consent of the property owner shall be
obtained prior to any cultivation commencing. This consent must be evidenced by
a signed and notarized statement from the property owner permitting the growth
of marijuana in a residence.
   H.   Any individual licensed to grow marijuana for personal use shall have a
license issued by the State of Oklahoma authorizing the use of medical
marijuana. Said license shall be made available to any authorized City employee
upon request.
   I.   There shall be a license fee in the amount of fifty dollars ($50.00)
and an annual renewal fee in the amount of fifty dollars ($50.00). The annual
license will expire on June 30th and shall be renewed prior to July 1st each
year. Failure to renew will result in a penalty fee of fifty percent (50%) of
the annual fee and shall require re-inspection as required by subsection
3-13-2B of this chapter. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
3-13-7: PENALTY:
In addition to license revocation or suspension, a violation of any of the
provisions contained in this chapter shall also be deemed an offense and
punishable, as provided in this Code. (Ord. 3684, 3-19-2019)
TITLE 4
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
EMERGENCY TELEPHONE SERVICE (911)
SECTION:
4-1-1: Definition
4-1-2: Operation And Fee Authorized
4-1-3: Fee Imposed
4-1-4: Prank Calls To 911
4-1-1: DEFINITION:
Pursuant to 63 Oklahoma Statutes section 2813, "emergency telephone service"
means any telephone system utilizing a three (3) digit number 911, for
reporting an emergency to the appropriate public agency providing law
enforcement, fire, medical or other emergency services, including ancillary
communications systems and personnel necessary to pass the reported emergency
to the appropriate emergency service and personnel. (Ord. 2946, 3-3-1992, eff.
5-4-1992)
4-1-2: OPERATION AND FEE AUTHORIZED:
Pursuant to 63 Oklahoma Statutes section 2814, the city is authorized to
provide for the operation of an emergency telephone service and is further
authorized to impose an emergency telephone fee for such service in areas,
subject to the jurisdiction of the city, for which emergency telephone service
has been contracted. The city is further authorized to perform other acts as
are necessary for the protection and preservation of the public health if
necessary for the operation of the emergency telephone system. (Ord. 2946, 3-3-
1992, eff. 5-4-1992)
4-1-3: FEE IMPOSED:
Pursuant to 63 Oklahoma Statutes section 2814, the city is hereby authorized by
this chapter to impose such fee in an amount not to exceed five percent (5%)
during the first year of the fee and not to exceed three percent (3%) in any
year thereafter of the tariff rate in areas subject to the jurisdiction of the
city for which emergency telephone service has been contracted. (Ord. 2946, 3-
3-1992, eff. 5-4-1992)
4-1-4: PRANK CALLS TO 911:
It is unlawful for any person to call the number 911 for the purpose of making
a false alarm or complaint or reporting false information which could result in
the dispatch of emergency services from any public agency provider. Any person
violating the provisions of this section, upon conviction, shall be guilty of
an offense punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. (Ord. 3051, 12-3-1996; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL HEALTH AND SANITATION PROVISIONS
SECTION:
4-2-1: Obstructing Health Officer
4-2-2: Discarding Medicine On Street
4-2-3: Quarantine, Violations
4-2-4: Abandoned Iceboxes, Refrigerators
4-2-5: Penalty
4-2-1: OBSTRUCTING HEALTH OFFICER:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully obstruct or interfere with any
health officer or physician charged with the enforcement of the health laws of
the city, or the state of Oklahoma. (1986 Code § 11-8)
4-2-2: DISCARDING MEDICINE ON STREET:
It shall be unlawful for any person, company or corporation to throw, leave or
deposit, or cause to be thrown, left or deposited upon any street, avenue,
alley, sidewalk, or in any of the parks or other public places, or on any
private property within the city, any medicine of any kind or description
whatsoever. (1986 Code § 11-7)
4-2-3: QUARANTINE, VIOLATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully violate or refuse to comply
with any lawful order, direction, prohibition, rule or regulation, concerning
quarantine, of the board of health, or any officer charged with enforcement of
such order, direction, prohibition, rule or regulation. (1986 Code § 11-9; amd.
2005 Code)
4-2-4: ABANDONED ICEBOXES, REFRIGERATORS:
It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to leave in a place
accessible to children any abandoned or discarded icebox, refrigerator or other
container of a capacity of one and one-half (11/2) cubic feet or more which has
an airtight door with a lock or other fastening device which cannot be easily
released for opening from the inside of the icebox, refrigerator or container
without first removing the door, lock or fastener. (1986 Code § 11-10; amd.
2005 Code)
4-2-5: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provisions of this chapter is guilty of an offense,
and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. In addition thereto, such person may be enjoined from
continuing such violations. Each day upon which a violation continues
constitutes a separate violation. (1986 Code § 11-12; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 3
NUISANCES
SECTION:
4-3-1: Nuisances Defined; Prohibited
4-3-2: Persons Responsible
4-3-3: Time Does Not Legalize
4-3-4: Remedies
4-3-5: Power To Define And Summarily Abate Nuisances
4-3-6: Certain Public Nuisances Defined
4-3-7: Health Nuisances; Abatement
4-3-8: Drainage Ditches
4-3-9: Congregations And Littering
4-3-10: Political Advertising Signs
4-3-11: Summary Abatement Of Nuisances
4-3-12: Abatement By Suit In District Court
4-3-13: Procedure Cumulative
4-3-14: Penalty
4-3-1: NUISANCES DEFINED; PROHIBITED:
   A.   Nuisance: A "nuisance" is unlawfully doing an act, or omitting to
perform a duty, or is any thing or condition, which either:
      1.   Annoys, injures, or endangers the comfort, repose, health, or safety
of others;
      2.   Offends decency;
      3.   Unlawfully interferes with, obstructs, or tends to obstruct, or
renders dangerous for passage, any lake or navigable river, stream, canal, or
basin, or any public park, square, street, or other public property; or
      4.   In any way renders other persons insecure in life or in the use of
property.
   B.   Public Nuisance: A "public nuisance" is one which affects at the same
time an entire community or neighborhood or any considerable number of persons,
although the extent of the annoyance or damage inflicted upon the individuals
may be unequal.
   C.   Private Nuisance: Every nuisance not included in subsection B of this
section is a private nuisance. (1986 Code § 13-1)
   D.   Nuisance Unlawful: It is unlawful for any person (owner, lessee, or
other) to create or maintain a nuisance within the city, or to permit a
nuisance to remain on premises under his control within the city. (1986 Code §
13-10)
4-3-2: PERSONS RESPONSIBLE:
Every successive owner of property who neglects to abate a continuing nuisance
upon or in the use of such property, created by a former owner, is liable
therefor in the same manner as the one who first created it. (1986 Code § 13-2)
4-3-3: TIME DOES NOT LEGALIZE:
No lapse of time can legalize a public nuisance amounting to an actual
obstruction of public right. (1986 Code § 13-3)
4-3-4: REMEDIES:
   A.   Public Nuisance: The remedies against a public nuisance are:
      1.   Prosecution on complaint before the municipal court.
      2.   Prosecution on information or indictment before another appropriate
court.
      3.   Civil action.
      4.   Abatement:
         a.   By a person injured as provided in 50 Oklahoma Statutes section
12.
         b.   By the city in accordance with law or ordinance. (1986 Code § 13-
4)
   B.   Private Nuisance: The remedies against a private nuisance are:
      1.   Civil action.
      2.   Abatement:
         a.   By person injured as provided in 50 Oklahoma Statutes sections 14
and 15.
         b.   By the city in accordance with law or ordinance. (1986 Code § 13-
5)
4-3-5: POWER TO DEFINE AND SUMMARILY ABATE NUISANCES:
   A.   Determination: As provided in 50 Oklahoma Statutes section 16, the city
has power to determine what is and what shall constitute a nuisance within its
corporate limits and, for the protection of the public health, the public
parks, and the public water supply, outside of its corporate limits.
   B.   Abatement: Whenever it is practical to do so, the city has power
summarily to abate any such nuisance after notice to the owner and an
opportunity for him to be heard, if this can be done. (1986 Code § 13-6)
4-3-6: CERTAIN PUBLIC NUISANCES DEFINED:
   A.   Enumeration: In addition to other public nuisances declared by other
sections of this code or law, the following are hereby declared to be public
nuisances:
      1.   Unwholesome Food Or Drink: The sale, or offering for sale, of
unwholesome food or drink; or the keeping of a place where such sales or
offerings are made.
      2.   Intoxicating Liquor: The sale, offering for sale, or furnishing of
intoxicating liquor in violation of the state law or ordinances of the city; or
the keeping of a place where intoxicating liquor is sold, offered for sale, or
furnished in violation of the state law or ordinances of the city.
      3.   Obscene Books, Objects: The exposure, display, sale, or distribution
of obscene pictures, books, pamphlets, magazines, papers, documents, or
objects; or the keeping of a place where such are exposed, displayed, sold, or
distributed.
      4.   Gambling Places: The keeping of a place where persons gamble,
whether by cards, slot machines, punchboards, or otherwise.
      5.   Prostitution Places: The keeping of a place where prostitution,
illicit sexual intercourse, or other immoral acts are practiced.
      6.   Unlawful Places: The keeping of a place where activities in
violation of state law or ordinance are practiced or carried on.
      7.   Public Dances: The conduct or holding of public dances in violation
of the ordinances of the city, or the keeping of a place where such dances are
held.
      8.   Exposure Of Diseased Persons: The public exposure of a person having
a contagious disease.
      9.   Loud Noises: The continued making of loud or unusual noises which
annoy persons of ordinary sensibilities; or the keeping of an animal which
makes such noises.
      10.   Electrical Interference With Radio Reception: The operation or use
of any electrical apparatus or machine which materially or unduly interferes
with radio or television reception by others.
      11.   Crowds Obstructing Public Ways: Any use of a street or sidewalk or
a place adjacent thereto which causes crowds of people to gather so as to
obstruct traffic on such street or sidewalk, or which otherwise obstructs
traffic thereon, except as may be authorized by law or ordinances.
      12.   Water Or Ice Falling From Building: Permitting water or other
liquid to flow or fall, or ice or snow to fall, from any building or structure
upon any street or sidewalk.
      13.   Polluted Water; Mosquito Breeding: All wells, pools, cisterns,
bodies, or containers of water in which mosquitoes breed or are likely to
breed, or which are so constructed, formed, conditioned, or situated as to
endanger the public safety.
      14.   Weeds And Refuse: Rank weeds or grass, carcasses, accumulations of
manure, refuse, or other things, which are, or are likely to be, breeding
places for flies, mosquitoes, vermin, or disease germs; and the premises on
which such exist.
      15.   Dangerous Buildings:
         a.   Any building or structure which is dangerous to the public health
or safety because of damage, decay, or other conditions.
         b.   Every building or other structure that shall become unsafe and
dangerous from fire, decay or other cause, or shall become hazardous from fire,
by reason of age, decay or construction, location or other cause, or shall be
detrimental to the health, safety or welfare of the city or its inhabitants
from any cause.
      16.   Dangerous Pit Or Hole: Any pit, hole, or other thing which is so
constructed, formed, conditioned, or situated as to endanger the public safety.
      17.   Fire Hazards: Any fire or explosion hazard which endangers the
public safety.
      18.   Dangerous Occupations: Any occupation or activity which endangers
the public peace, health, morals, safety, or welfare.
      19.   Vehicle Storage In Residence District: Any motor vehicle (whether
in operating condition or not), or any trailer without a current vehicle plate
as required by law for vehicles used on the public highways, when stored or
kept in a residence district.
      20.   Stables; Noise And Sanitation: Any stable or other place where
animals are kept that may become obnoxious or annoying to any resident of the
city, by reason of any noise or noises made by the animal therein, or by reason
of lack of sanitation.
      21.   Dog Kennels; Noise: The keeping of any dog kennels within this city
for the breeding and raising of dogs that shall become offensive or annoying to
the public by reason of the barking and noise made by the animals therein
contained.
      22.   Cesspools; Privies:
         a.   Any vault, cesspool or sink used to receive human excrement,
slops, garbage, refuse, or other filthy substance.
         b.   Every privy or water closet which shall be in an overflowing,
leaking or filthy condition, or in a condition dangerous, injurious or annoying
to the comfort, health and welfare of any resident of the city.
      23.   Objectionable Deposits: Any pond, slop, trash, refuse, cobs,
manure, decayed or decaying vegetable matter, left, kept or maintained in such
condition as to endanger the public health.
      24.   Hog Pens: The keeping of any hog pen within the limits of this
city.
      25.   Hides Of Animals: Any green or unsalted hides of any animal kept in
any exposed or open place within the limits of the city.
      26.   Defective Ditches, Receptacles: Any unclean, foul, leaking or
broken or defective ditch, drain, gutter, slop, garbage or manure barrel, box
or other receptacle, in the city.
   B.   Cumulative Provisions: The above enumeration of certain public
nuisances shall be cumulative and not limit other provisions of law or
ordinances defining public or private nuisances either in more general or more
specific terms. (1986 Code §
4-3-7: HEALTH NUISANCES; ABATEMENT:
   A.   Order To Abate; Notice:
      1.   Pursuant to authority granted in accordance with 63 Oklahoma
Statutes section 1-1011, the health officer shall have authority to order the
owner or occupant of any private premises in the city to remove from such
premises, at his own expense, any source of filth, cause of sickness, condition
conducive to the breeding of insects or rodents that might contribute to the
transmission of disease, or any other condition adversely affecting the public
health, within twenty four (24) hours, or within such other time as may be
reasonable, and a failure to do so shall constitute an offense.
      2.   Such order shall be in writing and may be served personally on the
owner or occupant of the premises, or authorized agent thereof, by the health
officer or by a police officer, or a copy thereof may be left at the last usual
place of abode of the owner, occupant, or agent, if known and within the state.
If the premises are unoccupied and the residence of the owner, occupant, or
agent is unknown, or is without the state, the order may be served by posting a
copy thereof on the premises, or by publication in at least one issue of a
newspaper having a general circulation in the city.
   B.   Abatement By City; Costs Imposed: If the order is not complied with,
the health officer may cause the order to be executed and complied with, and
the cost thereof shall be certified to the city clerk, and the cost of removing
or abating such nuisance shall be added to the water bill or other city utility
bill of the owner or occupant if he is a user of water from the city water
system or such other utility service. The cost shall be treated as part of such
utility bill to which it is added, and shall become due and payable, and be
subject to the same regulations relating to delinquency in payment, as the
utility bill itself. If such owner or occupant is not a user of any city
utility service, such cost, after certification to the city clerk, may be
collected in any manner in which any other debt due the city may be collected.
(1986 Code § 13-21)
4-3-8: DRAINAGE DITCHES:
   A.   Impeding Drainage: Any culvert, driveway, pipe, or other obstacle upon
or in the dedicated streets, alleys or ways of the city which impedes the flow
of water through drainage ditches now constructed or which might hereafter be
constructed by the city for the purpose of proper drainage of water falling
from any rainfalls, which might reasonably be anticipated, shall be and are
hereby declared to a public nuisances endangering and interfering with travel
upon and the repair and maintenance of city streets and annoying, injuring and
endangering the comfort, repose, health and safety of the citizens of the city.
(1986 Code § 13-22)
   B.   Notice; Abatement By City: All public nuisances existing contrary to
the provisions of this section not abated by the owners or occupants of
adjoining premises or their agents within ten (10) days after they shall be
given notice as provided herein, shall be abated by the street commissioner or
other officer or employee of the city, designated by motion or resolution of
the city council and acting under the direction of the city council by digging
up, breaking, if necessary or not reasonably avoidable, and removing such
culvert, driveway, pipe, or other obstacle and opening up such drainage ditch,
and leaving the same open. (1986 Code § 13-23)
   C.   Notice In Writing; Delivery: The notice herein mentioned shall be in
writing directing the owner or occupant of premises adjoining such nuisance to
abate the same by removing such obstacle impeding drainage, and shall be given
by mailing to the owner or occupant of such adjoining premises at his or their
last known post office address, or to both, if their names and post office
addresses can be ascertained with reasonable diligence, by registered or
certified mail or by delivery of such notice to such owner or occupant
personally by any officer, employee or agent of the city or by posting such
notice at some conspicuous place upon such premises if the name or mailing
address of the owner or occupant of said premises cannot be ascertained with
reasonable diligence. (1986 Code § 13-24)
4-3-9: CONGREGATIONS AND LITTERING:
   A.   Congregation Of Persons: Any assembly or congregation of two (2) or
more persons loitering or spending their time idly after dark upon public or
private streets, alleys, driveways, parking lots or other property within
public view or hearing, where some member or members of such assembly,
congregation or group cannot be identified by the city police, or who are not
promptly identified to the city police, are engaged or contemporaneously have
engaged in disturbing the peace, offending public decency, using vile or
profane language, annoying, injuring or endangering the comfort, repose,
health, or safety of others or littering public or private property by
throwing, dropping, laying or leaving cans, bottles, wastepaper, trash or other
refuse upon such public or private property, is hereby declared to be a public
nuisance. (1986 Code § 13-25)
   B.   Abatement By Chief Of Police: When any such public nuisance is in
existence within the presence or personal knowledge of the chief of police or
any member of the police department of the city or upon written complaint of
the existence of such public nuisance, as herein defined, by any citizen of the
city, such chief of police or member of the police department of the city may
abate such nuisance by ordering all members of such assembly, congregation or
group to disperse and to cease and desist from loitering or spending their time
idly at any public place or place open to the public or within public view
within the limits of the city, and may order minors under the age of eighteen
(18) in such assembly, congregation or group to go to their respective homes or
places of abode. (1986 Code § 13-26; amd. 2005 Code)
   C.   Refusal To Comply: Any person who refuses to comply with or violates
any order of the chief of police or any member of the police department
pursuant to this section shall be guilty of an offense against the city, unless
at the time of the giving of such order by the chief of police or any member of
the police department, such person shows justifiable cause to remain
temporarily upon the streets or other public place within the city for some
limited time to accomplish some lawful and legitimate purpose. (1986 Code § 13-
27)
   D.   Littering: It is further declared to be unlawful for any person to
litter any public or private street, alley, driveway, parking lot, or other
property not his own, by throwing, dropping, laying or leaving bottles, cans,
wastepaper, trash, or other refuse in or upon such public or private property.
(1986 Code § 13-28)
4-3-10: POLITICAL ADVERTISING SIGNS:
   A.   Definition: A "political advertising sign" is defined as any sign,
poster or placard printed, painted, made or designed for the purpose of
furthering or advertising the candidacy of any person who is or intends to
become or may be a candidate for the election to any public office, whether
such public office be in the local, state or federal government, or any
subdivision thereof. (1986 Code § 13-29)
   B.   Prohibited On Streets And Easements: No person, firm or corporation
shall erect or display any political advertising sign on any street or alley
right of way, or upon any public utility easement within the city. (1986 Code §
13-30)
   C.   Prohibited On Telephone Poles: No person, firm or corporation shall
place, tack, nail, staple or glue any political advertising sign on any
