telephone, telegraph, electric or street lighting pole within the city. (1986
Code § 13-31)
   D.   Nuisance Declared: Any political advertising sign erected, placed or
displayed in violation of the provisions hereof shall be a public nuisance. No
property right shall exist in such sign erected, placed or displayed in
violation of the provisions hereof, and such sign may be removed and destroyed
by any person. (1986 Code § 13-32)
4-3-11: SUMMARY ABATEMENT OF NUISANCES:
   A.   Dangerous Conditions; Immediate Abatement: Some nuisances are of such
nature as to constitute a grave and immediate danger to the peace, health,
safety, morals, or welfare of one or more persons or of the public generally.
It is recognized that circumstances may be such as to justify, and even to
require, the mayor or other appropriate officer or agency of the city
government to take immediate and proper action summarily to abate such
nuisances, or to reduce or suspend the danger until more deliberate action can
be taken toward such abatement.
   B.   Statement Of Nuisance Submitted To Council: The chief of the fire
department, the chief of police, the city attorney, the building inspector, the
electrical inspector, the plumbing inspector, or any other officer subordinate
to the mayor, may submit, through or with the consent of the mayor, to the city
council, a statement as to the existence of a nuisance as defined by the
ordinances of the city or law, and a request or recommendation that it be
abated. The mayor himself, the health officer, any council member, or any
resident or residents of the city may submit such a statement and a request or
recommendation to the city council.
   C.   Council Determination; Notice Of Hearing:
      1.   The city council shall determine whether or not the alleged nuisance
is a nuisance in fact. For the purpose of gathering evidence on the subject,
the council shall have power to subpoena and examine witnesses, books, papers,
and other effects.
      2.   Before proceeding to abate the nuisance or have it abated, the
council shall give notice of a hearing on the proposed abatement to the owner
of any property concerned and to any other person alleged or deemed responsible
for or to be causing the nuisance, and an adequate opportunity to be heard, if
such notice and opportunity for a hearing can be given. Such notice to the
owner and other persons concerned shall be given in writing by mail or by
service by a police officer if their names and addresses are known; but, if the
names or addresses are not known, and the peace, health, safety, morals, or
welfare of the persons or public adversely affected would not be unduly
jeopardized by the necessary delay, a notice of the hearing shall be published
in a newspaper of general circulation within the city.
   D.   Order To Abate; City Abatement; Costs Imposed:
      1.   If the city council finds that a nuisance does in fact exist, it
shall direct the owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing the
nuisance to abate it within a specified time if the peace, health, safety,
morals, or welfare of the person or persons or public adversely affected would
not be unduly jeopardized by the consequent delay.
      2.   If such peace, health, safety, morals, or welfare would be unduly
jeopardized by the consequent delay, or if the owner or other persons
responsible for or causing the nuisance do not abate it within the specified
time, the council shall direct the mayor to abate the nuisance or to have it
abated, if summary abatement is practical, as authorized by 50 Oklahoma
Statutes section 16.
      3.   The city clerk shall send a statement of the cost of such summary
abatement to the owner and/or other persons responsible for or causing the
nuisance, as may be just under the circumstances, if their names and addresses
are known. Until paid, such cost shall constitute a debt to the city
collectible as other debts of the city may be collected. (1986 Code § 13-8)
4-3-12: ABATEMENT BY SUIT IN DISTRICT COURT:
In cases where it is deemed impractical summarily to abate a nuisance, the city
may bring suit in the district court of the county where the nuisance is
located, as provided in 50 Oklahoma Statutes section 17. (1986 Code § 13-9)
4-3-13: PROCEDURE CUMULATIVE:
The various procedures for abating nuisances prescribed by this chapter and by
other provisions of law and ordinance shall be cumulative one to the other, and
the city may elect to follow any such procedure which is applicable in abating
any particular nuisance. (1986 Code § 13-33)
4-3-14: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter, by doing any act
prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or who fails to do any act
required by any such provision, or who fails to do any act when such provision
declares such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor, or who
violates any legal order or regulation made pursuant to this chapter, or who
maintains any nuisance as defined in this chapter, is guilty of an offense and,
upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed
a separate offense. (1986 Code § 13-34; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 4
WEEDS; TRASH; DILAPIDATED BUILDINGS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Legislative Intent
4-4-2: Definitions
4-4-3: Property Maintenance By Owner Or Occupant
4-4-4: Report Nuisance Conditions To City; Hearing
4-4-5: Hearing By Council; Order Abatement
4-4-6: Abatement By City Or Contract; Cost
4-4-7: Failure To Pay Costs
4-4-8: Service Of Notice
4-4-9: Enforcement Of State Law; Administrative Duties
4-4-10: Penalty
4-4-1: LEGISLATIVE INTENT:
It is hereby declared the legislative intent of the city council to conform
hereby to the provisions of 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 22-111, and hereby to
repeal any and all ordinances of this city in conflict herewith. (1986 Code §
13-11)
4-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
CLEANING: The removal of trash from property.
OWNER: The owner of record as shown by the most current tax rolls of the county
treasurer.
TRASH: The word "trash" extends to the widest sense of that term, and includes,
but without limitation upon any other meaning, refuse, litter, ashes, leaves,
debris, paper, combustible materials, offal, rubbish, waste, and useless or
unused or uncared for matter of all kinds, whether solid or liquid in form.
WEED:
   A.   Includes, but is not limited to, poison ivy, poison oak, or poison
sumac and all vegetation at any state of maturity which:
      1. Exceeds twelve inches (12") in height, except healthy trees, shrubs,
or produce for human consumption grown in a tended and cultivated garden,
unless such trees and shrubbery by their density or location constitute a
detriment to the health, benefit and welfare of the public and community or a
hazard to traffic or create a fire hazard to the property or otherwise
interfere with the mowing of said weeds;
      2. Regardless of height, harbors, conceals, or invites deposits or
accumulation of refuse or trash;
      3. Harbors rodents or vermin;
      4. Gives off unpleasant or noxious odors;
      5. Constitutes a fire or traffic hazard; or
      6. Is dead or diseased.
   B.   The term "weed" shall not include tended crops on land zoned for
agricultural use which are planted more than one hundred fifty feet (150') from
a parcel zoned for other than agricultural use. (1986 Code § 13-20; amd. 2005
Code)
4-4-3: PROPERTY MAINTENANCE BY OWNER OR OCCUPANT:
   A.   Prohibited Condition: No person shall permit any lot, yard, parkway, or
sidewalk, or the space abutting thereon, to the center of the street or to the
center of the alley, owned, occupied or controlled by him or for which he is
agent, or over which he has charge for the owner, to become covered or
overgrown with weeds or other objectionable, obnoxious or injurious growth or
accumulation.
   B.   Nuisance Declared: Any lot, yard, sidewalk, parkway, or space abutting
thereon, to the center of the street or alley, which shall become overgrown and
covered with weeds or other objectionable or injurious growth or accumulations,
so as to become offensive to view or detrimental to the general health of the
city, is hereby deemed and declared to be a public nuisance. (Ord. 3016, 5-16-
1995)
4-4-4: REPORT NUISANCE CONDITIONS TO CITY; HEARING:
   A.   Report To Clerk: Any officer or employee of the city who discovers an
accumulation of trash or the growth of grass and weeds, or both these
conditions, upon any premises within the limits of the city by reason of which
such premises appear to him to be in any condition as listed below shall report
such condition to the city clerk:
      1.   Detrimental to the health, benefit, and welfare of the public and
the community;
      2.   A hazard to traffic;
      3.   A fire hazard to the danger of property; or
      4.   Any two (2) or more of such results in combination. (1986 Code § 13-
12)
   B.   Report Placed On Council Agenda: Upon receiving the report prescribed
by subsection A of this section, or upon receipt of equivalent information from
any reliable source, the mayor shall place upon the agenda of the city council
for hearing and consideration at an appropriate date of meeting thereof, such
as will permit giving the notices prescribed by statutory law, the question
whether such premises, by reason of the conditions specified, are detrimental
to the health, benefit, and welfare of the public and community, or a hazard to
traffic, or a fire hazard to the danger of property, or any two (2) or more of
such results in combination. (1986 Code § 13-13)
   C.   Hearing Notice To Owner: Forthwith, and at least ten (10) days prior to
the hearing, the mayor shall give written notice of such hearing by certified
mail with return receipt requested to the owner of such property at the address
shown by the current year's tax rolls in the office of the treasurer of the
county in which such property is located. (1986 Code § 13-14)
4-4-5: HEARING BY COUNCIL; ORDER ABATEMENT:
Upon the date specified in such notice, the city council shall hear the matter
and shall receive information thereon, including anything which may be
presented by the owner of the premises, personally or by agent or attorney. If
the council determines that the conditions specified in subsection
4-4-4A of this chapter exist upon such premises, it shall order the property to
be cleaned of trash or the weeds and grass cut or mowed, or both cleaning and
cutting and mowing, if necessary to abate the conditions found to exist. (1986
Code § 13-15)
4-4-6: ABATEMENT BY CITY OR CONTRACT; COST:
   A.   Work Performed By City Or Contract: The work ordered to be performed
under section
4-4-5 of this chapter may be done by the employees of the city under
supervision of the mayor, or it may be let by contract to the lowest and best
bidder, after appropriate notice, in the manner for letting other contracts by
public bid. (1986 Code § 13-16)
   B.   Cost Determined; Statement Issued:
      1.   Upon the completion of the work ordered to be performed under
section
4-4-5 of this chapter, the mayor shall report the cost thereof to the city
council.
      2.   Such report shall be itemized as to each tract, as follows: labor,
machinery, rental or depreciation, fuel and supplies, cost of notice and other
costs.
      3.   The city council shall examine the report, and after receiving
appropriate information, shall determine the total actual costs of the work and
shall direct the city clerk to forward a statement and demand payment thereof
by certified mail, with return receipt requested, to the owner of the property
at the address shown by the current tax rolls in the office of the treasurer of
the county in which the property lies. (1986 Code § 13-17)
4-4-7: FAILURE TO PAY COSTS:
If the costs of the work performed under this chapter are not paid within
thirty (30) days from the date of mailing the notice prescribed by subsection
4-4-6B of this chapter, the city clerk shall forward a certified statement of
the amount of such costs to the county treasurer of the county in which the
property upon which the work was done is located, to be levied upon the
property and to be collected by the county treasurer in the manner prescribed
by the law of this state. (1986 Code § 13-19)
4-4-8: SERVICE OF NOTICE:
The service of all notices prescribed by this chapter shall be evidenced by the
return of the officer making such service, certified in his official capacity,
and filed in the office of the city clerk. (1986 Code § 13-18)
4-4-9: ENFORCEMENT OF STATE LAW; ADMINISTRATIVE DUTIES:
   A.   Weeds And Trash: The city attorney and the assistant city attorney are
hereby designated administrative officers for the purpose of carrying out the
duties of the mayor and city council in the enforcement of the provisions of
state law, 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 22-111, relating to the cleaning and
mowing of property. The city attorney or the assistant city attorney is
empowered to act individually in the enforcement of this statute. (1986 Code §
13-35)
   B.   Dilapidated Buildings: The city attorney and the assistant city
attorney are hereby designated administrative officers for the purpose of
carrying out the duties of the mayor and city council in the enforcement of the
provisions of state law, 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 22-112, relating to
dilapidated buildings. The city attorney or the assistant city attorney is
empowered to act individually in the enforcement of this statute. (1986 Code §
13-36)
4-4-10: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter, by doing any act
prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or who fails to do any act
required by any such provision, or who fails to do any act when such provision
declares such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor, or who
violates any legal order or regulation made pursuant to this chapter or who
maintains any nuisance as defined in this chapter, is guilty of an offense and,
upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which a violation continue shall be deemed a
separate offense. (1986 Code § 13-34; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 5
GARBAGE AND REFUSE
SECTION:
4-5-1: Definitions
4-5-2: Accumulation; Container Requirements
4-5-3: Collection Of Refuse
4-5-4: Service Charges
4-5-5: Rubble Accumulation And Collection
4-5-6: Disposal Of Wastes
4-5-7: Uncollected Garbage; Public Nuisance
4-5-8: Penalty
4-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
EXCESS VOLUME: Any amount of garbage and/or rubbish that will not fit inside of
the city provided container with the lid capable of being fully closed without
force.
GARBAGE: Shall mean putrescible wastes, and shall include all such substances
from all public and private establishments and from all residences. It shall
not, however, be construed to include human sewage.
HEALTH OFFICER: The medical director of the Craig County health department or
his authorized representative.
REFUSE: Shall include the terms "garbage", "rubbish" and "rubble" as defined in
this section.
RUBBISH: Tin cans, bottles, papers, cardboard, rags, grass cuttings, and all
other similar waste materials which can be placed in containers of the type
specified and required by this chapter.
RUBBLE: Tree limbs, scrap lumber, scrap building materials, discarded furniture
and appliances, dilapidated buildings, discarded fence posts, old tires, and
any other similar earthen, wooden, plastic, metal, or rubber waste materials
too large to be placed in containers.
SERVICE UNIT: One standard refuse container of not more than thirty two (32)
gallon capacity, or four (4) cubic feet.
SUPERINTENDENT: The superintendent of the Vinita solid waste department. (Ord.
3348, 3-6-2007; amd. Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
4-5-2: ACCUMULATION; CONTAINER REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Containers Required:
      1.   It shall be unlawful to deposit or place refuse upon any private or
public property unless the same shall be enclosed in an approved container in
conformity with subsection B of this section.
      2.   A number of containers sufficient to hold refuse that will
accumulate between collections shall be provided by the owner or occupant of
each premises, if such is not provided for by the city. (1986 Code § 9-2)
   B.   Approved Containers:
      1.   All residents, businesses or other individuals or entities shall use
the refuse containers or roll-off containers supplied by the city, or provide
their own, if such containers are not provided by the city. (Ord. 3348, 3-6-
2007)
      2.   In the event the city does not provide a container, residents shall
provide refuse containers described as follows: The refuse containers shall be
portable, with side handles, constructed of galvanized metal or equivalent in
such manner as to be strong, not easily corrodible, rodentproof, flyproof, and
shall have a tightfitting lid. Lids shall be kept in place on the receptacle at
all times except when depositing or removing wastes. Such containers shall have
a capacity of not more than thirty two (32) gallons, and racks or other means
to prevent overturning shall be provided. (1986 Code § 9-3; amd. 2005 Code)
      3.   (Rep. by Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
      4.   It shall be unlawful to destroy, mutilate or in other ways damage
the city refuse containers. (1986 Code § 9-3; amd. 2005 Code)
      5.   No rubble will be deposited into any city provided containers except
roll-off containers.
      6.   In addition to all penalties provided by this chapter, a charge of
seventy five dollars ($75.00) shall be made to the resident or entity with a
city provided ninety six (96) gallon container if said container is destroyed,
damaged, or stolen. Further, in addition to all penalties provided by this
chapter, a charge of two hundred seventy five dollars ($275.00) shall be made
to the entity with a city provided commercial container if said container is
destroyed, damaged, or stolen. (Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
4-5-3: COLLECTION OF REFUSE:
   A.   Authorized Collector:
      1.   No person, firm or corporation, other than the city or its agent,
shall collect, transport, or dispose of refuse within the corporate limits of
the city, except with approval by the city. (Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
      2.   Only enclosed packer trucks and approved roll-off containers shall
be used. (1986 Code § 9-4; amd. 2005 Code)
      3.   No person, firm or corporation shall pilfer or otherwise remove
refuse from the property of another within the corporate limits of the city
without the consent of the owner of such property. (1986 Code § 9-4)
   B.   Collection Frequency: Garbage and rubbish shall be collected from each
residence and each business at frequencies determined by motion of the city
council from time to time. (1986 Code § 9-5)
   C.   Placement Of Containers:
      1.   Containers shall be placed only at designated locations, as
determined by the solid waste department, and shall face the proper direction
for collection with the lid completely closed or capable of being completely
closed without force.
      2.   The city will make special arrangements to assist with placing a
resident's container at the designated location for collection when the solid
waste department determines it is appropriate to do so. (Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
      3.   No authorized agency or person shall collect refuse from containers
not so placed and maintained. (1986 Code § 9-6)
4-5-4: SERVICE CHARGES:
   A.   Monthly Billing: A monthly refuse service charge shall be assessed and
collected from each business, institution or establishment and from each
residential unit within the city. The city clerk will bill and collect said
refuse charge to be made in accordance with this section. (1986 Code § 9-9)
   B.   Rates Established:
      1.   Residential: The minimum service charge for each residential unit
shall be an amount(s) established by motion or resolution of the city council
from time to time.
      2.   Business: The minimum service charge for each business establishment
shall be an amount(s) established by motion or resolution of the city council
from time to time. (1986 Code § 9-9; amd. 2005 Code)
      3.   Residential And Business: An additional service charge, in an amount
(s) established by motion or resolution of the city council from time to time,
shall be assessed for:
         a.   Requiring the return of a refuse truck to empty a container that
was not properly placed for collection or was blocked by an obstruction and not
accessible for collection,
         b.   The collection of excess volume, or
         c.   The collection of rubble. (Ord. 3416, 11-18-2008)
   C.   Excessive Volume Of Refuse:
      1.   Those businesses and other establishments which generate a volume of
refuse in excess of normal amounts as determined by the superintendent shall be
charged an additional sum to be set by city council for each establishment.
      2.   Schools, hospitals and other governmental buildings shall be charged
at the same rate as business establishments. (1986 Code § 9-9)
      3.   Any resident having excess volume more than two (2) times in any one
month will be required to have two (2) residential polycarts. (Ord. 3416, 11-
18-2008)
   D.   Payment Of Charges; Delinquencies:
      1.   It shall be the duty of each person, firm, corporation, institution
or establishment to pay the charges herein provided by the tenth day of each
month, at the same time and in the same manner provided for the payment of
water bills 1 .
      2.   If not so paid, such service shall be discontinued along with the
water service and at the same time, and shall be subject to the same penalties
for restoration of water service. (1986 Code § 9-9)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 8, chapter 2 of this code.
4-5-5: RUBBLE ACCUMULATION AND COLLECTION:
   A.   Accumulation Restricted: It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit
or place rubble on any private or public property, or to allow rubble to
accumulate in the city, except that the same may be accumulated temporarily for
not more than thirty (30) days pending collection. (1986 Code § 9-7)
   B.   Preparation For Collection: Tree limbs not exceeding three inches (3")
in diameter shall be cut in lengths not to exceed three feet (3') and not to
exceed fifty (50) pounds. Other rubble shall be reduced to a size and weight
convenient for collection. (1986 Code § 9-7; amd. 2005 Code)
4-5-6: DISPOSAL OF WASTES:
   A.   Landfills: All garbage, rubbish and rubble shall be disposed by
sanitary landfill and cover. Sites for landfill shall be approved by the city
council and state department of environmental quality.
   B.   Burning; Scavenging: The burning of garbage or rubbish within the
corporate limits of the city, or at the disposal area, is prohibited 1 . No
person shall scavenge junk or otherwise remove any waste materials from the
disposal site without a written agreement with the city. (1986 Code § 9-8; amd.
2005 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also chapter 7 of this title.
4-5-7: UNCOLLECTED GARBAGE; PUBLIC NUISANCE:
Garbage, rubbish or rubble uncollected due to failure to pay the refuse service
charge, or due to improper type, placing or maintenance of containers is hereby
declared to be unlawful and a public nuisance. (1986 Code § 9-10)
4-5-8: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable
as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each and every violation of this chapter shall constitute
a separate offense and each day on which a violation occurs shall constitute a
separate offense and be punishable as such. (1986 Code § 9-11; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 6
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
4-6-1: Sale Of Fireworks
4-6-2: Discharge Of Fireworks
4-6-3: Exception; Public Displays
4-6-4: Penalty
4-6-1: SALE OF FIREWORKS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to display for sale,
offer for sale or sell within the corporate limits of the city, any fireworks
of any type, nature or description; provided however, that this section shall
not prohibit the sale of fireworks at those locations within the limits of the
city recommended by the planning commission and annually approved by the city
council. (1986 Code § 8-18)
4-6-2: DISCHARGE OF FIREWORKS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to set off or detonate
any fireworks of an explosive nature or noise emitting type, nature or
description within the corporate limits of the city. (1986 Code § 8-19)
4-6-3: EXCEPTION; PUBLIC DISPLAYS:
The provisions of this chapter shall not be construed to prohibit the
presentation of public displays of fireworks by responsible persons or
organizations who have first obtained permission of the city council for the
presentation of such displays. (1986 Code § 8-20)
4-6-4: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who violates any provision of this chapter
shall be guilty of an offense and, upon conviction, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed
a separate offense. (1986 Code § 8-29; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 7
ANTI-BURNING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
4-7-1: Short Title; Definitions
4-7-2: Burning Restrictions
4-7-3: Penalty
4-7-1: SHORT TITLE; DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Short Title: This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the
VINITA, OKLAHOMA, ANTI-BURNING ORDINANCE.
   B.   Definitions:
    COMMERCIAL OPEN BURNING: Burning of natural vegetation shall be allowed on
Commercially zoned property, inspected and approved by the Fire Chief,
Assistant Fire Chief, or their designee.
   RECREATIONAL BURNING: Burning for the enjoyment of residents in residential
outdoor firepits, fireplaces, charcoal or gas grills.
   RESIDENTIAL OPEN BURNING: Burning of natural vegetation including trees,
limbs, grass, shrubs, and leaves, solely for the purpose of land clearance. All
fires shall be ignited after sunrise and extinguished by sunset. (Ord. 3699, 3-
19-2019)
4-7-2: BURNING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Burning Prohibited; Exception: No person shall wilfully ignite or cause
to be ignited any fire out of doors within the limits of the City for the
purpose of burning trash, garbage, refuse, litter, rubbish, grass, brush, or
any combustible materials whether said fire be in a receptacle or incinerator
or not; except times approved by the Fire Chief or his designee, following
advance notification from the landowner upon whose property the fire is to be
set; persons shall be able to burn lawn, tree and garden waste on the property
that it was produced on, providing a water source is available and not to be
left unattended.
   B.   Mandatory Extinguishment: The Fire Department shall order the
extinguishment of any open burning that creates or adds to a hazardous
situation. Owners are required to extinguish the fire upon the order of the
Fire Department or if the fire escapes the confined area of the burn pile or
container. Failure of an owner to extinguish a fire may result in the Fire
Department extinguishing the fire at the owner's expense at a rate currently
set for fire runs outside the City limits.
   C.   Transporting To Site Within City: It shall be unlawful for any person,
firm or corporation to cause the transportation of any such lawn, tree, and
garden waste to any site within the corporate limits of the City of Vinita for
the specific purpose of off premises burning.
   D.   Responsibility For Open Burning; Compliance: Persons who conduct open
burning in accordance with the provisions of this chapter are not exempt or
excused from the consequences, damages or injuries that may result from such
conduct, nor are they exempt or excused from complying with all applicable
laws, ordinances, rules and orders.
   E.   Compliance With State And Federal Laws: All laws, rules and regulations
of the State of Oklahoma, United States Federal government, or any subsidiary
agency, department, or branch must be followed and nothing herein shall be
construed to change or amend any such laws, rules and regulations. (Ord. 3699,
3-19-2019)
4-7-3: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who violates any provision of this chapter
shall be guilty of an offense and, upon conviction, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-9-13 of this Code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed
a separate offense. (1986 Code § 8-29; amd. 2005 Code)
TITLE 5
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL OFFENSES
ARTICLE A. STATE LAWS; MISCELLANEOUS OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-1A-1: Misdemeanor Crimes And Offenses Under State Law
5-1A-2: Committing Or Aiding In Offense
5-1A-3: Theft Of Cable Television Service
5-1A-4: Texting While Driving Prohibited
5-1A-1: MISDEMEANOR CRIMES AND OFFENSES UNDER STATE LAW:
   A.   Misdemeanor Offenses Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to
commit any act constituting a misdemeanor, crime or offense as defined by title
21 or 63 of the Oklahoma Statutes, as amended from time to time.
   B.   Statute Provisions Adopted By Reference: The city does hereby adopt and
incorporate by reference the provisions of titles 21 and 63 of the Oklahoma
Statutes, and authorizes law enforcement officials by and on behalf of the city
to enforce the terms thereof within the city limits, and authorizes the
prosecution of the same in the Vinita municipal court 1 . (Ord. 3104, 4-5-1999)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  1-9-12 of this code for specific misdemeanor offenses and fines imposed.
5-1A-2: COMMITTING OR AIDING IN OFFENSE:
   A.   Attempts To Commit Offense: Every person who attempts to commit an
offense against the ordinances of the city, and in such attempt does any act
toward the commission of such offense, but fails or is prevented or intercepted
in the perpetration thereof, is guilty of an offense, and shall be punished in
the manner prescribed for the offense itself. (1986 Code § 14-2)
   B.   Aiding In Offense: When no punishment for counseling, aiding, or
abetting in the commission of a particular offense is expressly prescribed by
ordinance, every person who counsels, aids, or abets another in the commission
of such is guilty of an offense and punishable in the same manner as the
principal offender. (1986 Code § 14-3)
   C.   Penalty: Except in cases where a different punishment is now or may
hereafter be prescribed by ordinance, any person, firm or corporation who
commits an offense within this chapter shall, upon conviction, be punishable as
provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall constitute
a separate offense. (1986 Code § 14-1; amd. 2005 Code)
5-1A-3: THEFT OF CABLE TELEVISION SERVICE:
   A.   Prohibited Acts: Any person who commits any of the following acts shall
be guilty, upon conviction, of the misdemeanor of larceny of cable television
service or tampering with cable television service: (Ord. 3097, 2-2-1999; amd.
2005 Code)
      1.   Knowingly obtains or attempts to obtain cable television service
from another by means, artifice, trick, deception or devise, without payment to
the operator of a said service of all lawful compensation for each type of
service; or
      2.   Knowingly assists or instructs any other person in obtaining or
attempting to obtain any cable television service without the payment to the
operator of all lawful compensation; or
      3.   Knowingly tampers or otherwise interferes with or connects to by
means, whether mechanical, electrical, acoustical or other means, any cables
wires or other devices used for the distribution of cable television without
authority from the operator of said service; or
      4.   Knowingly manufactures; imports into this state; distributes, sells,
offers for sale, rental, or use; possesses for sale, rental, or use; or
advertises for sale, rental, or use, any device of any description, or any
plan, or kit for the device, designed in whole or in part to facilitate the
doing of any of the acts specified in subsections A1, A2 and A3 of this
section.
   B.   Evidence Of Intent: In any prosecution, as set forth in subsection A of
this section, the existence on the property and in the actual possession of the
accused, of: 1) any connection, wire, conductor or any device whatsoever, which
is connected in such a manner as would appear to permit the use of cable
television service without the same being reported for payment to and
specifically authorized by the operator of the cable television service; or 2)
the existence on the property and in the actual possession of the accused, in
quantities or volumes suggesting possession for resale, of any device designed
in whole or in part to facilitate the performance of any of the illegal acts
mentioned in subsection A of this section, shall be prima facie evidence of
intent to violate, and of the violation of, the provisions of subsection A of
this section, by the accused.
   C.   Use Of Satellite Dish: The provisions of this section shall not be
construed or otherwise interpreted to prohibit an individual from owning or
operating a device commonly known as a "satellite receiving dish" for the
purpose of receiving and utilizing satellite relayed television signals for his
own use. (Ord. 3097, 2-2-1999)
5-1A-4: TEXTING WHILE DRIVING PROHIBITED:
   A.   Handheld Devices: It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a
motor vehicle on any street or highway within the city of Vinita while using a
handheld electronic communication device to manually compose, send or read an
electronic text message while the motor vehicle is in motion.
   B.   Penalty: Any person who violates the provisions of subsection A of this
section shall, upon conviction be punished by a fine as stated in section
1-9-12 of this code.
   C.   Emergency Use: The provisions of subsection A of this section shall not
apply if the person is using the cellular telephone or electronic communication
device for the sole purpose of communicating with any of the following
regarding an imminent emergency situation:
      1.   An emergency response operator;
      2.   A hospital, physician's office or health clinic;
      3.   A provider of ambulance services;
      4.   A provider of firefighting services; or
      5.   A law enforcement agency.
   D.   Definitions: For the purpose of this section:
    CELLULAR TELEPHONE: An analog or digital wireless telephone authorized by
the federal communications commission to operate in the frequency bandwidth
reserved for cellular telephones.
   COMPOSE, SEND OR READ: With respect to a text message means the manual
entry, sending or retrieval of a text message to communicate with any person or
device.
   ELECTRONIC COMMUNICATION DEVICE: An electronic device that permits the user
to manually transmit a communication of written text by means other than
through an oral transfer or wire communication. This term does not include a
device that is physically or electronically integrated into a motor vehicle or
a voice operated global positioning or navigation system that is affixed to a
motor vehicle, or a hands free device that allows the user to write, send or
read a text message without the use of either hand except to activate,
deactivate or initiate a feature or function.
   TEXT MESSAGE: Includes a text based message, instant message, electronic
message, photo, video or electronic mail. (Ord. 3613, 12-1-2015, eff. 1-1-2016)
ARTICLE B. OFFENSES AGAINST DECENCY, MORALITY
SECTION:
5-1B-1: Gambling Related Offenses
5-1B-2: Vagrancy
5-1B-3: Begging
5-1B-4: Loitering On Streets Or Near Schools
5-1B-5: Prostitution And Related Offenses
5-1B-6: Indecent Conduct; Peeping Into Windows
5-1B-7: Offenses Involving Intoxicating Liquor
5-1B-8: Permitting Or Allowing Gatherings Where Minors Are Consuming Alcoholic
Beverages
5-1B-1: GAMBLING RELATED OFFENSES:
   A.   Betting On Or Playing Games: It is unlawful for any person to bet or
play at any game whatsoever, for money, property, checks, credits or other
representatives of value with cards, dice, or another device which may be
adapted to or used in playing any game of chance or in which chance is a
material element. (1986 Code § 14-4; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Slot Machines: It is unlawful for any person to set up, operate or
conduct, or permit to be set up, operated or conducted in or about his place of
business, whether as an owner, employee or agent, any slot machine for the
purpose of having or allowing the same to be played by others for money,
property, check, credit or any representative of value. (1986 Code § 14-5; amd.
2005 Code)
   C.   Dice Or Other Games: It shall be unlawful for any owner, proprietor,
manager or person in charge in any hotel lobby, store or place where articles
are kept for sale to suffer, allow or permit any person to throw or shake or
play dice, or any other game, scheme or device of chance, at or in such hotel
lobby, store or place. (1986 Code § 14-6; amd. 2005 Code)
   D.   Loitering: It is unlawful for any person to loiter about in the
immediate vicinity where persons are gambling, whether by playing games,
operating a slot machine or other device, or otherwise. (1986 Code § 14-7)
5-1B-2: VAGRANCY:
   A.   Vagrants Defined: The following persons are vagrants within the meaning
of this article:
      1.   An idle person who lives without any means, or who has no visible
means of support and makes no exertion to obtain a livelihood by honest
employment.
      2.   Any person who strolls or loiters idly about the streets of the
city, having no local habitation and no honest business or employment.
      3.   Any person who strolls about to tell fortunes or to exhibit tricks
not licensed in accordance with law or ordinance.
      4.   Any common prostitute, any manager or controller of a house of
prostitution or ill fame, or anyone employed therein as a barkeeper, caller of
figures for dances, or habitual frequenter thereof.
      5.   Any professional gambler or gambler commonly known as a tinhorn
gambler, card player, or card shark.
      6.   Any person who goes about to get alms, who is not afflicted or
disabled by a physical malady or misfortune.
      7.   Any habitual drunkard.
      8.   Any person who abandons or neglects or refuses to support his
family. (1986 Code § 14-10)
   B.   Vagrancy Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to be a vagrant in
the city, and any person who is a vagrant in the city shall be punished as
provided by the ordinances of the city. (1986 Code § 14-11)
5-1B-3: BEGGING:
It is unlawful for any person to beg alms from any person, organization, or
agency except an organization or agency, public or private, whose purpose or
one of whose purposes is to aid persons in need. (1986 Code § 14-12)
5-1B-4: LOITERING ON STREETS OR NEAR SCHOOLS:
   A.   Loitering; Sleeping On Streets: It is unlawful for any person, without
lawful reason, between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and
sunrise, to loiter or wander aimlessly within the city on the streets, in other
public places, or on property of another; or during such time to sleep on any
street, in any other public place, or on any property of another without the
expressed or tacit consent of the owner or person in charge of such place.
(1986 Code § 14-14)
   B.   Interfering With School Activities: It is unlawful for a person not to
leave or to return within thirty (30) days thereafter, without written
permission, after being asked to leave by the chief administrative officer of
the school or his designated representative after such person interferes,
commits an act which interferes or enters for the purpose of interfering with
the peaceful conduct of activities at a public or private school. (1986 Code §
14-14; amd. 2005 Code)
5-1B-5: PROSTITUTION AND RELATED OFFENSES:
   A.   Definition: "Illicit sexual intercourse" is sexual intercourse with any
person other than one's lawful husband or wife. (1986 Code § 14-16)
   B.   Prostitution:
      1.   It is unlawful for any person to offer, submit, or give himself or
herself to a lewd or immoral use, such as illicit sexual intercourse, or to
engage in any lewd or immoral act, for money or any other thing of value. (1986
Code § 14-15; amd. 2005 Code)
      2.   It is unlawful for any person to engage in illicit sexual
intercourse or any other immoral act, or knowingly to consort with a prostitute
or other person of immoral vocation, or to consort with another for an immoral
purpose or to occupy any room for an immoral purpose, whether in a public or
private place in the city, or to loiter about a house or place of prostitution
or a house or place devoted to lewd or immoral acts. (1986 Code § 14-17)
   C.   House Of Prostitution:
      1.   It is unlawful for any person or any agent or employee thereof, to
keep or assist in keeping a house of prostitution or a house or place in the
city where persons meet or assemble for illicit sexual intercourse or for any
other lewd or immoral purpose; or knowingly to permit a prostitute or other
person of an immoral vocation to become or remain a guest in a hotel or rooming
house. (1986 Code § 14-18)
      2.   It is unlawful for any person to be an inmate or resident of a house
of prostitution or of a house or place devoted to lewd or immoral acts. (1986
Code § 14-19; amd. 2005 Code)
5-1B-6: INDECENT CONDUCT; PEEPING INTO WINDOWS:
   A.   Indecent Conduct: It is unlawful for any person to conduct himself or
herself in a lewd or indecent manner or in a manner offensive to the good
morals of the city, or to perform any act which is detrimental to the good
morals of the city, in any public or private place within the city.
   B.   Peeping Into Windows: It is unlawful for any person to hide or loiter
in the vicinity of any private dwelling house, apartment, or building with the
intent to watch, or gaze or look at, occupants therein in a clandestine manner;
or, while so hiding or loitering, to watch, or gaze or look at, occupants
therein in a clandestine manner. (1986 Code § 14-20)
5-1B-7: OFFENSES INVOLVING INTOXICATING LIQUOR 1 :
   A.   Unlawful Manufacture Or Sale:
      1.   It is unlawful for any person to manufacture, barter, sell, give
away, or otherwise furnish to another, any intoxicating liquor or beverage of
any kind except as permitted by law. (1986 Code § 14-21)
      2.   It is unlawful for any person or any agent or employee thereof, to
keep, maintain, or aid or abet in keeping or maintaining, a place where
intoxicating liquor is manufactured, sold, bartered, given away or otherwise
furnished in violation of law or the ordinances of the city. (1986 Code § 14-
24)
   B.   Possession, Transporting: It is unlawful for any person to have in his
possession or under his control any intoxicating liquor or beverage of any
kind, except as permitted by law, or to transport or in any manner convey from
place to place within the city any such intoxicating liquor or beverage except
as permitted by law. (1986 Code § 14-22)
   C.   Loitering: It is unlawful for any person to loiter in any place where
intoxicating liquor or beverage of any kind is bartered, sold, given away, or
otherwise furnished contrary to law. (1986 Code § 14-23)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 3, chapter 3 of this code for alcoholic beverage regulations.
5-1B-8: PERMITTING OR ALLOWING GATHERINGS WHERE MINORS ARE CONSUMING ALCOHOLIC
BEVERAGES:
   A.   Definitions: For purposes of this section, the following definitions
shall apply:
    ALCOHOL: Ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl, or spirits of wine, from
whatever source or by whatever process produced.
   ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE: Includes alcohol, spirits, liquor, wine, beer, and every
liquid or solid containing alcohol, spirits, wine, or beer, and which contains
one-half of one percent or more of alcohol by volume and which is fit for
beverage purposes either alone or when diluted, mixed, or combined with other
substances. This term includes intoxicating beverages and "low point beer" as
defined herein.
   GATHERING: A party, gathering, or event, where a group of three (3) or more
persons have assembled or are assembling for a social occasion or social
activity.
   INTOXICATING BEVERAGE: Includes beverages containing more than three and
two-tenths percent (3.2%) alcohol by weight.
   LEGAL GUARDIAN:
      1.   A person who, by court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor; or
      2.   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by the
court.
   LOW POINT BEER: Means and includes beverages containing more than one-half
of one percent (1/2 of 1%) alcohol by volume, and not more than three and two-
tenths percent (3.2%) alcohol by weight, including, but not limited to, beer or
cereal malt beverages obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion of
barley or other grain, malt or similar products.
   MINOR: Any person under twenty one (21) years of age.
   PARENT: A person who is a natural parent, adoptive parent, foster parent, or
stepparent of another person.
   PREMISES: Any residence or other private property, place, or premises,
including any commercial or business premises.
   RESPONSE COSTS: The costs associated with responses by law enforcement,
fire, and other emergency response providers to a gathering, including, but not
limited to: 1) salaries and benefits of law enforcement, code enforcement,
fire, or other emergency response personnel for the amount of time spent
responding to, remaining at, or otherwise dealing with a gathering, and the
administrative costs attributable to such response(s); 2) the cost of any
medical treatment for any law enforcement, code enforcement, fire, or other
emergency response personnel injured responding to, remaining at, or leaving
the scene of a gathering; 3) the cost of repairing any city equipment or
property damaged, and the cost of the use of any such equipment, in responding
to, remaining at, or leaving the scene of a gathering; and 4) any other
allowable costs related to the enforcement of this section.
   B.   Consumption Of Alcohol By Minor In Public Place, Place Open To Public,
Or Place Not Open To Public:
Except as permitted by state law, it is unlawful for any minor to:
      1.   Consume at any public place or any place open to the public
alcoholic beverage; or
      2.   Consume at any place not open to the public any alcoholic beverage,
unless in connection with the consumption of the alcoholic beverage that minor
is being supervised by his or her parent or legal guardian.
   C.   Hosting, Permitting, Or Allowing A Party, Gathering, Or Event Where
Minors Consuming Alcoholic Beverages Prohibited:
      1.   a. It is the duty of any person having control of any premises, who
knowingly hosts, permits, or allows a gathering at said premises to take all
reasonable steps to prevent the consumption of alcoholic beverages by any minor
at the gathering. Reasonable steps are controlling access to alcoholic
beverages at the gathering; controlling the quantity of alcoholic beverages
present at the gathering; verifying the age of persons attending the gathering
by inspecting driver's licenses or other government issued identification cards
to ensure that minors do not consume alcoholic beverages while at the
gathering; and supervising the activities of minors at the gathering.
         b.   It is unlawful for any person having control of any premises to
knowingly host, permit, or allow a gathering to take place at said premises
where at least one minor consumes an alcoholic beverage, whenever the person
having control of the premises either knows a minor has consumed an alcoholic
beverage or reasonably should have known that a minor consumed an alcoholic
beverage had the person taken all reasonable steps to prevent the consumption
of an alcoholic beverage by a minor as set forth in subsection C1a of this
section.
      2.   This section shall not apply to conduct involving the use of
alcoholic beverages that occurs exclusively between a minor and his or her
parent or legal guardian.
      3.   Nothing in this section should be interpreted to prohibit any family
activity held in the confines of the family home from providing the use of
alcohol to immediate family members within the supervision of parents and
guardians. However, if a minor leaves such a family gathering intoxicated and
is found in public then said providers of alcohol will be held responsible in
the same manner as a nonfamily gathering.
      4.   Nothing in this section should be interpreted to prohibit any
religious practice which includes the use of alcohol. However, if a minor
leaves such a religious gathering intoxicated and is found to be in public then
said providers of alcohol will be held responsible in the same manner as a
nonreligious gathering.
      5.   This section shall not apply to any premises licensed by the state
of Oklahoma to dispense alcoholic beverages.
   D.   Penalty: Any person who shall violate the provisions of this section
shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the city and upon conviction
thereof shall be punished with a fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00), or by
imprisonment not exceeding sixty (60) days, or by both such fine and
imprisonment, plus all court costs and statutory penalties, as set forth in
section
1-9-14 of this code.
   E.   Reservation Of Legal Options: Violations of this section may be
prosecuted by the city of Vinita criminally, civilly, and/or administratively
as provided by this code. The city may seek administrative fees and response
costs associated with enforcement of this section through all remedies or
procedures provided by statute, ordinance, or law. This section shall not limit
the authority of peace officers or private citizens to make arrests for any
criminal offense arising out of conduct regulated by this section, nor shall it
limit the city's ability to initiate and prosecute any criminal offense arising
out of the same circumstances necessitating the application of this section.
   F.   Local Authority: This section shall not apply where prohibited or
preempted by state or federal law. (Ord. 3406, 8-19-2008)
ARTICLE C. OFFENSES AGAINST THE PEACE
SECTION:
5-1C-1: Weapons; Firearms
5-1C-2: Assemblages; Prohibited Acts
5-1C-3: Disturbing The Peace; Disorderly Conduct
5-1C-4: Loud Noise Or Music
5-1C-5: Displaying Insulting Signs
5-1C-1: WEAPONS; FIREARMS 1 :
   A.   Carrying Certain Weapons Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to
carry upon or about his person any pistol, revolver, bowie knife, dirk, dagger,
metal knuckle, switchblade knife, or other deadly weapon or instrument, whether
concealed or not, except when doing so in line of duty or as may be permitted
by law. (1986 Code § 14-26)
   B.   Discharging Firearms, Air Rifles And BB Guns: It is unlawful for any
person to discharge a firearm in the city except when doing so in the line of
duty, when lawfully doing so in defense of oneself or another person, or of
property, or when otherwise authorized by law or ordinance. It is unlawful to
discharge an air rifle or BB gun in the city. (1986 Code § 14-27)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  5-2-2 of this title.
5-1C-2: ASSEMBLAGES; PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Unlawful Assembly: It is unlawful for three (3) or more persons to
assemble together, or, being assembled together, to act in concert to do any
unlawful act against the peace, or to the terror of others, or to make any
movement thereto or any preparation therefor, or otherwise to assemble together
unlawfully or riotously. (1986 Code § 14-28)
   B.   Disturbing Religious Worship: It is unlawful for any person to disturb
any congregation or assembly of persons meeting for religious worship by making
noise; by rude, indecent or improper behavior; by profane, improper, or loud
language; or in any other manner, either within the place of worship or within
hearing distance thereof. (1986 Code § 14-30)
   C.   Disturbing Public Assembly: It is unlawful for any person to disturb
any lawful public gathering or assembly by making noise; by rude, indecent, or
improper behavior; by profane, improper, or loud language; or in any other
manner, either within the place of assembly or within hearing distance thereof.
(1986 Code § 14-31)
5-1C-3: DISTURBING THE PEACE; DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
It is unlawful for any person to wilfully or maliciously disturb the peace of
another or others by violent, obstreperous, or improper conduct or carriage; by
loud or unusual noise; or by unseemly, obscene, offensive, or abusive language;
or to insult another or others by such conduct or language; or to conduct
himself in a disorderly manner. (1986 Code § 14-29; amd. 2005 Code)
5-1C-4: LOUD NOISE OR MUSIC:
It is unlawful for any person to disturb the peace and quietude of any part of
the city by operating, having operated, or permitting to be operated, any
contrivance, whether electric or not, with or without a loudspeaker, in such
manner as to emit loud music, noise, or words. However, this shall not prohibit
religious bodies from playing chimes, bells, carillons, or other religious
music. (1986 Code § 14-32)
5-1C-5: DISPLAYING INSULTING SIGNS:
It is unlawful for any person to display any sign, emblem, badge, flag, or
device which in its common acceptance is insulting, profane, or abusive to the
citizens of the city, and which is calculated, or of which the natural
consequence is, to cause a breach of the peace or an assault. (1986 Code § 14-
33)
ARTICLE D. OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS
SECTION:
5-1D-1: Assault And Battery
5-1D-2: Intimidating Laborers Or Employers
5-1D-1: ASSAULT AND BATTERY:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following terms shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    ASSAULT: Any wilful and unlawful attempt or offer with force or violence to
do a corporal hurt to another.
   BATTERY: Any wilful and unlawful use of force or violence upon the person of
another.
   B.   Prohibited Acts: It is unlawful to commit an assault or an assault and
battery within the city, and any person committing an assault or an assault and
battery within the city is guilty of an offense. (1986 Code § 14-35)
5-1D-2: INTIMIDATING LABORERS OR EMPLOYERS:
   A.   Laborers: It shall be unlawful for any person or persons, by force,
threats or intimidation, to prevent, or endeavor to prevent, any hired foreman,
journeyman, apprentice, workman, laborer, servant or other person employed by
another from continuing or performing his work, or from accepting any new work
or employment, or to induce such hired person to relinquish his work or
employment, or to return any work he has in hand before it is finished. (1986
Code § 14-36)
   B.   Employers: It shall be unlawful for any person or persons, by the use
of force, threats or intimidation, to prevent, or endeavor to prevent, another
from employing any person or compel another person to employ any person, or to
force or induce another to alter his mode of carrying on his business, or to
limit or increase the number of his hired foremen, journeymen, apprentices,
workmen, laborers, servants or other persons employed by him, or their rate of
wages or time of service. (1986 Code § 14-37)
ARTICLE E. OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY
SECTION:
5-1E-1: Petty Larceny
5-1E-2: Meddling With Vehicles
5-1E-3: Injuring Buildings Or Structures
5-1E-4: Placing Signs On Property Of Another
5-1E-5: Trespassing
5-1E-1: PETTY LARCENY:
   A.   Definition: "Petty larceny" is the taking of personal property of value
of not to exceed fifty dollars ($50.00) accomplished by fraud or stealth and
with intent to deprive another thereof, when the property is not taken from the
person of another. (1986 Code § 14-38)
   B.   Violation: Petty larceny is unlawful. (1986 Code § 14-38; amd. 2005
Code)
5-1E-2: MEDDLING WITH VEHICLES:
It is unlawful for any person to crank, start, otherwise meddle with, molest,
enter, occupy, loiter in, take, or drive away any automobile or other vehicle
belonging to another, without the consent of the owner or person in charge
thereof. (1986 Code § 14-39; amd. 2005 Code)
5-1E-3: INJURING BUILDINGS OR STRUCTURES:
It is unlawful for any person to destroy, injure, deface, besmear, or molest
any structure, building, outbuilding, fence, or any other private property,
real or personal, belonging to another; or to use any such property wrongfully
to the detriment of the owner or other person entitled to its use; or to
interfere wrongfully with the use of such property by its owner or any other
person entitled to its use. (1986 Code § 14-40)
5-1E-4: PLACING SIGNS ON PROPERTY OF ANOTHER:
It is unlawful for any person to place, stick, tack, paste, post, paint, mark,
write, or print any sign, poster, picture, announcement, advertisement, bill,
placard, device or inscription upon any public or private building, fence,
sidewalk, bridge, viaduct, post, automobile, other vehicle, or other property
of another, without the consent of the owner or person in charge thereof. (1986
Code § 14-41)
5-1E-5: TRESPASSING:
Every person who intrudes or squats upon any lot or piece of land within the
city without license or authority from the owner thereof, or who erects or
occupies thereon any hut, hovel, shanty, or other structure without such
license or authority, and every person who places, erects, or occupies within
the bounds of any street, alley, or avenue of the city, any hut, hovel, shanty
or other structure whatever, is guilty of an offense. (1986 Code § 14-42)
ARTICLE F. OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC AUTHORITY
SECTION:
5-1F-1: Refusing Or Failing To Assist Officer
5-1F-2: Resisting Officer
5-1F-3: Offenses Related To Prisoners
5-1F-4: Personating An Officer Or Employee
5-1F-5: False Alarms Or Representation
5-1F-6: Removal Of Barricades
5-1F-1: REFUSING OR FAILING TO ASSIST OFFICER:
   A.   Authority To Call For Assistance: An officer of the city making or
about to make an arrest, or executing or about to execute a warrant or other
process, in accordance with the ordinances of the city or with state or federal
law, or suppressing or about to suppress a riot, affray, or unlawful assembly,
may call upon a person or persons to assist him in making such arrest,
executing such process, or suppressing such riot, affray, or unlawful assembly.
   B.   Refusal To Assist: It is unlawful for any person lawfully called upon
thus to assist an officer of the city to refuse or fail to do so. (1986 Code §
14-44)
5-1F-2: RESISTING OFFICER:
It is unlawful for any person knowingly or wilfully to resist, oppose, or
obstruct the chief of police, any other police officer, the municipal judge, or
other officer or employee of the city in the discharge of his official duties;
or, by threats or otherwise, to intimidate or to attempt to intimidate any such
officer or employee from the discharge of his official duties; or to assault or
beat, or revile, abuse, be disrespectful to, use abusive or indecent language
toward or about, any such officer or employee while such officer or employee is
in the discharge of his official duties. (1986 Code § 14-45)
5-1F-3: OFFENSES RELATED TO PRISONERS:
   A.   Rescuing; Assisting Escape; Giving Weapons, Intoxicants: It is unlawful
for any person, in any unlawful manner, to set at liberty, rescue, or attempt
to set at liberty or rescue, any prisoner from any officer or employee of the
city having legal custody of the same or from the city jail or other place of
confinement by the city, or to assist such prisoner in any manner to escape
from such prison or custody, or to give such prisoner any weapon or object
which might be used as a weapon or instrument to assist him in escape, or to
give such prisoner any alcoholic beverage or narcotics. (1986 Code § 14-46)
   B.   Escape Of Prisoners: It is unlawful for any person confined in the city
jail or other place of confinement by the city, or working upon the streets or
other public places of the city in pursuance of any judgment, or otherwise held
in legal custody by authority of the city, to escape or attempt to escape from
any such jail, prison, or custody. (1986 Code § 14-47)
   C.   Concealing Prisoner: It is unlawful for any person to wilfully and
knowingly conceal any prisoner who, having been confined in the city jail or
other place of confinement by the city, upon a charge or conviction of any city
ordinance or code provision, has escaped therefrom. (1986 Code § 14-48)
5-1F-4: PERSONATING AN OFFICER OR EMPLOYEE:
It is unlawful for any person to personate any officer or employee of the city,
falsely represent himself to be an officer or employee of the city, or exercise
or attempt to exercise any of the duties, functions, or powers of an officer or
employee of the city without being fully authorized to do so, and in such
assumed character does any act whereby another person is injured, defrauded,
vexed or annoyed. (1986 Code § 14-49)
5-1F-5: FALSE ALARMS OR REPRESENTATION:
   A.   False Fire Alarm: It is unlawful for any person to turn in a false fire
alarm, or in any manner to deceive or attempt to deceive the fire department or
any officer or employee thereof with reference to any fire alarm or reported
fire, or knowingly to cause the fire department or its officers or employees to
make a useless run. (1986 Code § 14-50)
   B.   False Representation To Officer: It is unlawful for any person or any
agent or employee thereof, knowingly to make any material misrepresentation to
any officer, employee or agency of the city government in any official
application to, or official dealing or negotiation with, such officer or
agency; or to commit perjury before any tribunal or office of the city. (1986
Code § 14-51)
5-1F-6: REMOVAL OF BARRICADES:
It is unlawful for any person, except by proper authority, to remove any
barricade or obstruction placed by authority of the city to keep traffic off
any pavement, street, curb, sidewalk, or other area. (1986 Code § 14-52)
CHAPTER 2
MINORS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Curfew
5-2-2: Selling Or Furnishing Cartridges Or Weapons
5-2-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Age And Hour Restrictions: It shall be and is hereby declared unlawful
for any person under the age of eighteen (18) years to travel upon or
congregate upon the streets and ways of the city from and after the hour of
twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight until five o'clock (5:00) A.M. on the nights of
Sunday through Thursday, and from and after the hour of one o'clock (1:00) A.M.
until five o'clock (5:00) A.M. on the nights of Friday and Saturday.
   B.   Authority To Extend Or Suspend Hours: The mayor (or in his absence the
president of the city council) is hereby authorized to extend or suspend the
curfew for special occasions for good cause shown, in which event, the person
making application therefor shall notify the police department in writing of
such extension of the curfew.
   C.   Exceptions: Persons within the following categories shall be excused
from the provisions hereof:
      1.   The person is accompanied by his or her parent or other adult member
of his or her family or guardian; or
      2.   The person is returning to his or her home from school, church,
work, or civic meeting, without taking unnecessary time or delay in doing so.
   D.   Notice Of Youth Detention To Parent: In the event of the apprehension
of any youth for any offense after the curfew hours, the parents or guardian of
such youth shall be immediately given notice of such detention by the police
department. (1986 Code § 14-13)
5-2-2: SELLING OR FURNISHING CARTRIDGES OR WEAPONS:
   A.   Cartridges: It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, barter, give
or furnish to any minor any loaded cartridges, except as authorized by law.
(1986 Code § 14-54)
   B.   Weapons: It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, barter, give or
furnish to any minor any pistol, revolver, dirk, bowie knife, metal knucks or
other dangerous or deadly weapons. (1986 Code § 14-55)
ARTICLE A. YOUTH ACCESS TO TOBACCO PRODUCTS AND VAPOR PRODUCTS
SECTION:
5-2A-1: Definitions
5-2A-2: Sale To Minors Prohibited
5-2A-3: Demand Proof Of Age
5-2A-4: Violations; Liability
5-2A-5: Violation By Minor
5-2A-6: Distributing Samples To Minors
5-2A-7: Cigarette Sales In Original, Sealed Package
5-2A-8: No Public Access
5-2A-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
   PERSON: Any individual, firm, fiduciary, partnership, corporation, trust, or
association, however formed.
   PROOF OF AGE: A driver's license, license for identification only, other
generally accepted means of identification that describes the individual of
twenty-one (21) years of age or older and contains a photograph or other
likeness of the individual and appears on its face to be valid.
   SAMPLE: A tobacco product or vapor product distributed to members of the
public at no cost for the purpose of promoting the product.
   SAMPLING: The distribution of samples to members of the public in a public
place.
   TOBACCO PRODUCT: Any product that contains tobacco or nicotine and is
intended for human consumption.
   VAPOR PRODUCT: Any noncombustible products, that may or may not contain
nicotine, that employ a mechanical heating element, battery, electronic
circuit, or other mechanism, regardless of shape or size, that can be used to
produce a vapor in a solution or other form. “Vapor products” shall include any
vapor cartridge or other container with or without nicotine or other form that
is intended to be used with an electronic cigarette, electronic cigar,
electronic cigarillo, electronic pipe, or similar product or device and any
vapor cartridge or other container of a solution, that may or may not contain
nicotine, that is intended to be used with or in an electronic cigarette,
electronic cigar, electronic cigarillo or electronic device. “Vapor products”
do not include any products regulated by the United States Food and Drug
Administration under Chapter V of the Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (Ord. 3050,
12-3-1996; amd. Ord. 3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-2: SALE TO MINORS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or furnish in any manner any
tobacco product or vapor product to another person who is under twenty-one (21)
years of age, or to purchase in any manner a tobacco product or vapor product
on behalf of any such person. Provided, however, that it shall not be unlawful
for an employee under twenty-one (21) years of age to handle such products when
required in the performance of the employee's job. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996; Ord.
3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-3: DEMAND PROOF OF AGE:
It shall be unlawful for a person engaged in the sale or distribution of
tobacco products or vapor products not to demand proof of age from a
prospective purchaser or recipient if an ordinary person would conclude on the
basis of appearance that the prospective purchaser may be under twenty-one (21)
years of age. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996; Ord. 3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-4: VIOLATIONS; LIABILITY:
   A.   Fines Imposed For Violations: Any person who violates section
5-2A-2 or
5-2A-3 of this article shall be subject to a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) for
the first offense within a one (1) year period, seventy five dollars ($75.00)
for the second offense within a one (1) year period, and one hundred dollars
($100.00)for a third offense or subsequent offense within a one (1) year
period. Proof that the defendant demanded, was shown, and reasonably relied
upon proof of age shall be a defense to any action brought pursuant to this
subsection. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Violation By Employee: If the sale is made by an employee of the owner
of a store in which tobacco products or vapor products are sold at retail, the
employee shall be guilty of a violation and shall be subject to a fine. (1986
Code § 3050, 12-3-1996)
   C.   Failure To Pay Fine; Suspend Driver's License: Upon failure of the
employee to pay the fine to the city within ninety (90) days of the day of
assessment of such fine, the city shall notify the Oklahoma department of
public safety and said department shall suspend or not issue a driver's license
to said employee until proof of payment has been furnished to said department
of public safety. (1986 Code § 3050, 12-3-1996; amd. 2005 Code)
   D.   Multiple Locations: For the purposes of determining the liability of a
person controlling franchises or business operations in multiple locations, for
any violation of section 5-2A-2 or 5-2A-3 of this article, each individual
franchise or business location shall be deemed a separate entity. (Ord. 3050,
12-3-1996; amd. Ord. 3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-5: VIOLATION BY MINOR:
   A.   Accepting Tobacco Products Or Vapor Products; False Identification: It
is unlawful for any person in the city who is under twenty-one (21) years of
age to purchase, accept receipt of, or have in their possession a tobacco
product or vapor product, or to present or offer to any person any purported
proof of age which is false, fraudulent, or not actually his or her own, for
the purpose of purchasing or receiving any tobacco product or vapor product.
Provided, however, that it shall not be unlawful for employees to handle such
tobacco product or vapor products when required in the performance of the
employee’s job. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996)
   B.   Fines Imposed For Violation: Any person who violates this section shall
be subject to a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) for a first offense within a one
(1) year period, seventy five dollars ($75.00) for a second offense within a
one (1) year period, and one hundred dollars ($100.00) for a third offense or
subsequent offense within a one (1) year period. Upon failure of the individual
to pay such fine within ninety (90) days of the day of such fine, the city
shall notify the Oklahoma department of public safety and said department shall
suspend or not issue a driver's license to said individual until proof of
payment has been furnished to said department of public safety. (Ord. 3050, 12-
3-1996; amd. 2005 Code; Ord. 3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-6: DISTRIBUTING SAMPLES TO MINORS:
   A.   Distributing Prohibited: It shall be unlawful in the city for any
person to distribute tobacco product or vapor products samples to any person
under twenty- one (21) years of age.
   B.   Distributing Near Schools, Playgrounds: Notwithstanding subsection A,
no person shall distribute tobacco product or vapor product samples in the city
in or on any public street, sidewalk, or park that is within three hundred feet
(300') of any playground, school, or other facility where the facility is being
used primarily by persons under eighteen (18) years of age. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-
1996)
   C.   Fines Imposed For Violation: Any person who violates subsection A or B
of this section shall be subject to a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) for the
first offense within a one (1) year period, seventy five dollars ($75.00) for
the second offense within a one (1) year period, and one hundred dollars
($100.00) for a third offense or subsequent offense within the one (1) year
period.
   D.   Failure To Pay Fine; Driver's License Suspension: Upon failure of the
individual to pay the fine provided for in subsection C of this section within
ninety (90) days of the day of such fine, the city shall notify the Oklahoma
department of public safety and said department shall suspend or not issue a
driver's license to said individual until proof of payment has been furnished
to said department of public safety. (Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996; amd. 2005 Code;
Ord. 3855, 11-5-2024)
5-2A-7: CIGARETTE SALES IN ORIGINAL, SEALED PACKAGE:
It is unlawful for any person in the city to sell cigarettes except in the
original, sealed package in which they were placed by the manufacturer. Any
person who violates this section is guilty of an offense, and the city shall
assess such person a fine of two hundred dollars ($200.00) for each offense.
(Ord. 3050, 12-3-1996)
5-2A-8: NO PUBLIC ACCESS:
No public access to tobacco products or vapor products is permitted except for
stores that do not admit persons under twenty-one (21) years of age. (Ord.
3855, 11-5-2024)
CHAPTER 3

5-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, when used in this chapter, have the meanings
prescribed in this section, except in those cases where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
ANIMAL: Any horse, mule, donkey, pony, cow, sheep, goat, swine, dog, cat,
rabbit, chicken, goose, duck, turkey, or other animal or fowl.
ANIMAL SHELTER: A nonprofit establishment providing a temporary home for dogs,
cats and any other animal allowed in the city limits and not otherwise excluded
by ordinance. Animal shelters are entities which provide one or more of the
following: a) provide care and treatment to animals needing protection, b)
attempt to find homes for homeless animals and to reunite lost pets with their
families, and c) provide humane euthanasia for homeless or unadoptable animals.
AT LARGE: Not securely confined by a fence or other means on premises under the
control of, or occupied by, the owner of the animal, and not under the control
of the owner, a member of his immediate family twelve (12) years of age or
older, or an agent of the owner, by leash or otherwise.
CATTERY: Any premises or place where four (4) or more cats are kept over six
(6) months of age. Veterinary clinics shall not fall within this definition.
KENNEL: Any premises or place where four (4) or more dogs are kept over six (6)
months of age. Veterinary clinics shall not fall within this definition.
MENACING BEHAVIOR: An animal, while not under direct control, causes a
reasonable person to believe that an unprovoked attack on a person or on a
domestic animal is imminent.
NONDOMESTIC ANIMAL: Any animal that is not included within the definition of
"animal" listed in this section. Nondomestic animals shall include, but not be
limited to, coyotes, wolves, tigers, lions, bears, elk, moose and deer.
OWNER: Any person, firm or corporation owning, harboring or keeping an animal.
The occupant of any premises on which a domesticated or tamed animal remains,
or to which it customarily returns, for a period of ten (10) days or more, is
deemed to be harboring or keeping the animal.
POTENTIALLY DANGEROUS DOG AND DANGEROUS DOG: Are given the definition as set
forth in 4 Oklahoma Statutes section 44, as it may be amended or replaced from
time to time.
VICIOUS ANIMAL 1 : An animal which has bitten, or attempted to bite, any
person, without undue provocation, or which attacks or assaults any person, or
which has mauled or killed a dog, cat or other domestic animal; provided that
such animal shall not be declared to be vicious or dangerous if the threat,
injury or damage was sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a
wilful trespass or other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner of the
animal, or was tormenting, abusing, or assaulting the animal or has, in the
past, been observed or reported to have tormented, abused, or assaulted the
animal or was committing or attempting to commit a crime. (1986 Code § 3-1;
amd. Ord. 3252, 10-19-2004; Ord. 3449, 11-3-2009; Ord. 3516, 12-20-2011; Ord.
3533, 9-4-2012)
 
Notes
1 1. 4 OS § 46(B).
5-3-2: DOG LICENSE REQUIRED; FEE; VACCINATION:
   A.   License Required; Vaccination: It is unlawful for any person to keep or
harbor any dog over six (6) months old within the city without having first
obtained a license therefor. The license shall be issued by the city clerk upon
presentation of a certificate by a licensed veterinarian stating that the dog
has been vaccinated against rabies.
   B.   License Fee; Term: The fee for the license shall be ten dollars
($10.00) and the license shall be valid for the remainder of the calendar year
for which it is purchased. In the event the fees herein provided for are not
paid on or before January 31 of each year, the fee shall double for each dog
registered. This penalty provision shall not apply to dogs registered within
sixty (60) days from the date such dog is brought into the city, or within
sixty (60) days from the date such dog becomes six (6) months of age. (Ord.
3449, 11-3-2009)
   C.   License Tag Attached To Collar: The city clerk shall issue to the
licensee a metal tag. The licensee shall be required to provide each dog with a
collar to which the license tag must be affixed, and shall see that the collar
and tag are continually worn. (Ord. 3465, 4-20-2010)
   D.   Duplicate Tag; Fee: In case a tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate
shall be issued by the city clerk upon presentation of a receipt showing the
payment of the license fee and upon payment of a five dollar ($5.00) fee for
such duplicate.
   E.   Tags Nontransferable: Dog tags shall not be transferable from one dog
to another.
   F.   Contents Of Application For License: At the time application is made
for the license and upon forms provided for such purpose, the applicant shall
show his name and address and the name, breed, color, and sex of each dog owned
or kept by him.
   G.   Exceptions To Licensing Provisions: The provisions of this section
shall not apply to dogs whose owners are nonresidents temporarily within the
city for less than five (5) days. (Ord. 3449, 11-3-2009)
5-3-3: ANIMAL SHELTERS, KENNELS AND CATTERIES:
   A.   Animal Shelters; Licensing For Private Shelters:
      1.   The city has previously established a municipal animal shelter
(a.k.a., pound). Such shelter, and any future shelters established by the city,
shall be under the control of the animal control supervisor who shall be the
chief of police, or his designee. The animal control supervisor shall provide
proper sustenance for all animals impounded and shall treat them in a humane
manner. The animal control supervisor shall also ensure compliance of the
shelter facility with all applicable local, county, state and federal laws,
rules and/or regulations.
      2.   The city may also contract for the use of an animal shelter
maintained by another governmental entity, or private party, approved by the
city council.
      3.   All private animal shelters shall apply for a license from the city,
and pay a fee of five dollars ($5.00) therefor. Thereafter, all private animal
shelters shall apply for and pay an annual renewal fee of five dollars ($5.00).
Government owned animal shelters and veterinarian clinics are exempt from the
licensing requirement.
   B.   Kennels And Catteries:
      1.   Permits: It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a kennel or
cattery without first procuring a license from the city to operate the kennel
or cattery. Each day an unlicensed kennel or cattery is in operation is
considered to be a separate violation. All veterinary hospitals shall be exempt
from the payment of kennel or cattery license fees.
      2.   Permit Fees; Annual Renewal: Each applicant for a kennel or a
cattery shall pay an application fee of five dollars ($5.00), and an initial
licensing fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00). Prior to obtaining the license,
a kennel owner shall have each dog licensed, tagged, and vaccinated. Prior to
obtaining a license, each cattery must have each cat vaccinated. If the
application is approved, the clerk shall issue a license renewable January 1 of
each year upon payment of a fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00).
      3.   Inspection Required: Prior to the issuance of a permit, the kennel
or cattery site shall be inspected to ensure compliance with the proper care
and sanitary requirements contained herein, and to ensure that such facilities
are designed to prohibit animals from being at large within the city.
      4.   Vaccination Required: All dogs and cats kept in kennels or
