properly equipped, and/or whether its equipment is in proper adjustment and
repair. (1986 Code § 20-19)
6-6-7: JAKE BRAKES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful and an offense within the city limits for any
person, firm or corporation to use vehicle or trailer brakes which create an
excessive or unusual noise such as is created by the use of "jake" brakes.
   B.   Any person, firm, association, corporation or copartnership, who shall
violate any of the provisions hereof shall be deemed guilty of an offense and
upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed one
hundred dollars ($100.00) plus court costs. (Ord. 3197, 11-19-2002)
CHAPTER 7
PEDESTRIANS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Subject To Traffic Control Signals
6-7-2: Right Of Way In Crosswalks
6-7-3: Crossing At Right Angles
6-7-4: Yield By Pedestrians
6-7-5: Prohibited Crossing
6-7-6: Railroad Signals
6-7-7: Walking Along Roadways
6-7-8: Soliciting Rides Or Business
6-7-9: Drivers To Exercise Due Care
6-7-1: SUBJECT TO TRAFFIC CONTROL SIGNALS:
Pedestrians shall be subject to traffic control signals as provided for in
chapter 3 of this title, but at all other places pedestrians shall be granted
those rights and be subject to the restrictions stated in this chapter. (1986
Code § 20-79)
6-7-2: RIGHT OF WAY IN CROSSWALKS:
   A.   Driver Yield To Pedestrian:
      1.   When traffic control signals are not in place or not in operation,
the driver of a vehicle shall yield the right of way, slowing down or stopping
if need be to so yield, to a pedestrian crossing the roadway within a crosswalk
when the pedestrian is upon the half of the roadway upon which the vehicle is
traveling, or when the pedestrian is approaching so closely from the opposite
half of the roadway as to be in danger.
      2.   This subsection shall not apply under the conditions stated in
subsection
6-7-4B of this chapter.
   B.   Pedestrian Suddenly Leaving Curb: No pedestrian shall suddenly leave a
curb or other place of safety and walk or run into the path of a vehicle which
is so close that it is impossible for the driver to yield.
   C.   Vehicle Approaching From Rear Of Stopped Vehicle: Whenever any vehicle
is stopped at a marked crosswalk or at any unmarked crosswalk at an
intersection to permit a pedestrian to cross the roadway, the driver of any
other vehicle approaching from the rear shall not overtake and pass such
stopped vehicle. (1986 Code § 20-80)
   D.   Use Right Half Of Crosswalks: Pedestrians shall move, whenever
practicable, upon the right half of crosswalks. (1986 Code § 20-81)
6-7-3: CROSSING AT RIGHT ANGLES:
No pedestrians shall cross a roadway at any place other than by route at right
angles to the curb or by the shortest route to the opposite curb, except within
a crosswalk. (1986 Code § 20-82)
6-7-4: YIELD BY PEDESTRIANS:
   A.   Crossing At Other Than Crosswalk: Every pedestrian crossing a roadway
at any point other than within a marked crosswalk or within an unmarked
crosswalk at an intersection shall yield the right of way to all vehicles upon
the roadway.
   B.   Tunnel Or Overhead Crossing: Any pedestrian crossing a roadway at a
point where a pedestrian tunnel or overhead pedestrian crossing has been
provided shall yield the right of way to all vehicles upon the roadway.
   C.   Exception: The foregoing rules in this section have no application
under the conditions stated in section
6-7-5 of this chapter, when pedestrians are prohibited from crossing at certain
designated places. (1986 Code § 20-83)
6-7-5: PROHIBITED CROSSING:
Between adjacent intersections at which traffic control signals are in
operation, pedestrians shall not cross at any place except in a crosswalk.
(1986 Code § 20-84)
6-7-6: RAILROAD SIGNALS:
No pedestrian shall pass through, around, over, or under any crossing, gate or
barrier at a railroad grade crossing while such gate or barrier is closed or is
being opened or closed. (1986 Code § 20-85)
6-7-7: WALKING ALONG ROADWAYS:
   A.   Use Of Sidewalks: Where sidewalks are provided, it is unlawful for any
pedestrian to walk along and upon an adjacent roadway.
   B.   Use Of Shoulder; Left Side: Where sidewalks are not provided, any
pedestrian walking along and upon a highway shall when practicable walk only on
the left side of the roadway or its shoulder facing traffic which may approach
from the opposite direction, and shall yield to approaching vehicles. (1986
Code § 20-86)
6-7-8: SOLICITING RIDES OR BUSINESS:
   A.   No person shall stand in a roadway for the purpose of soliciting a
ride, donation, employment, or business from the occupant of any vehicle.
   B.   No person shall stand on or in proximity to a street or highway for the
purpose of soliciting the watching or guarding of any vehicle while parked or
about to be parked on a street or highway. (1986 Code § 20-87)
6-7-9: DRIVERS TO EXERCISE DUE CARE:
Notwithstanding the foregoing provisions of this chapter, every driver of a
vehicle shall exercise due care to avoid colliding with any pedestrian upon any
roadway, and shall give warning by sounding the horn when necessary, and shall
exercise proper precaution upon observing any child or any confused or
incapacitated person upon a roadway. (1986 Code § 20-88)
CHAPTER 8
BICYCLES AND MOTORCYCLES
SECTION:
6-8-1: Effect Of Regulations
6-8-2: Traffic Laws Apply
6-8-3: Obedience To Traffic Control Devices
6-8-4: Riding On Bicycles
6-8-5: Riding On Roadways And Bicycle Paths
6-8-6: Speed
6-8-7: Emerging From Alley Or Driveway
6-8-8: Carrying Articles
6-8-9: Parking
6-8-10: Riding On Sidewalk
6-8-11: Lamps And Other Equipment
6-8-12: Motorcycles And Motor Scooters
6-8-1: EFFECT OF REGULATIONS:
   A.   Compliance Required: It is an offense for any person to do any act
forbidden or fail to perform any act required in this chapter.
   B.   Parental Responsibility: The parent of any child and the guardian of
any ward shall not authorize or knowingly permit any such child or ward to
violate any of the provisions of this chapter.
   C.   Application Of Regulations: These regulations applicable to bicycles
shall apply whenever a bicycle is operated upon any highway or upon any path
set aside for the exclusive use of bicycles subject to the exceptions stated
herein. (1986 Code § 20-89)
6-8-2: TRAFFIC LAWS APPLY:
Every person riding a bicycle upon a roadway shall be granted all of the rights
and shall be subject to all of the duties applicable to the driver of a vehicle
by the laws of this state declaring rules of the road applicable to vehicles or
by the traffic ordinances of the city applicable to the driver of a vehicle,
except as to special regulations in this chapter and except as to those
provisions of laws and ordinances which by their nature can have no
application. (1986 Code § 20-90)
6-8-3: OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
   A.   Obey Signs And Signals: Any person operating a bicycle shall obey the
instructions of official traffic control signals, signs, and other control
devices applicable to vehicles, unless otherwise directed by a police officer.
   B.   Turn Signs: Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating that no
right or left or U-turn is permitted, no person operating a bicycle shall
disobey the direction of any such sign, except where such person dismounts from
the bicycle to make any such turn, in which event such person shall then obey
the regulations applicable to pedestrians. (1986 Code § 20-91)
6-8-4: RIDING ON BICYCLES:
   A.   Use Of Seat: A person propelling a bicycle shall not ride other than
astride a permanent and regular seat attached thereto.
   B.   Carrying Persons: No bicycle shall be used to carry more persons at one
time than the number for which it is designed and equipped. (1986 Code § 20-92)
6-8-5: RIDING ON ROADWAYS AND BICYCLE PATHS:
   A.   Roadway: Every person operating a bicycle upon a roadway shall ride as
near to the right side of the roadway as practicable, exercising due care when
passing a standing vehicle or one proceeding in the same direction.
   B.   Multiple Persons Riding: Persons riding bicycles upon a roadway shall
not ride more than two (2) abreast except on paths or parts of roadways set
aside for the exclusive use of bicycles.
   C.   Bicycle Paths: Wherever a usable path for bicycles has been provided
adjacent to a roadway, bicycle riders shall use such path and shall not use the
roadway. (1986 Code § 20-93)
6-8-6: SPEED:
No person shall operate a bicycle at a speed greater than is reasonable and
prudent under the conditions then existing. (1986 Code § 20-94)
6-8-7: EMERGING FROM ALLEY OR DRIVEWAY:
The operator of a bicycle emerging from an alley, driveway, or building shall,
upon approaching a sidewalk or the sidewalk area extending across any alleyway,
yield the right of way to all pedestrians approaching on the sidewalk or
sidewalk area, and upon entering the roadway shall yield the right of way to
all vehicles approaching on the roadway. (1986 Code § 20-95)
6-8-8: CARRYING ARTICLES:
No person operating a bicycle shall carry any package, bundle, or article which
prevents the rider from keeping at least one hand upon the handlebars. (1986
Code § 20-96)
6-8-9: PARKING:
No person shall park a bicycle upon a street other than upon the roadway
against the curb, or upon the sidewalk in a rack to support the bicycle, or
against a building or at the curb, in such manner as to afford the least
obstruction to pedestrian traffic. (1986 Code § 20-97)
6-8-10: RIDING ON SIDEWALK:
   A.   Business District, Riding Prohibited: No person shall ride a bicycle
upon a sidewalk within a business district.
   B.   Signs Prohibiting; Compliance: The city council, by motion or
resolution, is authorized to have erected signs on any sidewalk or roadway
prohibiting the riding of bicycles thereon by any person; and when such signs
are in place, no person shall disobey the same.
   C.   Yield To Pedestrians: Whenever any person is riding a bicycle upon a
sidewalk, such person shall yield the right of way to any pedestrian and shall
give audible signal before overtaking and passing such pedestrian. (1986 Code §
20-98)
6-8-11: LAMPS AND OTHER EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Lights: Every bicycle in use at nighttime shall be equipped with a lamp
on the front which shall emit a white light visible from a distance of at least
three hundred feet (300') to the front and with a red reflector on the rear of
a type which shall be visible from all distances from fifty feet (50') to three
hundred feet (300') to the rear when directly in front of lawful upper beams of
headlamps on a motor vehicle. A lamp emitting a red light visible from a
distance of three hundred feet (300') to the rear may be used in addition to
the red reflector.
   B.   Brake: Every bicycle shall be equipped with a brake which will enable
the operator to make the braked wheel skid on dry, level, clean pavement. (1986
Code § 20-99; amd. 2005 Code)
6-8-12: MOTORCYCLES AND MOTOR SCOOTERS:
   A.   Riding Restrictions; Vehicle Specifications:
      1.   Use Of Seat; Carrying Passengers:
         a.   A person operating a motorcycle, motor scooter, or a motor
bicycle shall ride only upon the permanent and regular seat attached thereto,
and such operator shall not carry any other person nor shall any other person
ride on the vehicle unless it is designed to carry more than one person, in
which event a passenger may ride only upon the permanent and regular seat if
designed for two (2) persons, or upon another seat firmly attached thereto, at
the rear or side of the operator. (1986 Code § 20-66; amd. 2005 Code)
         b.   No driver of a two (2) or three (3) wheel motor vehicle shall
carry any other person on, upon or within such vehicle on any street, alley or
highway within the city, except as hereafter provided; provided, however, that
if any two (2) or three (3) wheel motor vehicle with a wheel diameter of twelve
inches (12") or greater shall have either a double seating device with double
footrests or a sidecar attachment providing a separate seat space within such
sidecar attachment for each person riding therein so that such person shall be
seated entirely within the body of said sidecar, then it shall be permissible
for an operator who has attained the age of sixteen (16) years or older to
carry a passenger.
      2.   Demonstration Ride: A demonstration ride by a licensed dealer or his
employee is excepted from the provisions hereof.
      3.   Riding On Sidewalks: No motorcycle or motor scooter shall be ridden
upon any sidewalk of the city.
      4.   Handlebars: Handlebars on motorcycles and motor scooters shall not
exceed twelve inches (12") in height, measured from the crown or point of
attachment.
      5.   Holding Onto Other Vehicles: No rider of a motorcycle or motor
scooter shall hold onto any moving vehicle for the purpose of being propelled.
      6.   Passing Between Lanes: No driver of a motorcycle or motor scooter
shall pass other vehicles in between lanes of traffic traveling in the same
direction; authorized emergency vehicles excepted. (1986 Code § 20-124)
      7.   Operation Of Motor Scooters: It is unlawful for any person to
operate a motor driven cycle, including a motor scooter or motor driven
bicycle, on a street in the city during a time when state law prohibits the
operation of such vehicle. (1986 Code § 20-75)
   B.   Speed: No person shall operate any motorcycle, motor driven cycle,
motor scooter, or any other similar two (2) or three (3) wheel motor vehicle at
a speed greater than the speed limit provided by ordinance of the city for
automobiles or other motor vehicles nor at a speed greater than thirty five
(35) miles per hour. (1986 Code § 20-125)
   C.   Equipment: The following equipment shall be required on all motorcycles
and all motor scooters being operated and driven in the city:
      1.   Rear View Mirrors: All vehicles covered under this section shall be
equipped with two (2) mirrors, containing a reflection surface of not less than
three inches (3") in diameter, mounted one on each side of the vehicle and
positioned so as to enable the operator to clearly view the roadway for a
distance of two hundred feet (200') to the rear of his vehicle.
      2.   Windshield: All vehicles covered under this section shall be
equipped with a windshield of sufficient quality, size and thickness to protect
the operator from foreign objects, except that in lieu of such windshield, the
operator shall wear goggles or face shield of material and design to protect
him from foreign objects.
      3.   Brakes; Lamp:
         a.   All vehicles covered under this section shall be equipped with
brakes adequate to control the movement of same to stop and hold such vehicles,
including two (2) separate means of applying the brakes; one means shall be
effective to apply brakes to the front wheel and one means shall apply the
brakes to the rear wheels.
         b.   All such vehicles shall be equipped with a stop lamp on the rear
of the vehicle, which shall display a red or amber light, or any shade of color
between red and amber, visible from a distance of not less than one hundred
feet (100') to the rear in normal sunlight, and which shall be actuated upon
application of the service brake.
      4.   Speedometer: All vehicles covered under this section shall be
equipped with a properly operating speedometer capable of registering at least
the maximum legal speed limit for that vehicle.
      5.   Fenders: All vehicles covered under this section shall be equipped
with a fender over each wheel. All fenders shall be of the type provided by the
manufacturer.
      6.   Lights: All vehicles covered under this section shall carry at least
one lighted headlamp capable of showing a white light visible at least three
hundred feet (300') in the direction in which the same are proceeding, and one
tail lamp mounted on the rear which, when lighted, shall emit a red light
plainly visible from at least three hundred feet (300') to the rear, and such
lights required by this section shall be burning whenever such vehicles are in
motion during the period from one-half (1/2) hour after sunset and one-half (1/
2) hour before sunrise and at any other time when, due to insufficient light or
unfavorable atmospheric conditions, persons and vehicles on the street are not
clearly discernible at a distance of at least five hundred feet (500') ahead.
      7.   Headgear: No person under twenty one (21) years of age shall operate
or ride upon any vehicle covered under this section unless such person is
equipped with and wearing on his head a crash helmet of the type and design
manufactured for use by the operators of such vehicle. All crash helmets shall
consist of lining, padding and chin straps and be of the type as not to distort
the view of the driver.
      8.   Mufflers: It shall be an offense to operate a vehicle covered under
this section with the exhaust system modified so that motor noise is increased
greater than that of the original muffler equipment provided by the
manufacturers of the vehicle. (1986 Code § 20-126)
   D.   Persons Under Sixteen; Hours: The operation of motorcycles, motor
driven cycles, motor scooters, or other similar two (2) or three (3) wheel
motor vehicles within the corporate limits of the city is prohibited for
persons under sixteen (16) years of age between the hours of eleven o'clock
(11:00) P.M. and five thirty o'clock (5:30) A.M. (1986 Code § 20-127; amd. 2005
Code)
CHAPTER 9
IMPOUNDING VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-9-1: Authority To Impound Vehicles
6-9-2: Impounding For Certain Causes
6-9-3: Nuisance; Penalty
6-9-1: AUTHORITY TO IMPOUND VEHICLES:
Members of the police department are hereby authorized to remove a vehicle from
a street or highway to the nearest garage or other place of safety, or to a
garage designated or maintained by the police department, or otherwise
maintained by the city, under the circumstances hereinafter enumerated:
   A.   Bridge, Viaduct: When any vehicle is left unattended upon any bridge,
viaduct, or causeway, or in any tube or tunnel where such vehicle constitutes
an obstruction to traffic.
   B.   Disabled Vehicle: When a vehicle upon a highway is so disabled as to
constitute an obstruction to traffic and the person or persons in charge of the
vehicle are by reason of physical injury incapacitated to such an extent as to
be unable to provide for its custody or removal.
   C.   Illegally Parked: When any vehicle is left unattended upon a street and
is so parked illegally as to constitute a definite hazard or obstruction to the
normal movement of traffic. (1986 Code § 20-129)
6-9-2: IMPOUNDING FOR CERTAIN CAUSES:
From and after the effective date hereof, the chief of police shall be
authorized and directed to cause the impoundment, in any public or private
storage yard or place, of vehicles under the following circumstances:
   A.   Private Property With Owner Consent: When such vehicle is parked on
private property without the consent first had and obtained of the owner,
occupant, or person in charge of said private property, and after complaint in
written form signed by said owner, occupant, or person in charge of such
property.
   B.   Blocking Driveway, Alley: When any such vehicle is found parked in
front of, or blocking, any private driveway or public alley.
   C.   Between Curb And Street: When such vehicle is found parked between the
curb of a public street and a private property line, unless permitted under
this city code.
   D.   Delinquent Parking Tickets: When such vehicle has had issued against it
ten (10) or more parking tickets, which parking tickets are delinquent and
unpaid on the date of such impoundment. (1986 Code § 20-130)
6-9-3: NUISANCE; PENALTY:
Any owner of a vehicle found in violation of any provision of section
6-9-2 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of creating a public nuisance,
which said violation is hereby declared to be, and, upon plea of guilty or
conviction therefor, shall be fined the sum of fifty dollars ($50.00), which
shall be in addition to any other penalties lawfully assessed against said
owner. (1986 Code § 20-132; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 10
ABANDONED VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-10-1: Definitions
6-10-2: Abandonment Of Vehicles
6-10-3: Authority To Impound
6-10-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement of
this chapter:
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
PROPERTY: Any real property within the city which is not a street, highway or
alleyway.
STREET OR HIGHWAY: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for
purposes of vehicular travel.
VEHICLE: A machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel
along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners, or slides and transport
persons or property or pull machinery and shall include, without limitation,
automobiles, trucks, trailers, motorcycles and tractors. (1986 Code § 20-133)
6-10-2: ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES:
No person shall abandon any vehicle within the city, and no person shall leave
any vehicle at any place within the city for such time and under such
circumstances as to cause such vehicle reasonably to appear to have been
abandoned. (1986 Code § 20-134)
6-10-3: AUTHORITY TO IMPOUND:
The chief of police, or any other member of his department designated by him is
hereby authorized to remove or have removed any vehicle left at any place
within the city which reasonably appears to be in violation of this chapter,
lost, stolen or unclaimed. Such vehicles shall be impounded by the chief of
police or any member of his department. (1986 Code § 20-136; amd. 2005 Code)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Trees And Shrubbery
7-1-2: Obstructing Public Ways
7-1-3: Deposits Of Trash, Weeds
7-1-4: Assemblies Obstructing Public Ways
7-1-5: Drainage On Streets; Pipes And Culverts
7-1-6: Playing On Streets And Sidewalks
7-1-7: Washing Vehicles; Filling Station Drainage
7-1-8: Driving On Newly Paved Streets
7-1-9: Electric Light And Telephone Poles
7-1-10: Penalty
7-1-1: TREES AND SHRUBBERY:
   A.   Trees Permitted On Residential Streets: Permission is hereby given to
any owner, lessee or occupant of any property abutting on any residential
street to set out and grow any kind of tree for shade purposes between the
property line and the curb line of such property line, such trees to be set on
a line or lines running parallel with the line of such property, and shall not
be set or grown in any other place or in any other manner. (1986 Code § 19-1)
   B.   Decayed Trees Removed: All decayed, dead or broken trees, and all dead,
decayed or broken parts of trees, which are unsightly and liable to fall or be
blown down, and which are standing near any sidewalk in the city, shall be
removed by the owner or occupant or person having charge of the adjacent
property or the property on which same are located. (1986 Code § 19-2)
   C.   Trimming Trees And Shrubbery:
      1.   The owner of any premises abutting on any street in the city shall
trim all trees and shrubbery growing in the parking, between the sidewalk and
the roadway of any such street, and all trees and shrubbery growing on any part
of the premises adjacent to the sidewalk or any street or alley, in such manner
that the boughs or limbs thereof shall not obstruct free and convenient passage
and travel along the streets, sidewalks, and alleys.
      2.   When such premises are occupied by some person other than the owner,
such occupant shall trim the trees and shrubbery in the same manner as
hereinbefore required of the owner.
      3.   Such trees and shrubbery shall be trimmed so that the lowest
branches or foliage shall not be lower than ten feet (10') above the roadway of
a street or alley, nor lower than eight feet (8') above the sidewalk. (1986
Code § 19-3)
      4.   Any owner or occupant who shall fail, refuse or neglect to trim
trees and shrubbery as provided in this subsection, after receiving five (5)
days' notice from the superintendent of streets to do so, shall be guilty of an
offense against the city. Every day that the said owner or occupant shall fail,
refuse or neglect to trim said trees or shrubbery, after the expiration of the
five (5) days' notice, shall be a separate offense. (1986 Code § 19-4)
   D.   Injuring Trees And Shrubbery: It is unlawful for any person to injure
any tree or shrubbery on a street or alley in the city; provided, that this
shall not prohibit the lawful and proper care and removal of such trees and
shrubbery. (1986 Code § 19-5)
7-1-2: OBSTRUCTING PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   Merchandise: It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
place upon the sidewalks, parkways, streets and alleys of the city any goods,
wares, articles or merchandise or any other obstruction, and leave same
thereon; or to use the same as a place to carry on a business or trade. (1986
Code § 19-6)
   B.   Interference With Pedestrians Or Traffic: It is unlawful for any
person, firm or corporation to use or obstruct the sidewalks of the city in any
manner so as to interfere unduly with pedestrian traffic thereon, or to use or
obstruct the streets and alleys of the city in any manner so as to interfere
unduly with lawful traffic and parking thereon. (1986 Code § 19-7)
7-1-3: DEPOSITS OF TRASH, WEEDS:
It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to deposit, throw or sweep
into or upon the streets, alleys, parking or sidewalks of the city any paper,
rubbish, grass, weeds, tree trimmings, dirt, trash, crates, boxes or other
refuse of any kind. (1986 Code § 19-8)
7-1-4: ASSEMBLIES OBSTRUCTING PUBLIC WAYS:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to obstruct the free use of any
street, alley, sidewalk or other public way or walk by congregating or
assembling thereon. (1986 Code § 19-9)
7-1-5: DRAINAGE ON STREETS; PIPES AND CULVERTS:
   A.   Water Flowing Into Storm Drains:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to obstruct
any street, sidewalk or alley within the city, by placing any approach driveway
or other obstruction or substance whatever that will obstruct or prevent the
natural flow of water into the storm sewers or drains or dam the same so as to
back any water upon the streets, alleys, sidewalks or gutter.
      2.   Any such obstruction is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and the
street department may abate it at any time, either with or without notice to
owners or occupants of abutting property owners. (1986 Code § 19-10)
   B.   Drainage Tiles; Size, Permit:
      1.   Size: No person shall install or lay any drainage pipe or culvert of
less than twelve inch (12") diameter in the construction, repair, or alteration
of any driveway, sidewalk or other private way, which said drainage pipe or
culvert when installed will be upon public property, with the exception that
ten inch (10") diameter steel or equivalent metal pipe or culverts may be used
in flat areas of the city where adjoining drainage ditches are not sufficiently
deep that any advantage could be gained from larger pipe or culverts.
      2.   Materials: All drainage pipes or culverts so installed in the city
shall be either of steel or equivalent metal or concrete construction.
      3.   Permit: Such person shall first obtain a permit from the city clerk
with the approval of the street superintendent for work to be done. The word
"person" as it appears herein shall mean person, firm, association,
corporation, partnership or other group of persons. (1986 Code § 19-11)
      4.   Inspection: It shall be the duty of the street superintendent to
inspect each and every drainage tile installed within the corporate limits of
the city, which installations are governed by the provisions of this
subsection, and to enforce the provisions thereof. (1986 Code § 19-12)
7-1-6: PLAYING ON STREETS AND SIDEWALKS:
It is unlawful for any person to play on the sidewalks or upon the main
travelled portion of the streets and alleys of the city, except as may be
authorized by ordinance. (1986 Code § 19-13)
7-1-7: WASHING VEHICLES; FILLING STATION DRAINAGE:
   A.   Washing Vehicles On Street: The washing of an automobile or other
vehicle in any street of the city is hereby prohibited. (1986 Code § 19-14)
   B.   Water, Mud Draining Onto Street: No automobile or other vehicle shall
be washed at any place within the city where the water, dirt, mud or other
substances removed therefrom by or during the washing thereof shall drain into
or upon any street or sidewalk of the city. (1986 Code § 19-15)
   C.   Filling Stations And Other Businesses: It is unlawful for any owner or
operator of a filling station or other place of business, or any agent or
employee thereof, to cause or allow water, grease or other fluid to flow or
drain into, upon, over or across any sidewalk, parking, street, alley or other
public way. (1986 Code § 19-16)
7-1-8: DRIVING ON NEWLY PAVED STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride or drive any animal, or to drive
any vehicle over any newly paved street, venue or alley in the city before such
paving shall have been accepted by the city, and before the same shall have
been formally opened by the city for public travel thereon. Provided, the
contractor or other person having charge of such paving shall erect and
maintain barriers at the end of the streets, avenues and alleys on which such
paving is being done, as well as at all street intersections thereon. (1986
Code § 19-17)
7-1-9: ELECTRIC LIGHT AND TELEPHONE POLES:
   A.   Placement In Alleys: All electric light and telephone poles hereafter
erected, set or reset shall be erected and set in the alleys of the city, and
in no case shall the same be erected or set upon the streets or parkways of the
city. (1986 Code § 19-60)
   B.   Height Of Poles: All telephone poles and electric light poles hereafter
erected or set in the alleys or on the public grounds of the city shall be of
good quality and of sufficient height that the wire strung thereon shall be at
least thirty feet (30') above the level of the ground. (1986 Code § 19-61)
7-1-10: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any provision of this chapter
by doing any act prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or declared to
be an offense or misdemeanor thereby, or who shall fail to do any act required
by any such provision, or who shall fail to do any act such provision declares
such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor, shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor; and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided
in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which any such violation continues shall
constitute a separate misdemeanor. (1986 Code § 19-62; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 2
EXCAVATIONS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Compliance; Permit Required
7-2-2: Cash Deposit Required
7-2-3: Duty Of Street Superintendent
7-2-4: Replacing Street Surface
7-2-5: Safeguards
7-2-6: Bridge For Pedestrians
7-2-7: Penalty
7-2-1: COMPLIANCE; PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   Compliance Required: No person shall excavate, dig in, alter or change
or interfere with any street, avenue, alley, sidewalk, pavement, curbing or
other public ground or the surface thereof, within the limits of the City, for
any purpose whatsoever, unless the provisions of this chapter have been
complied with.
   B.   Permit: Such person shall first obtain a permit from the City Clerk
with the approval of the Street Superintendent for such work to be done. The
word "person" as it appears herein shall mean person, firm, association,
corporation, partnership or other group of persons. (1986 Code § 19-18)
7-2-2: CASH DEPOSIT REQUIRED:
   A.   Deposit Required; Amount:
      1.   It is hereby required of all persons, before the issuance of a
permit for doing of any such work as described in section
7-2-1 of this chapter, that they deposit with the City Clerk in cash, a sum to
cover the cost of replacement and repair of any such street, avenue, alley,
sidewalk, pavement, or other public ground of the City and the surface thereof
in the same condition as the same was prior to the time of doing any work as
described in section
7-2-1 of this chapter. (1986 Code § 19-19)
      2.   The amount of such cash deposit shall be five hundred dollars
($500.00). (1986 Code § 19-19; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Authority To Alter Deposit Amount: Provided, however, that the amount
of the cash deposit above required is for normal or ordinary excavations and
the Street Superintendent may make adjustments in the amount of such cash
deposit when conditions, including width or area of excavation, are such that
the cost of making repairs and replacements of such excavations or alterations,
including surfaces, shall be less than or greater than the cost for the usual,
normal or ordinary excavations or alterations. (1986 Code § 19-19)
7-2-3: DUTY OF STREET SUPERINTENDENT:
All such street excavation work shall be done under the supervision of the
Street Superintendent. The cash or bond shall be returned, upon performance of
the work as herein required, in a reasonable time. The Street Superintendent
shall utilize such portion of the cash deposit or bond as may be necessary for
the purpose of restoring said places to their former condition. (1986 Code §
19-22)
7-2-4: REPLACING STREET SURFACE:
All excavations conducted on City property or easements must be conducted under
the supervision of a properly licensed plumbing contractor and conform to the
following minimum standards:
   A.   All excavated material (i.e., spoil material) must be removed from the
work site.
   B.   All excavations must be backfilled from the bottom thereof to ground
level with aggregate base rock (i.e., less than 3/4 inch size rock or gravel)
at the conclusion of the excavation operation, after which such fill material
shall be firmly tamped, and the surface of any affected street, avenue or alley
returned to a durable, smooth and serviceable condition as good or better than
before such work was done, with such work to be conducted under the supervision
of the Street Commissioner.
   C.   The Vinita Street Commissioner (918) 256-6468 must be contacted prior
to all excavations so as to enable him to determine in advance whether the
amount of the cash deposit as required under section
7-2-2 of this chapter, is adequate to cover any costs to the City for manpower
or resources.
Failure to comply with the minimum standards set forth hereinabove will result
in suspension of all permit privileges authorizing operations within the City
limits of the City of Vinita as follows:
 
First violation  30 day suspension of all licenses and privileges to conduct
                 operations within the City of Vinita
Second violation 90 day suspension of all license and permit privileges to
                 conduct operations within the City of Vinita
Third violation  1 year suspension of all license and permit privileges to
                 conduct operations within the City of Vinita
 
Any plumbing contractor found to be operating in the City of Vinita in the
absence of valid licenses as required by both the State of Oklahoma and the
City of Vinita, will be reported to the State regulators. (Ord. 3675, 3-6-2018)
7-2-5: SAFEGUARDS:
It is hereby made the duty of any person, during any excavation, to safely
guard the public against any and all accidents liable to occur as a result of
the same, by providing suitable and adequate warning signs, lights, safeguards,
railings, and guard devices around any such excavations, ditches, or trenches.
From sunset to sunrise, such person shall maintain a sufficient number of red
lights or torches on each side of such excavations, trenches, or ditches as is
necessary to give adequate and suitable warning of danger. (1986 Code § 19-21)
7-2-6: BRIDGE FOR PEDESTRIANS:
   A.   Bridge Required: Any person authorized to do any work described in this
chapter must, at the time of the excavation and until the place is restored to
its original condition, construct and maintain an appropriate bridge across
said work for the passage of pedestrians at all times. At night such persons
shall place and maintain a red light on each side of said bridge to warn the
public, and said bridge shall have banisters or guard rails, if any ditch is
left open on either side. Torches may be used in place of the red lights herein
required. (1986 Code § 19-23)
   B.   Red Lights Placed Along Ditch: In all cases where the ditch or
excavation runs parallel with the street either to the sidewalk in the street
or a driveway, a red light shall be placed not less than twenty five feet (25')
apart all along said ditch. Said lights shall be maintained from sunset until
sunrise. (1986 Code § 19-24)
7-2-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
7-1-10 of this title. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 3
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION; STREET SPECIFICATIONS
SECTION:
7-3-1: Applicability Of Regulations
7-3-2: Specifications Furnished By Engineer
7-3-3: Keeping Sidewalks In Repair
7-3-4: Payment Of Costs
7-3-5: Construction, Line And Grade
7-3-6: Excavations
7-3-7: Embankment
7-3-8: Materials; Mixing
7-3-9: Finish
7-3-10: Sidewalk And Curbing Requirements
7-3-11: Asphaltic Concrete Specifications
7-3-12: Portland Cement Specifications
7-3-13: Sidewalks Laid In Violation Of Chapter
7-3-14: Condemnation By Council
7-3-15: Penalty
7-3-1: APPLICABILITY OF REGULATIONS:
Whenever the city council shall order any sidewalk to be constructed or
repaired, the same shall be constructed or repaired in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter. (1986 Code § 19-47)
7-3-2: SPECIFICATIONS FURNISHED BY ENGINEER:
In any and all cases where this chapter fails to provide proper specifications
for a sidewalk, areas, curbing and guttering, the city engineer shall furnish
specifications which shall be approved by the mayor and city council. (1986
Code § 19-53; amd. 2005 Code)
7-3-3: KEEPING SIDEWALKS IN REPAIR:
It shall be the duty of every person, firm or corporation owning property in
the city to keep the sidewalk adjoining his lot or lots in repair and in a safe
condition for the public use and travel and to not permit or suffer the same to
become broken, unsafe or out of repair. (1986 Code § 19-57)
7-3-4: PAYMENT OF COSTS:
   A.   Pavement: The entire walk and excavation or embankment to be paid for
will be paid for as per contract to be entered into with the city. (1986 Code §
19-36)
   B.   Extra Work: Any extra work required by the city engineer shall a paid
for at the rate of the actual cost plus fifteen percent (15%) thereof. (1986
Code § 19-37; amd. 2005 Code)
7-3-5: CONSTRUCTION, LINE AND GRADE:
   A.   Construction; Supervision: All sidewalks, curbs, gutters and private
crossings shall be constructed of cement, asphalt or other substance or
material that will make and produce a hard, smooth surface, and be constructed
under the supervision of the street superintendent of the city. (1986 Code §
19-25)
   B.   Line And Grade: All work shall be completed in a workmanlike manner
according to lines and grades as given by the city engineer, and work shall be
commenced and carried on at a point or points designated by said engineer.
(1986 Code § 19-26)
7-3-6: EXCAVATIONS:
   A.   Manner Of Making Excavations; Classifications: Excavations shall be
made to a point exactly four inches (4") below the finished grade of the
sidewalk. After excavations are made, the surface shall be tamped thoroughly,
with a tamper that shall weigh not less than twenty (20) pounds and be not less
than twelve inches (12") square, to the satisfaction of the engineer. All
excavations shall be measured and estimated, by the cubic yards, under the
heads in subsections A1 through A3 of this section, as follows: (1986 Code §
19-27)
      1.   Class A: Class A shall include all ordinary clays, loams, sands,
loose gravel, and earthly materials, or earth containing loose stones or
boulders intermixed, which do not exceed three (3) cubic feet in size. (1986
Code § 19-28)
      2.   Class B: Class B shall include all stones, boulders and detached
pieces of rock lying in separate masses more than three (3) cubic feet and less
than one cubic yard; also slate, shale, soapstone, cemented gravel, coarse
boulders in gravel or hardpan. (1986 Code § 19-29)
      3.   Class C: Class C shall include all pieces of rock or boulders one
cubic yard or more in contents and all solid masses of solid, well defined
ledges of stone or masses of rock. (1986 Code § 19-30)
   B.   Surplus Materials: All excavating materials not used in the work shall
be deposited in such a place and spread in such a manner as the city engineer
may direct. The maximum length of free haul shall not exceed one thousand five
hundred feet (1,500'). Excavating material not wanted by the city or property
owner shall be disposed of by the contractor. Cuts shall have a width of seven
feet (7') at the bottom and have a slope of one foot (1') horizontal to one
foot (1') vertical. (1986 Code § 19-31)
7-3-7: EMBANKMENT:
Where a fill is necessary to bring the surface to subgrade, the same shall be
made of earth or other material to be furnished by the contractor, and the fill
shall be compact in six inch (6") layers flushing, if necessary, to secure a
solid foundation. The embankment shall have a width of seven feet (7') at the
top and a slope of one and one-half feet (11/2') horizontal to one foot (1')
vertical. (1986 Code § 19-32)
7-3-8: MATERIALS; MIXING:
The following rules shall govern the kinds of material to be used in sidewalks
and the mixing of the same:
   A.   Cement: Any brand of Portland cement fulfilling the requirements
suggested by the American Society for Testing Materials may be used.
   B.   Sand: The sand shall be clean and sharp.
   C.   Chat, Stone Or Gravel: The chat, broken stone or gravel shall be clean
and hard and of such dimensions that it will pass through a two inch (2") ring.
   D.   Mixing Material: Upon the properly prepared subgrade shall be placed a
concrete base three and one-half inches (31/2") thick, composed of one volume
of cement and five (5) volumes of aggregate, the aggregate being composed of
three (3) volumes of chat, broken stone or gravel; the sand shall be buried so
as to just fill the voids in the rock. The cement and aggregate shall be
thoroughly mixed dry by shoveling and turning over not less than twice; water
shall be added and the mixture again turned twice or more to secure a perfect
mass, or in lieu thereof same may be turned and mixed in any concrete mixing
machine. The mass shall be deposited in well constructed forms and thoroughly
packed until free mortar flushes over all parts of the surface and the surface
is exactly one-half inch (1/2") below the finished grade of the walk. No
concrete that has been mixed over forty (40) minutes shall be used. (1986 Code
§ 19-33)
7-3-9: FINISH:
Immediately after the base has been completed, there shall be placed thereon a
wearing surface consisting of one-half inch (1/2") of mortar composed of one
volume of portland cement and one and one-half (11/2) volumes of clean sand
with sufficient water to make mortar stiff. This shall be brought to grade with
a straight edge and then thoroughly compacted by troweling it three (3) times
or more. No patches will be allowed, and in finishing the walk it shall be cut
in five foot (5') or six foot (6') sections. The finished walk shall be
protected from the sun and wind by a moist cover for at least twenty four (24)
hours after its completion; the walk shall also be protected from freezing in
cold weather. The walk shall not be thrown open to travel for at least three
(3) days after its completion, and the contractor shall, at his own expense,
protect the walk from injury until it has been accepted by the city. (1986 Code
§ 19-34)
7-3-10: SIDEWALK AND CURBING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Walk Reinforced For Driveway: Walks across driveways shall be
reinforced, which shall consist of one inch (1") finished coat or wearing
surface, laid upon a seven inch (7") concrete base prepared as heretofore
specified. (1986 Code § 19-35)
   B.   Expansion Joints: All grooved joints shall be made not to exceed four
feet (4'), one 1-inch expansion joint shall be made every fifty feet (50') and
also where walks abut curb or old walk. (1986 Code § 19-38)
   C.   Grade: All sidewalks, curbing and guttering shall be constructed upon
grades to be furnished by the city engineer. (1986 Code § 19-39)
   D.   Business And Residential Streets:
      1.   Business: All sidewalks laid and constructed on any business street
shall be twelve feet (12') wide, including curbing, and shall adjoin the
abutting property line. (1986 Code § 19-40)
      2.   Residential: All sidewalks laid and constructed on any residential
street shall be four feet (4') wide, the inside of which shall be three feet
(3') from the line of the property abutting such sidewalk. (1986 Code § 19-41)
      3.   Incline: All sidewalks constructed on the business streets shall
have an incline from the abutting property line to the outside of curb of two
inches (2"), and all sidewalks on residential streets shall be one inch (1")
higher next to the property line. (1986 Code § 19-42)
   E.   Curbing:
      1.   All curbing shall be not less in size than five inches (5") on top
and leveled one inch (1") to the foot in height, and shall not be less than one
foot (1') in the ground from the bottom of the gutter, and in no case less than
one foot (1') in width, and the top of said curb shall be leveled at the outer
edge one-fourth inch (1/4"). (1986 Code § 19-43)
      2.   On all residential streets eighty feet (80') wide or more, the
curbing shall be placed so that the outer edge thereof will be twenty feet
(20') from the abutting property line, and on all residential streets less than
eighty feet (80') in width, the curbing shall adjoin the sidewalk on the
outside. (1986 Code § 19-44)
   F.   Gutters: All gutters shall be two and one-half feet (21/2') wide, and
united to the adjoining curbing and shall have an incline of six inches (6")
from the outside line to the curbing. (1986 Code § 19-45)
   G.   Corner Lots; Sidewalks Continue To Curb: All sidewalks on corner lots
shall continue to the curb line. (1986 Code § 19-46)
   H.   Railings: All railing around areas shall be of one and one-half inch
(11/2") gas pipe with posts not less than three feet (3') high and not more
than five feet (5') apart. (1986 Code § 19-48)
   I.   Sidewalks Over Areas: All sidewalks built over areas or open spaces
shall be constructed with suitable supports by walls, arches, or iron beams
according to specifications to be approved by city engineer. (1986 Code § 19-
49)
   J.   Manholes: All manholes through sidewalks shall be fitted with iron
covers. (1986 Code § 19-50)
   K.   Area Ways In Sidewalks: All area ways in sidewalks not otherwise
provided for herein shall be protected by iron railings securely fastened in a
workmanlike manner. (1986 Code § 19-51)
7-3-11: ASPHALTIC CONCRETE SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Roadbed:
      1.   The roadbed shall be shaped and crowned (the full width) with a
blade grader and shall have a crown of at least one-fourth inch (1/4") fall per
foot and a one inch (1") fall per twenty (20) lineal feet longitudinally.
      2.   All exposed rock larger than three inches (3") and any unstable soil
shall be removed and replaced with suitable material.
      3.   The roadbed shall be firmly compacted to conform to the typical
cross section as shown on the plans or the elevation established by the
engineer or inspector.
      4.   The finished road shall be twenty seven feet two inches (27'2") wide
including outside of curb to outside of curb.
   B.   Subbase:
      1.   The subbase material shall be a type A crushed limestone, passing a
one and one-half inch (11/2") sieve by weight, eighty percent (80%) to one
hundred percent (100%).
      2.   The subbase material shall be spread uniformly and in sufficient
quantities to conform to the required depth.
      3.   The subbase material shall be rolled and sprinkled to secure
thorough compaction. Rolling shall be done with a pneumatic type roller, a
three (3) wheeled roller, or a tandem roller.
      4.   Rolling shall continue until the subbase is compacted to not less
than ninety five percent (95%) of standard proctor density and shall be the
following thicknesses: four inches (4") for residential streets, six inches
(6") for collector streets and eight inches (8") for arterial streets.
   C.   Asphalt Cover Base:
      1.   Before applying asphalt cover base, the subbase shall be cleaned and
a tack coat of asphaltic cement cut back with thirty five percent (35%) to
sixty five percent (65%) naphtha or white gasoline and applied over the surface
with an approved sprayer at the rate of one-tenth (1/10) gallon per square yard
of surface.
      2.   Temperature in the shade at which asphaltic cement may be laid shall
be at no time when there is frost in the foundation course, thirty five degrees
Fahrenheit (35°F) if rising or forty degrees Fahrenheit (40°F) if falling.
      3.   The asphaltic cement shall be heated at the paving plant to a
temperature of two hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (250°F) to three hundred
degrees Fahrenheit (300°F) and shall be mixed with the aggregates at a rate of
five and one-half (0.055) to six and one-half (0.065) percent by weight of
total mix.
      4.   The mineral aggregates shall be a type A crushed limestone, passing
a one inch (1") sieve by weight one hundred percent (100%) and shall be heated
at the paving plant so that when delivered to the mixer they shall be at as low
a temperature as is consistent with proper mixing and laying and in no case to
exceed three hundred twenty five degrees Fahrenheit (325°F).
      5.   The mixture shall be delivered to the work in tight vehicles with
metal bottoms previously cleaned of all foreign materials.
      6.   The asphaltic mixture shall be spread by means of a mechanical self-
powered paver and all fat spots removed and replaced immediately after any
course is screeded and before any rolling is done.
      7.   Spreading shall be as continuous as possible and as soon as it will
bear the rollers without undue displacement, shall be uniformly compacted with
steel wheel and self-propelled pneumatic rollers to a thickness of two and one-
half inches (21/2"). This rolling shall continue in such a manner and
sufficient number of times as to eliminate all roller marks and until a
compacted density of not less than ninety five percent (95%) of the laboratory
test has been achieved.
      8.   No traffic shall be permitted on the asphaltic pavement until final
rolling has been made.
   D.   Joints: Longitudinal and transverse joints shall be well bonded and
sealed. For joints between old and new pavements or between successive days'
work (except when a canvas-rope joint is used for transverse joints), the edge
of the previously laid course shall be cut back to its full depth and given a
tack coat and emulsified asphalt before placing the mixture against them.
   E.   Integral Curb:
      1.   The curb shall be constructed on the outside edge of the pavement in
a monolithic manner with the gutter or pavement and in conformity with the
lines, grades and dimensions as shown on the plans or as directed by the
engineer or inspector.
      2.   If the curb is to be constructed of asphaltic cement, it shall be
laid with a mechanical machine designed and built for this type of curb.
      3.   If the curb is to be constructed of Portland cement concrete, it
shall be constructed in accordance with specifications as prescribed for
Portland cement streets, curbs and gutters. (See specifications on file in the
office of the city engineer and inspector.)
      4.   If the combined curb and gutter is a separate installation from the
street, the edge of the gutter shall be cleaned, given a tack coat and a
premoulded type of joint shall be bonded to the edge before laying the asphalt
mixture, against the concrete gutter.
      5.   If desired, the concrete gutter may be left two inches (2") lower
than the top of the finished asphalt pavement and when the asphaltic concrete
pavement is laid, the mixture can be permitted to extend across the top of the
gutter and bonded to the curb. Gutter shall have a slope toward the curb of at
least one-fourth inch (1/4") per foot.
   F.   Leveling Or Surfacing:
      1.   The mineral aggregates for this course shall be type C crushed
limestone, passing a three-eights inch (3/8") sieve by weight eighty percent
(80%) to one hundred percent (100%) and shall be heated at the paving plant so
that when delivered to the mixer they shall be at as low a temperature as is
consistent with proper mixing and laying and in no case to exceed three hundred
twenty five degrees Fahrenheit (325°F).
      2.   The asphaltic cement shall be heated at the paving plant to a
temperature of two hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (250°F) to three hundred
degrees Fahrenheit (300°F) and shall be mixed with the aggregates at a rate of
five and one-half (0.055) to six and one-half (0.065) percent by weight of the
total mix.
      3.   Temperature in the shade at which asphaltic cement may be laid shall
be thirty five degrees Fahrenheit (35°F) if rising or forty degrees Fahrenheit
(40°F) if falling and at no time when there is frost in the foundation course.
      4.   The mixture shall be delivered to the work in tight vehicles with
metal bottoms previously cleaned of all foreign materials and shall be spread
by means of a mechanical self-powered paver.
      5.   All fat spots shall be removed and replaced immediately after any
course is screeded and before any rolling is started.
      6.   Spreading shall be as continuous as possible and as soon as it will
bear the rollers without undue displacement, shall be uniformly compacted with
steel wheel and self-propelled pneumatic rollers to a thickness of one and one-
half inches (11/2").
      7.   Rolling shall continue in such a manner and sufficient number of
times as to eliminate all roller marks and until compacted to a density of not
less than ninety five percent (95%) of the laboratory test for this identical
mixture.
      8.   No traffic shall be permitted on the asphaltic pavement until final
rolling has been made.
   G.   Drawings: A cross section drawing shall be furnished the contractor
which will be in accordance with specifications. (1986 Code § 19-58)
7-3-12: PORTLAND CEMENT SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Subgrade:
      1.   Subgrade soils shall be of uniform materials and density to provide
satisfactory pavement performance. It shall be thoroughly compacted with
suitable equipment so as to have uniform density at moisture contents of not
less than standard optimum (AASHOT98).
 
Types of soil
 5p-A Parsons Silt loam 0-1% Slopes
 M5-A Taloka  Silt loam 0-1% Slopes
 6p-B Dennis  Silt loam 1-3% Slopes
 6p-C Dennis  Silt loam 3-5% Slopes
 7p-C Bates   Loam      3-5% Slopes
 
      2.   Topsoil and loose material shall be removed to a depth of at least
twelve inches (12").
      3.   Base shall be firm and free of mud and soft spots.
      4.   All soft spots shall be removed and compacted in six inch (6")
layers with like materials to a density of the adjacent base.
      5.   All rocks three inches (3") in diameter or larger shall be removed
from base to a depth of six inches (6") and the hold compacted as per
subsection A4 of this section.
      6.   Special care must be taken in backfilling water, gas, sewer and
other drainage facilities and other permanent structures in the paved area.
They must be backfilled in six inch (6") layers, with a like material and
compacted to a density comparable to the adjacent base.
      7.   Prepared subgrade or base will be restricted to all vehicle traffic.
   B.   Design:
      1.   Thickness: The thickness shall be determined by its use, i.e.: a)
local residential streets, six inches (6"); b) collector streets, seven inches
(7"); and c) major arterial system, eight inches (8").
      2.   Width: The minimum width in two (2) lane streets, except in unusual
cases, will be twenty seven feet two inches (27'2") including curb. It must
have a traverse slope of one-fourth inch (1/4") per foot of width and one inch
(1") fall per twenty feet (20') longitudinally. In four (4) lane streets, there
shall be allowed ten feet (10') to thirteen feet seven inches (13'7") for each
traffic lane. Lane widths in excess of thirteen feet seven inches (13'7") will
not be allowed.
      3.   Mix: Water cement ratio 5.5:6.0.
 
Water            45.8 or 33 gallons
Cement           564 pounds          Retained 3/4 inch, not to exceed 11/
Sand             1,200 pounds        2 inches
Gravel           2,000 pounds
Total dry weight 3,809.8 pounds
 
   C.   Concrete Quality:
      1.   Strength: The critical stresses in concrete pavement are flexural,
expressed in modulus of rupture; under average conditions the modulus of
rupture (3 point loading) will not be less than five hundred fifty (550) psi at
twenty eight (28) days. The cement factor will be not less than six (6) bags
per yard of concrete.
      2.   Entrained Air: In frost affected areas, concrete pavements are
subjected to many cycles of freezing and thawing and to the application of de-
icing agents, thus it is essential to have a mix with a low water-cement ratio,
an adequate cement factor and sufficient quantities of entrained air. The
amount of entrained air will vary with the maximum aggregate size, i.e.:
 
Maximum Size Aggregate Entrained Air
2 2/3, 2, 21/2         5 #1
3/4, 1                 6 #1
3/8, 1/2               7 #1
 
For the following reasons, entrained air should be incorporated into the mix
design for all concrete pavements:
         a.   Makes the hardened concrete more weather resistant.
         b.   Prevents segregation.
         c.   Increases workability.
         d.   Reduces bleeding.
         e.   Reduces the amount of water required for workability.
      3.   Water: The amount of mixing water also has a critical influence on
durability and weather resistance of hardened concrete. The least amount of
mixing water with a given cement content that will produce a plastic and
workable mix will result in the greatest durability of the hardened concrete.
The sump as measured in a standard slum core should never exceed three inches
(3") for hand finished concrete and two inches (2") to two and one-half inches
(21/2") for machine finished concrete. With air entrained concrete, the water-
cement ratio will not exceed five and one-half (51/2) gallons of water per
ninety four (94) pound bag of cement. The cement content will be not less than
six (6) bags per cubic yard.
      4.   Drying Agents: The use of drying agents (calcium chloride) will not
be permitted.
      5.   Temperatures:
         a.   The placement of concrete on frozen ground will not be permitted.
         b.   Air temperatures should be above freezing, thirty two degrees
(32°) and rising.
         c.   The concrete temperature should be at least forty degrees (40°)
or higher.
         d.   After placement, concrete will be protected against sudden drops
in temperature until it has obtained its initial set, four (4) days. In hot
summer time, especially when the ambient temperature exceeds one hundred
degrees (100°), it should be protected against excessive heat. (See "curing",
subsection C8 of this section.)
      6.   Placement: Concrete will not be placed until the following items
have been checked and approved by the inspector:
         a.   Base or subgrade.
         b.   Forms.
         c.   Grade and lines.
            (1)   One-fourth inch (1/4") to one foot (1') traversely.
            (2)   One inch (1") to twenty feet (20') longitudinally.
         d.   Temperatures.
         e.   Mix design (water-cement ratio and entrained air content).
      7.   Vibration: The concrete should be placed in an orderly and
progressive manner, using vibrations for compaction and distribution and screed
vibration for surface leveling and grading.
      8.   Curing: After finishing, the hardened concrete will be properly
cured by covering with impervious paper, burlap, cotton mats, sand canvas or
hay and kept continuously wet for at least seven (7) days. An approved curing
compound may be used and applied immediately after finishing. It should be used
in ample quantity to completely cover all exposed surfaces.
      9.   Travel And Use: Freshly poured concrete will be restricted to
traffic as follows:
         a.   Water cure - foot traffic, twenty four (24) hours.
         b.   Curing compounds - foot traffic, seven (7) days.
         c.   All concrete - vehicle traffic, twenty one (21) days.
   D.   Joints:
      1.   Longitudinal Joints: These joints shall be spaced to coincide with
lane markings from ten foot (10') to thirteen foot seven inch (13'7")
intervals. Longitudinal joints will be keyed and the top one-fourth inch (1/4")
by one inch (1") recessed and filled with hot mix joint sealer (type E joint).
      2.   Expansion Joints: Expansion joints will be placed at distances no
greater than six hundred feet (600') and at all street intersections. One inch
(1") premold may be used with a two inch (2") by five foot (5') thickened base
(type A joint) , or with normal base one inch (1") premold expansion joint
filler and three-fourths inch (3/4") by fifteen inch (15") dowel bars at twelve
inch (12") center (type A alternate joint). Type A expansion joint will be used
around all manholes and catch basins. The top one-fourth inch (1/4") by one
inch (1") will be filled with hot mix joint sealer.
      3.   Traverse Contraction Joints: Traverse contraction joints may be
sawed one-fourth (1/4) of pavement thickness or they may be formed during
construction by insertion of preformed material one-eighth inch (1/8") to one-
fourth inch (1/4") to a depth of one-fourth (1/4) of the thickness of the slab
(type C joint). After sawing, they shall be filled with hot mix joint sealer.
Spacing of the traverse joints will depend on the type aggregate used and
subgrade conditions.
         a.   Crushed granite or limestone - twenty foot (20') intervals.
         b.   Siliceous gravel - sixteen foot (16') intervals.
         c.   Gravel smaller than three-fourths inch (3/4") - sixteen foot
(16') intervals.
         d.   A traverse construction joint made by the ending of a day's pour
will be similar to the type D joint and/or type E joint. It should be
bulkheaded, recessed one-fourth inch (1/4") by one inch (1") for hot mix joint
sealer and contain five-eighths inch (5/8") round, smooth dowel bars fifteen
inches (15") long at twelve inch (12") centers.
(Type D traverse construction joints)
(Type E tied traverse construction joints)
      4.   Curbs And Gutters: An integral curb will be poured monolithically
with the pavement in a one step operation in which all concrete work is done
simultaneously. The gutter flow line should be pretested before the final set
of the concrete. This will permit correction of high spots or pockets where
surface water may collect.
      5.   Utilities: Water, gas, electric lines and storm sewers will be laid
outside the proposed curb line. When any of the above items cross the base or
subgrade under the slab, they will be backfilled and compacted with a like
material in six inch (6") layers to a density equal to the adjacent subgrade.
   E.   Specifications Adopted By Reference: The specifications in section
7-3-2 of this chapter are adopted from the Portland Cement Association's
"Design For Concrete Pavements For City Streets" and "Oklahoma Highway
Specifications". All reference to types of joint construction may be found in
the Portland cement manual. (1986 Code § 19-59)
7-3-13: SIDEWALKS LAID IN VIOLATION OF CHAPTER:
   A.   Removal Of Sidewalk; Laying By City; Costs: Any sidewalk heretofore
constructed, or which may hereafter be constructed contrary to the provisions
of this chapter may be required by the mayor and city council to be taken up by
the city engineer and a proper sidewalk constructed to conform to the
requirements of this chapter, under the supervision and direction of the city
engineer, and the cost thereof shall be taxed against the abutting lot or lots
as provided by the laws of this state. (1986 Code § 19-52)
   B.   Separate Offense: Every day the owner, contractor or builder shall lay
or construct, or attempt to lay or construct, any sidewalk, curb or gutter in
violation of the provisions of this chapter shall constitute a separate
offense. (1986 Code § 19-55)
7-3-14: CONDEMNATION BY COUNCIL:
The city council may, at any time by resolution, condemn any portion of any
defective sidewalk when, in its judgment, it shall be deemed necessary, and
provide for the construction of a new sidewalk in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter. (1986 Code § 19-54)
7-3-15: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
7-1-10 of this title. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 4
CEMETERIES
SECTION:
7-4-1: Operation By City
7-4-2: Cemetery Superintendent
7-4-3: Cemetery Care Fund
7-4-4: Payment Of Fees
7-4-5: Issuance Of Burial Permits
7-4-6: Record Of Lot Sales
7-4-7: Vaults
7-4-8: Monuments, Improvements And Embellishments
7-4-9: Coping, Walk Or Wall Prohibited
7-4-10: Removal Of Wreaths, Decorations
7-4-11: Driving Vehicles In Cemetery
7-4-12: Penalty
7-4-1: OPERATION BY CITY:
The city shall operate and maintain the Fairview Cemetery and shall fix the
rules and regulations for the management and operating of same. (1986 Code § 6-
1)
7-4-2: CEMETERY SUPERINTENDENT:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor shall appoint some qualified person to the
office of cemetery superintendent with the consent of the city council, who
shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor and city council. (1986 Code § 6-2)
   B.   Duties: The cemetery superintendent shall perform the following duties:
      1.   To care for and protect the cemetery grounds and their
appurtenances.
      2.   To enforce the rules and regulations of the city pertaining to the
cemetery.
      3.   To superintend the repairs and construction of improvements and the
maintenance of all permanent improvements and embellishments of any kind which
tend to beautify such cemetery or preserve it permanently as a place of burial
for the human dead. (1986 Code § 6-3)
7-4-3: CEMETERY CARE FUND:
   A.   Fund Established: There shall be a cemetery care fund for the
maintenance and improvement of the cemetery owned and operated by the city in
accordance with 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 26-109, including any current
supplement. Twelve and one-half percent (12.5%) of all monies received from the
sale of lots and interments shall be segregated and set aside in this permanent
fund. The cemetery care fund shall be expended for purchasing lands for
cemeteries and for making capital improvements, if necessary. The balance of
the fund shall be invested in the manner provided by law for the investment of
municipal funds. The interest from the investments shall be used for the same
purposes as the principal or in improving, caring for, and embellishing the
lots, walks, drives, parks, and other necessary improvements on such
cemeteries. (Ord. 3506, 9-6-2011)
7-4-4: PAYMENT OF FEES:
   A.   Price Of Lots: The price of lots in the city cemetery shall be
established by motion or resolution of the city council. (1986 Code § 6-6)
   B.   Interment Fee: The interment fee for opening and closing graves in the
city cemetery shall be established by motion or resolution of the city council.
(1986 Code § 6-7)
   C.   Payment Of Fee Required:
      1.   No deed for any cemetery lot shall be issued, no grave opened nor
shall any monument be set, located or placed until and unless the requisite
price, fee, or charge therefor has been paid in full and in cash to the
appropriate city officer, and the proper permit issued. (1986 Code § 6-8)
      2.   In no case shall any person dig any grave, or inter any human body
in or upon any lot owned by the city in the cemetery until the city shall have
received the full price to be paid for the lot or lots in or upon which said
grave or interment is to be made, and until a permit is issued by the city
clerk, as provided for in section
7-4-5 of this chapter. (1986 Code § 6-11)
   D.   Sale And Conveyance Of Lots: All lots in the city cemetery shall be
sold at such prices as the mayor and city council may from time to time adopt
and establish. All lots sold therein shall be conveyed by certificate to be
issued by the city clerk and signed by the mayor and countersigned by said
clerk, under the seal of the city, which certificate shall show the lot or lots
described by numbers as shown upon the plat of the cemetery, the price paid, to
whom issued who shall be the owner, and date of issuance. (1986 Code § 6-10)
7-4-5: ISSUANCE OF BURIAL PERMITS:
The city clerk shall have the power and authority to contract and sell any lot
or lots in the cemetery, at the price or prices fixed and established by the
mayor and city council, and to issue permits for the burial of the human dead
in the cemetery, provided such permits shall not be issued until all monies and
charges due the city shall have been paid. (1986 Code § 6-12)
7-4-6: RECORD OF LOT SALES:
It shall be the duty of the city clerk to keep a record, in a well bound book
to be kept for that purpose, of all sales of lots in the cemetery, which record
shall show the number and location of the lot or lots sold, the date of sale,
to whom sold, and the amount paid for each lot or lots, and the name of the
person whose body is interred in the cemetery. (1986 Code § 6-13)
7-4-7: VAULTS:
All burials at Fairview Cemetery shall be made in outside containers which are
made of natural stone, or of metal, or of reinforced concrete, or of an equal
strength synthetic product. All such containers must be made and installed as
to prevent their collapse while in use, therefore eliminating sunken graves.
(1986 Code § 6-17)
7-4-8: MONUMENTS, IMPROVEMENTS AND EMBELLISHMENTS:
The erection of monuments, tombstones, filling of graves, improving, adorning
and embellishing graves, or the marking thereof by private parties in the
cemetery shall be done under the supervision of the superintendent and not
otherwise, and no improvement shall be made and no erection of monuments or
marking of graves be had until all charges owing to the city on said lot or
lots to be improved shall have been fully paid. (1986 Code § 6-14)
7-4-9: COPING, WALK OR WALL PROHIBITED:
It is hereby declared unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to install
any coping, walk or wall in the city cemetery; however, this prohibition shall
not apply to the city where such improvements are necessary for the public good
in maintaining the cemetery. (1986 Code § 6-9)
7-4-10: REMOVAL OF WREATHS, DECORATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to remove wreaths, flowers, potted plants
or other decorations, whether the same be live or artificial, placed on or near
graves in any cemetery owned, operated or maintained by the city other than the
persons placing such wreaths, flowers, potted plants or other decorations on or
near such graves or their agents or authorized representatives; provided
however, that the city, its agents, representatives or employees may, one week
following Memorial Day or other occasion when graves in the cemetery may be
decorated, remove and dispose of such decorations other than permanent
plantings and potted flowers or plants placed upon grave markers in a position
where they do not interfere with the mowing of the cemetery. (1986 Code § 6-16)
7-4-11: DRIVING VEHICLES IN CEMETERY:
All vehicles driven into the cemetery shall be subject to the orders and
directions of the superintendent or other authorized officer in charge of the
cemetery. (1986 Code § 6-15)
7-4-12: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any provision of this chapter
by doing any act prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby, or declared to
be an offense or misdemeanor thereby, or who shall fail to do any act required
by any such provision, or who shall fail to do any act when such provision
declares such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day upon which any such violation continues shall
constitute a separate misdemeanor. (1986 Code § 6-18; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 5
PARKS AND RECREATION
SECTION:
7-5-1: Rules And Regulations
7-5-2: Determination Of Fees
7-5-3: Park Curfew; Overnight Camping
7-5-4: Unlawful Use Of Vehicles In Park
7-5-5: Penalty
7-5-1: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The city council shall promulgate, invoke, create, amend and enforce such
rules, regulations, and other requirements as it deems necessary or expedient
in connection with fishing and fishing privileges, hunting and hunting
privileges, boating and boating privileges, and swimming, and the use of all
other recreational facilities owned or operated by the city. (1986 Code § 15-1)
7-5-2: DETERMINATION OF FEES:
The city shall provide by rules, from time to time, the fees charged for any
such recreational privileges on any property or facility for recreational
purpose owned or operated by the city. (1986 Code § 15-2)
7-5-3: PARK CURFEW; OVERNIGHT CAMPING:
   A.   Closing Hours For Public Parks:
      1.   All public parks within the city limits of Vinita, Oklahoma, shall
be closed to the public from ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. until six o'clock (6:00)
A.M. each day; provided that the parks department may post more restrictive
hours or extend the hours at any or all parks until twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight.
      2.   No person shall go upon or remain upon any public park at any time
the park is closed, whether such closing occurs as the result of the time set
forth in this section or as a result of the posting performed by the parks
department. It shall not be a violation of this section for a person to go upon
or remain upon any public park at any time the park is closed when they have
permission from the city council or when they are participating in an event or
function which has previously been approved by the city council.
   B.   Consent Required; Waiver:
      1.   The use of the parks and public areas within the corporate limits of
the city for overnight camping is prohibited without the consent of the mayor
and city council.
      2.   The foregoing prohibition and any applicable penalty may be waived
by the mayor and council at any regular or special meeting in favor of any
organized group or association, for such time as specified, not to exceed five
(5) days and nights, consecutively.
   C.   Presumptive Evidence: The installation or stopping of any trailer or
the erection of any tent or shelter after one hour before sundown in the area
described in subsection B1 of this section shall constitute presumptive
evidence of the breach of this chapter. (Ord. 3471, 6-1-2010)
7-5-4: UNLAWFUL USE OF VEHICLES IN PARK:
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any truck, automobile, motorcycle,
motor scooter, or other motor vehicle or to ride any horse, pony or other
animal in or upon the public parks within the limits of the city, except upon
clearly defined public roadways or public parking areas in such parks or except
in cases of public necessity when authorized and directed to do so by public
officials of the city. (1986 Code § 15-6)
7-5-5: PENALTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to use any of such recreational facilities
or to hunt, fish, swim or use any boat in connection with any of said
recreational facilities owned or operated by the city without having complied
with the rules and regulations promulgated by the city council in connection
therewith. Anyone violating any of the rules and regulations, or failing to
comply with such, or anyone who does any act forbidden by this chapter, or
fails to do any act required by this chapter, shall be guilty of an offense
and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-9-13 of this code. Each day the violation continues shall constitute a new
and different offense. (1986 Code § 15-7; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 6
RAILROADS
SECTION:
7-6-1: Street And Alley Improvements
7-6-2: Sidewalk Construction By Railroads
7-6-3: Climbing On Trains
7-6-4: Speed Of Trains
7-6-5: Obstructing Streets
7-6-6: Railroad Negligence
7-6-7: Penalty
7-6-1: STREET AND ALLEY IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Parallel With Street: When a railway occupies any portion of a street
with its tracks running in a general direction of such street, either on or
adjacent thereto, the railway company shall improve the space between its
tracks and two feet (2') on either side thereof in the same manner that the
remainder of the street is to be, or has been, improved, or with such other
satisfactory material as the city council by motion or resolution may approve.
   B.   Within Alley: In case any railway company shall occupy an alley with
its tracks, such company shall improve, gutter, drain, and grade such alley,
and shall surface or pave it with the same material which is to be, or has
been, used on the alley, or with such other satisfactory material as the
council by motion or resolution may approve.
   C.   Crossing Street:
      1.   When the tracks of any railroad company cross any street that is
being or has been paved, the company shall pave as much of the street as is
occupied by its tracks and two feet (2') on each side, using the same material
as is to be, or has been, used on the street, or such other satisfactory
material as the council by motion or resolution may approve.
      2.   When more than one track crosses a street within a distance of one
hundred feet (100'), measuring from inside rail to inside rail, the railroad
company shall grade, gutter, drain, and curb the street area between its
tracks, and surface or pave it with the same material which the city is to use
or has used, on the street.
   D.   Keeping In Good Repair: Railroad companies shall keep all such
improvements made by them in a good state of repair at all times. (1986 Code §
21-1)
7-6-2: SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION BY RAILROADS:
   A.   Railroad Responsibility: Railway companies shall construct sidewalks
crossing their rights of way, using the same material as is used in adjacent
sidewalks insofar as this is practicable under the circumstances. They shall
construct sidewalks on both sides of the streets when both sides are used by
pedestrians. The company shall keep such sidewalks in a good state of repair at
all times.
   B.   Statutory Note: Section A of this section follows generally 11 Oklahoma
Statutes section 36-117. 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 36-118(A) provides that,
if the railroad company refuses to improve streets and build sidewalks as
provided by the above section, the city may do so at the railroad company's
expense, and sue in the district court to collect from the company. 11 Oklahoma
Statutes sections 36-118(B) provides also that the city shall have a lien on
the property of the company for the amount of such expense. (1986 Code § 21-2)
7-6-3: CLIMBING ON TRAINS:
It is unlawful for any person to climb upon, hold onto, or in any manner attach
himself to, any railway train, locomotive, or railway car, while such is in
motion within the city, unless such person is acting in line of duty; or to
board any train or railroad car (passenger, freight, or other) except with a
